Wiping over Thick Socks: The Hanafi Extension of the Khuff Ruling
Ruling on wiping over thick socks and prohibition on headgear/gloves

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for valid wiping over non-leather footwear and explain why the Hanafi school permits it based on Imam Abu Hanifa's retraction and the principle of qiyās.

Core Idea
Wiping over thick socks is allowed when they enable walking a farsakh; the ruling is based on hardship and the Prophet's practice.

The Hanafi school uniquely extends the concession of wiping over leather khuffs to thick socks that serve the same function. This lesson examines the classification of socks, the intra-madhhab disagreement that was resolved by the Imam's retraction, and the prohibition on wiping headwear or gloves. Understanding this case illustrates how Hanafi scholars use qiyās khafī (hidden analogy) and the principle of rafʿ al-ḥaraj (removing hardship) to expand concessions beyond the literal text.

Guided Path
1
Classify the types of socks
Identify the three categories: mujallad (leather-lined top and bottom), munʿal (leather-soled), and thakhīn (thick). Note that the first two are unanimously allowed; the third is the subject of dispute.
Thin socks (raqīq) are unanimously disallowed.
2
Understand the condition for allowance
The key condition is that the sock enables continuous walking for a farsakh (approx. 3 miles) or more. This is the 'illah (effective cause) for the concession.
This condition mirrors the function of a khuff.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Imam Abu Hanifa originally disallowed wiping over thick socks. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad allowed it. The Imam retracted 3-7 days before his death, adopting the Sahibayn's view. The fatwa is on permissibility.
This shows the dynamic nature of ijtihad within the madhhab.
4
Apply the ruling to other materials
Felt (libad) socks are not mentioned in Zahir al-Riwayah, but if they enable travel, wiping is allowed. This extends the principle beyond strict categories.
The correct view is that anything that can be walked in for a distance qualifies.
5
Distinguish prohibited items
Turban, cap, face-veil, and gloves cannot be wiped over because the concession is based on text (khuffs) and there is no hardship in removing them. Qiyās is not permissible against clear text.
The prohibition is unanimous.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
حكم الجرموق وغيره والجورب المجلّد والمنعّل والثخين، لا على عمامة وقلنسوة وبُرقع وقفازين. والمسح على الجورب المجلد : [ أي الذي وضع الجلد على أعلاه وأسفله. (ط)] هو خف من كتان أو قطن أو نحو ذلك، والمسح عليه إذا كان مجلداً أو منعلاً أو ثخيناً لإمكان متابعة المشي فيه فرسخاً أو أكثر، ثم المسح على الجورب المنعل جاز اتفاقاً، وعلى الرقيق لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وعلى الثخين غير جائز عند الإمام، وقالا: يجوز، وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بثلاثة أيام أو بسبعة، وعليه الفتوى؛ لما روي أنه عليها توضأ و مسح على الجوربين والنعلين رواه أبو داود والترمذي. والمنعّل [ أي الذي وضع الجلد على أسفله. (ط)] والثخين [ أي الذي يقوم على الساق من غير شد اعلم أن المسح غير قاصر على ما ذكر، بل كل ما كان في معنى الخف في إمكان المشي عليه وإمكان قطع السفر به ملحق به ومالا ،فلا وأما المتخذ من اللبد فلم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية، قيل: إن كان يطيق السفر به جاز المسح عليه وإلا فلا، وهو الصحيح، وفي "الخانية": أنه يجوز المسح على الخف الذي يكون من اللبد ، وإن لم يكن منعلاً؛ لأنه يمكن قطع المسافة به. (فتح المعين) لا على عمامة إلخ وهذا مما لا خلاف في عدم جواز مسح هذه الأشياء؛ لأن المسح على الخف ثبت بالنص على خلاف القياس فلا يلحق به غيره، وأيضاً لا مشقة في نزع هذه الأشياء بخلاف الخف، فامتنع الإلحاق، و"القلنسوة" بفتحتين وضم المهملة، يلف عليه العمامة. (فتح) كرس دستانه. (ع) وبرقع بضم الباء ،والقاف الذي تغطي به النساء وجوهها. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٠/١] وقفازين بضم القاف وتشديد الفاء، تثنية قفاز، وهو شيء يلبسه النساء والصيادون في أيديهم
Ruling of the boot (jurmūq) and other things, and the sock that is leather-lined (mujallad), soled (munʿal), and thick (thakhīn). Not on a turban, cap, face-veil, or gloves. And wiping over the leather-lined sock: it is a khuff made of linen or cotton, etc. Wiping over it is allowed if it is leather-lined, soled, or thick, because it enables continuous walking for a farsakh or more. Then wiping over a soled sock is unanimously allowed. Over a thin sock, it is unanimously not allowed. Over a thick sock, it is not allowed according to Imam Abu Hanifa, but Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say it is allowed. And Imam Abu Hanifa retracted (his view) three or seven days before his death, and the fatwa is on this (permissibility). Because it is narrated that he (the Prophet) performed wudu and wiped over his socks and sandals, reported by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. The soled: one on which leather is placed on the bottom. The thick: one that stands on the leg without tying. Know that wiping is not limited to what has been mentioned; rather, everything that is in the meaning of a khuff in terms of possibility of walking on it and possibility of covering travel is annexed to it; what is not is not. As for (socks) made of felt, it is not mentioned in the zahir al-riwayah. It is said: if it is capable of being used for travel, wiping over it is allowed; otherwise no. This is the correct view. In al-Khaniyya: it is permissible to wipe over the khuff made of felt, even if not soled, because it is possible to cover the distance with it. Not on a turban etc. This is what there is no disagreement about the impermissibility of wiping on these items, because wiping over the khuff is established by the text contrary to analogy, so nothing else is annexed to it. Also, there is no hardship in removing these items, unlike the khuff, so annexation is prevented. Al-Qalansuwa: with two fathas and a damm on the important letter, it is a thing on which the turban is wound. Gloves: with a damm on the qaf and tashdid on the fa', dual of quffaz, something worn by women and hunters on their hands.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage discusses the extension of the ruling of wiping to items that resemble khuffs. The matn mentions 'al-jurmūq wa ghayrihi' (the boot and other things), referring to thick socks (jawārib). The commentary distinguishes three types: leather-lined (mujallad), soled (munʿal), and thick (thakhīn). Wiping is valid on the first two unanimously, but on thick socks there is an intra-Hanafi dispute. Imam Abu Hanifa initially disallowed it, but the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed it, and the Imam retracted shortly before his death. The fatwa is on permissibility, supported by a hadith where the Prophet wiped over his socks and sandals. The condition for any substitute is that it enables walking a farsakh or covering a travel distance. Items not in the meaning of a khuff, such as a turban, cap, face-veil, or gloves, cannot be wiped over because the ruling is established by text against analogy, so only the specified items are included. There is no hardship in removing these items, so the concession is not extended. The text also mentions felt (libad) socks: though not in the Zahir al-Riwayah, the correct ruling is that if they can be used for travel, wiping is allowed.

Key Terms
جورب (jūrb (plural: jawārib)): A sock, usually made of cotton or linen, sometimes with leather lining or sole.
مجلّد (mujallad): A sock with leather on both its top and bottom.
منعّل (munʿal): A sock with leather only on the bottom (soles).
ثخين (thakhīn): A thick sock that stands on the leg without tying, enabling walking.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the operative fatwa (mufta bihi) for wiping over thick socks in the Hanafi school according to the passage?
A) It is not allowed.
B) It is allowed.
C) It is allowed only for the sick.
D) It is makruh.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over thick socks is permitted in the Hanafi school because they share the same ‘illah as khuffs – hardship in removal – and because Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his original view before his death.

The Ruling on Wiping over Splints and Bandages
Ruling on wiping over splints, wound bandages, and dispute on head wounds.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over splints and bandages, cite the hadith evidence, and evaluate the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding a completely wounded head.

Core Idea
Wiping over splints has no time limit; a fully wounded head still requires wiping because it is an original act, not a substitute.

When an injury prevents washing a limb during wuḍūʾ or ghusl, the Hanafi school permits wiping over the covering. This lesson examines the primary evidence—the hadith of Ali—and the extension of the ruling to other wounds. It also explores an internal debate: is wiping required when the entire head is wounded? The answer hinges on whether head wiping is an original or substitute act.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is wiping over the splint (jabīrah) and similar items like wound bandages. The ruling is that wiping substitutes for washing, so it has no time limit and is combined with ghusl if needed.
Unlike the khuff, there is no fixed duration.
2
Locate the dalil
The evidence is the hadith of Ali ibn Abi Talib: when his forearm was fractured, the Prophet ordered him to wipe over the splint.
The hadith is ahad but accepted in practice.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The explicit command to wipe indicates that such wiping is sufficient and permissible as a substitute for washing the injured area.
It establishes the permissibility and obligation when needed.
4
Note the extension to other wounds
The ruling for splints is extended to wound bandages, venesection bandages, and similar items via dalālah al-naṣṣ (implication of the text), based on the shared illah of necessity.
This expansion is a feature of Hanafi istinbāṭ.
5
Identify the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
For a completely wounded head, some Hanafis (e.g., al-Mubtagha) argued that wiping is not obligatory because wiping on the head is a substitute for washing, and a substitute cannot have a substitute. The correct view (supported by al-Baḥr al-Rāʾiq) is that it is obligatory because head wiping is an original act, not a substitute.
The dispute centers on the nature of head wiping in wuḍūʾ.
6
Evaluate the tarjih
The relied-upon position (muftā bihī) is the obligation of wiping over the head bandage, as affirmed by later Hanafi authorities like Ibn ʿĀbidīn.
This is due to the principle that wiping on the head is an independent obligation from the Quran.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمسح على الجبيرة وخرقة القرحة ونحو ذلك كالغسل، فلا يتوقت ويُجمع مع الغسل، ويجوز وإن شدّها بلا وضوء، ويمسح أي الجبيرة كعصابة الفصد وعصابة الجراحة الأصل في جواز المسح على هذه الأشياء حديث علي أنه قال: "كسرت إحدى زندي، فأمرني رسول الله الله أن أمسح عليها"، ثم هذا، وإن كان في الجبيرة خاصة، لكن عرف الحكم في القروح بدلالة النص. (مستخلص) كالغسل هذا لا يشمل ما إذا كان بالرأس ،جراحة فإن وظيفتها المسح، ويمكن الجواب بأنه من باب التغليب، وفي "المبتغى" : ومن كان جميع رأسه مجروحا لا يجب المسح عليه؛ لأن المسح بدل عن الغسل ولا بدل للمسح، وقيل: يجب، والصواب هو الوجوب، وقوله: "المسح بدل عن الغسل غير صحيح؛ لأن المسح على الرأس أصل بنفسه لا بدل عنه كما لا يخفى البحر الرائق بلا وضوء لأن في اعتباره حرجاً بخلاف الخف.
And wiping over the splint (jabīrah) and the cloth of a sore (qarḥah) and similar things is like washing, so it is not time-limited and it is combined with a bath, and it is permissible even if he tightened it without wuḍūʾ. And he wipes, i.e., the splint, like the bandage of venesection and the bandage of a wound. The basis for the permissibility of wiping over these things is the hadith of Ali where he said: 'One of my forearms was fractured, and the Messenger of Allah ordered me to wipe over it.' Then this, although it is specifically about the splint, the ruling of sores is known by implication of the text. (Mustakhlas) 'Like washing' does not include if the injury is on the head, because its function is wiping, and it can be answered that it is from the category of dominant application. In al-Mubtagha: Whoever has his entire head wounded, wiping is not obligatory on him, because wiping is a substitute for washing, and there is no substitute for wiping. And it is said: it is obligatory, and the correct is the obligation. And his statement: 'wiping is a substitute for washing' is not correct, because wiping on the head is an original act itself, not a substitute for anything, as is not hidden in al-Bahr al-Ra'iq. Without wuḍūʾ because requiring it would cause hardship, unlike the khuff.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage gives the ruling on wiping over medical necessities: a splint (jabīrah), a cloth covering a wound, etc. The author states that the ruling for these items is the same as for washing (ghusl), meaning there is no specific time limit (unlike the khuff's fixed duration), and one can combine it with the bath (i.e., if one needs ghusl, he wipes over the splint with wet hands instead of washing underneath). The condition of prior wuḍūʾ is not required for applying the splint; this is to remove hardship, contrary to the khuff. The evidence is the hadith of Ali: when his forearm was broken, the Prophet ordered him to wipe over the splint. This proof is extended to other wounds via implication. The text also discusses a subtle point: what if the injury is on the head? Since the head's original function for someone in a state of wuḍūʾ is wiping (not washing), the rule here is that he does not need to wipe over the bandage; rather, he wipes the healthy part. But if the entire head is wounded, there is a dispute: some say wiping is not required because it would be a substitute for a substitute, but the correct view is that wiping is obligatory because wiping on the head is an original act, not a substitute for washing. The commentary from al-Bahr al-Raʾiq clarifies that this is because wiping is not a replacement for washing; it is a primary duty.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabīrah): Sticks or supports used to set broken bones, covered with bandages.
الغسل (ghusl): Full body wash; here used as a comparison meaning the ruling is like washing (i.e., covers the same area, no time limit).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What evidence is cited for the permissibility of wiping over a splint?
A) The practice of the caliphs
B) The hadith of Ali
C) Analogy to wiping over khuffs
D) Ijma'

Key Takeaway
Wiping over medical bandages is a necessary concession in wuḍūʾ and ghusl, with no time limit, and for the head, wiping remains obligatory even if fully wounded.

Wiping Over Thick Socks: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute and Its Resolution
Explains the ruling on wiping over thick socks with ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute on wiping over thick socks and state the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his prohibition of wiping over thick socks; the fatwa now is permissibility based on the Prophet's action.

This lesson examines the ruling on wiping over thick socks during wudu. While all Hanafi authorities agree on wiping over leather-covered or soled socks, they initially differed on thick socks without leather. The source passage explains that Imam Abu Hanifa later retracted his view, adopting the position of his two disciples, and the fatwa now follows this permissibility. Understanding this dispute illustrates how ikhtilaf within a madhhab is resolved through evidence and scholarly consensus.

Guided Path
1
Identify the sock types and their definitions
The passage defines three types: mujallad (leather-covered on top and bottom), mun'al (soled with leather), and thakhīn (thick, standing without tying). Note the shared condition: each must allow walking a farsakh or more.
This condition aligns them with the function of a khuff.
2
Separate agreed and disputed cases
All agree that wiping over a soled sock (mun'al) is valid (jā'iz), and over a thin sock (raqīq) is invalid. The dispute is over the thick sock (thakhīn).
The disagreement is limited to one sub-case.
3
State the positions of the three Imams
Imam Abu Hanifa initially held that wiping over a thick sock is not permissible (lā yajūz). The two Ṣāḥibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) held it is permissible (yajūz).
The text says 'Qālā: yajūz' (the two said permissible).
4
Analyze the Imam's retraction and its impact
Imam Abu Hanifa retracted his view three or seven days before his death. Consequently, the fatwa (mufta bihi) now is permissibility, making it the operative ruling of the school.
This shows that the Imam's final position aligns with the Ṣāḥibayn.
5
Examine the evidence and its scope
The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi: the Prophet wiped over socks and sandals during wudu. This establishes permissibility. The passage then extends the ruling: any covering that enables walking a travel distance (like felt khuffs) is included.
The hadith is aḥad (zanni al-thubut) but accepted as evidence for this ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والجورب المجلّد والمنعّل والثخين. والجورب المجلّد : [ أي الذي وضع الجلد على أعلاه وأسفله. (ط)] هو خف من كتان أو قطن أو نحو ذلك، والمسح عليه إذا كان مجلداً أو منعلاً أو ثخيناً لإمكان متابعة المشي فيه فرسخاً أو أكثر، ثم المسح على الجورب المنعل جاز اتفاقاً، وعلى الرقيق لا يجوز اتفاقاً، وعلى الثخين غير جائز عند الإمام، وقالا: يجوز، وإليه رجع الإمام قبل موته بثلاثة أيام أو بسبعة، وعليه الفتوى؛ لما روي أنه عليه السلام توضأ و مسح على الجوربين والنعلين رواه أبو داود والترمذي. والمنعّل [ أي الذي وضع الجلد على أسفله. (ط)] والثخين [ أي الذي يقوم على الساق من غير شد اعلم أن المسح غير قاصر على ما ذكر، بل كل ما كان في معنى الخف في إمكان المشي عليه وإمكان قطع السفر ملحق به ومالا، فلا وأما المتخذ من اللبد فلم يذكر في ظاهر الرواية، قيل: إن كان يطيق السفر به جاز المسح عليه وإلا فلا، وهو الصحيح، وفي "الخانية": أنه يجوز المسح على الخف الذي يكون من اللبد ، وإن لم يكن منعلاً؛ لأنه يمكن قطع المسافة به. (فتح المعين)
The sock covered with leather, soled, and thick. The sock covered with leather: [i.e., that which has leather placed on its top and bottom. (T)] It is a khuff made of linen or cotton or the like, and wiping over it is valid if it is covered with leather, soled, or thick, because it is possible to continue walking in it for a farsakh or more. Then, wiping over a soled sock is valid by agreement, over a thin sock is not valid by agreement, and over a thick sock is not valid according to Imam (Abu Hanifa), but the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) said it is valid. The Imam retracted before his death by three or seven days, and the fatwa is upon that (permissibility) due to what is related that he (the Prophet) performed wudu and wiped over the two socks and two sandals, narrated by Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi. The soled: [i.e., that which has leather placed on its bottom. (T)] And the thick: [i.e., that which stands on the leg without tying. Know that wiping is not restricted to what was mentioned, but rather everything that is analogous to the khuff in the possibility of walking in it and the possibility of covering travel distance is included, and what is not is not. As for what is made of felt, it is not mentioned in the Zahir al-Riwayah. It is said: if one can travel with it, wiping over it is valid, otherwise not, and this is the correct view. In al-Khaniyya: It is valid to wipe over a khuff made of felt even if it is not soled, because it is possible to cover the distance with it. (Fath al-Mu'in)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is an expansion on the ruling of wiping over socks (jawrabs). It begins by defining the types of socks: those covered with leather (mujallad), those soled (mun'al), and those thick (thakhin). The author states that wiping over such socks is permissible if they allow one to walk a farsakh (approx. 5-6 km) or more, meaning they must be durable like khuffs. There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf: all agree wiping over a soled sock is valid, and wiping over a thin sock is not. But for a thick sock (without leather sole), Imam Abu Hanifa initially forbade it, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) allowed it. Imam later retracted his position before his death, and the fatwa now is on permissibility. The proof is a hadith from Abu Dawud and al-Tirmidhi showing the Prophet (peace be upon him) wiped over socks and sandals during wudu. The passage then extends the ruling: any covering that functions like a khuff (allowing travel) is included, such as felt khuffs, even if not soled, as per al-Khaniyya. The main point is that the permissibility of wiping is based on necessity and ease of walking, not on material alone.

Key Terms
الجورب (al-jawrab): A sock or stocking, often made of cloth or wool.
المجلد (al-mujallad): Covered with leather, either on top and bottom or just the sole.
المنعل (al-mun'al): Having a sole made of leather or other solid material.
الثخين (al-thakhīn): Thick, standing on the leg without tying; capable of walking a distance.
الخف (al-khuff): A leather sock or boot typically made of leather.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the status of the hadith that the Prophet wiped over socks and sandals in the Hanafi school?
A) It is mutawatir and thus conclusive.
B) It is ahad but accepted as evidence, leading to the Imam's retraction.
C) It is mursal and therefore not used.
D) It is only used by the Sahibayn and not by Imam Abu Hanifa.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school ultimately permits wiping over thick socks that enable walking a farsakh, based on the Prophet's action and the Imam's retraction.

No Wiping on Turban, Cap, Burqa, or Gloves
States the invalidity of wiping on head and hand coverings with legal rationale.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on wiping over a turban, cap, burqa, and gloves, and explain the legal reasoning that prevents extending the khuff dispensation to these items.

Core Idea
Wiping over coverings is limited to the khuff only—exceptions to qiyas cannot be extended.

In wudu, wiping over a khuff is a special dispensation. This lesson clarifies that this dispensation does not apply to other head and hand coverings. The text from Kanz al-Daqa'iq states unequivocally that wiping on a turban, cap, burqa, or gloves is impermissible, and provides two key reasons: first, the khuff ruling is a text-based exception to analogy, so it cannot be extended; second, there is no hardship in removing these items, unlike the khuff.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Items
List the four coverings mentioned: turban (عمامة), cap (قلنسوة), burqa (برقع), gloves (قفازين). Recognize that these cover the head or hands but are not the same as khuffs in legal terms.
2
Recognize the General Principle
Recall that wiping over a covering is generally not allowed; the only exception is the khuff (leather socks/overshoes) as established by textual evidence.
The Hanafi school treats the khuff dispensation as a unique ruling contrary to qiyas.
3
Understand the First Reason: Exception Cannot Be Extended
Since the permissibility of wiping on khuffs is proven by text (nas) against analogy, it cannot be extended to other items via qiyas. The rule: what thabata 'alā khilāf al-qiyās lā yulḥaq bihi ghayruh.
This is a key usul principle: exceptions to qiyas are not analogized.
4
Understand the Second Reason: No Hardship
Unlike khuffs, which are difficult to remove repeatedly, these items (turban, cap, burqa, gloves) are easily removed. Therefore, there is no need for a dispensation.
The term 'masaha' (wiping) on these items does not fulfill the requirement of washing the respective body part.
5
Conclude the Ruling
Based on these two reasons, wiping on these items is invalid (lā yajūz). Within the Hanafi school, there is no disagreement on this point.
Some other schools allow wiping on turbans in certain situations, but the Hanafi position is strict.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا على عمامة وقلنسوة وبُرقع وقفازين. وهذا مما لا خلاف في عدم جواز مسح هذه الأشياء؛ لأن المسح على الخف ثبت بالنص على خلاف القياس فلا يلحق به غيره، وأيضاً لا مشقة في نزع هذه الأشياء بخلاف الخف، فامتنع الإلحاق، و"القلنسوة" بفتحتين وضم المهملة، يلف عليه العمامة. (فتح) وبرقع بضم الباء، والقاف الذي تغطي به النساء وجوهها. وقفازين بضم القاف وتشديد الفاء، تثنية قفاز، وهو شيء يلبسه النساء والصيادون في أيديهم.
Not on a turban, cap, burqa, or gloves. And this is something in which there is no disagreement regarding the impermissibility of wiping these things, because wiping on the khuff is established by textual evidence contrary to analogy, so nothing else is annexed to it. Also, there is no hardship in removing these things unlike the khuff, so annexation is disallowed. And the cap (qalansuwa): with two fatha and a damma on the sīn, around which the turban is wrapped. (Fath) And burqa: with a damma on the bā and qāf, that which women cover their faces with. And gloves (quffāzain): with a damma on the qāf and tashdīd on the fā, dual of quffāz, a thing worn by women and hunters on their hands.
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement explaining that wiping over a turban, cap, burqa, or gloves is not valid for wudu. The author clarifies that there is consensus (within the Hanafi school) on this point. The reasoning is twofold: first, the permissibility of wiping over khuffs is an exception to the general rule (qiyas) established by a specific text; therefore, it cannot be extended to other items via analogy. Second, unlike khuffs, these items are easily removed, so there is no hardship requiring a dispensation. The passage then provides definitions of these items: the qalansuwa is a cap worn under the turban, the burqa is a face veil, and quffāzain are gloves. This ruling is important for students to understand that the dispensation for wiping is strictly limited to what the texts specify, and not all head or hand coverings qualify.

Key Terms
القلنسوة (al-qalansuwa): A cap worn under the turban.
البرقع (al-burqu'): A face veil worn by women.
القفازين (al-quffāzain): Gloves worn by women or hunters.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the reason given for not allowing wiping on a turban or cap?
A) Because the Prophet never did it.
B) Because these items are easily removed, so there is no hardship.
C) Because they are not made of leather.
D) Because they cover only part of the head.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over head and hand coverings other than the khuff is invalid because the khuff dispensation is an exception that cannot be extended and there is no hardship in removing them.

Wiping over Splint (Jabira) and Bandage: Conditions and Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Fiqh ruling on wiping over splints with hadith evidence and intra-madhhab disagreement.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi conditions for wiping over a splint (jabira) and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding its obligatory nature.

Core Idea
Wiping over a splint is a valid substitute for washing, but its obligation is disputed between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples.

This lesson examines the fiqh of wiping over medical wrappings (jabira and bandages). Based on the hadith of Ali (RA), the Hanafi school permits wiping when removal would cause harm. However, there is a difference of opinion within the school on the ruling's binding force. We will unpack the conditions, the extent of wiping, and the evidence for each position.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Evidence
The primary evidence is the hadith of Ali (RA) who said: 'One of my forearms was broken, so the Messenger of Allah commanded me to wipe over it.' Note the imperative 'amsah' (wipe) and how it is interpreted by different Hanafi imams.
The hadith is found in various sources; it is a khabar wahid (single narration).
2
Determine the Conditions for Wiping
Wiping over a bandage is permissible only when removing it and washing the wound would cause harm (darrar). If no harm, one must remove the bandage and wash normally. This condition is explicit in the text.
The condition of harm is key – without it, the ruling reverts to washing.
3
Extent of Wiping
The text states the stronger view (al-asahh) is that wiping over the majority (al-akthar) of the bandage suffices. The fatwa is upon this. Understand that complete coverage is not required, but the majority must be wiped.
This is based on the report of Ibn Ziyad and is relied upon.
4
Explore the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Abu Hanifa holds that wiping over the splint is not fard nor wajib; omitting it without excuse leaves the prayer valid but the person sinful? Actually, he says the prayer is valid. The Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold it is wajib; omitting it without harm invalidates the prayer. The mufta bihi is the Sahibayn's view: it is wajib but not fard, so prayer is valid if omitted but sin is incurred.
The reconciliation mentioned in the text is that they are discussing different scenarios (with or without harm). The relied-upon view is that it is wajib.
5
Apply the Ruling to Falling of Bandage
If the bandage falls off after healing (bar'), the wipe is invalidated and the area must be washed for future prayers. If it falls before healing, the wipe remains valid and the bandage can be replaced without repeating the wipe.
This shows the temporary nature of the wipe – it lasts only as long as the excuse.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والمسح على الجبيرة [وهي العيدان التي تجبر بها العظام المكسورة] الأصل في جواز المسح على هذه الأشياء حديث علي أنه قال: "كسرت إحدى زندي، فأمرني رسول الله أن أمسح عليها"، ثم هذا، وإن كان في الجبيرة خاصة، لكن عرف الحكم في القروح بدلالة النص. (مستخلص) كالغسل هذا لا يشمل ما إذا كان بالرأس جراحة فإن وظيفتها المسح، ويمكن الجواب بأنه من باب التغليب، وفي "المبتغى" : ومن كان جميع رأسه مجروحا لا يجب المسح عليه؛ لأن المسح بدل عن الغسل ولا بدل للمسح، وقيل: يجب، والصواب هو الوجوب، وقوله: "المسح بدل عن الغسل غير صحيح؛ لأن المسح على الرأس أصل بنفسه لا بدل عنه كما لا يخفى البحر الرائق بلا وضوء لأن في اعتباره حرجاً بخلاف الخف. على كل العصابة كان تحتها جراحة أو لا، فإن سقطت عن برء بطل وإلا لا، أي العصابة ولا يفتقر إلى النية في مسح الخف والرأس. على كل العصابة وعن ابن زياد إن مسح على الأكثر جاز، وإلا فلا، وهو الأصح، أي الحكم بالجواز في استيعاب الأكثر وعليه الفتوى هذا إذا كان حل الخرقة وغسل ما تحتها يضره، وإن كان الحل لا يضر الجرح ولا يضر المسح أيضاً، فعليه النزع وغسل ما حول الجراحة، والمسح على الجراحة بشرط أن يتمكن من الحل والربط، وإذا لم يتمكن بأن كان في محل لا يقدر على ربطها بنفسه ولا يجد من يربطها فعليه المسح على كلها أو أكثرها. مسكين وغيره العصابة أي ما تشد بها الجراحة. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٠/١] 11 عن برء: البرء: بالفتح عند أهل الحجاز، وبالضم عند غيرهم، وعن" بمعنى لام التعليل، أي لأجل برء، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اسْتِغْفَارُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ لِأَبِيهِ إِلَّا عَنْ مَوْعِدَةٍ وَعَدَهَا إِيَّاهُ ﴾ (التوبة: ١١٤)، كذا في "مغني اللبيب"، ويجوز أن تكون بمعنى "بعد"، على حد قوله تعالى: لَتَرْكَبُنَّ طَبَقاً عَنْ طَبَقٍ ﴾ (الانشقاق:١٩)، أي حالة بعد حالة، وفي كلام القهستاني ما يفيد أن "عن" بمعنى الباء السببية. فتح المعين بطل لزوال العذر، فيغسل موضعها إن كان متوضئا بخلاف الخف فإنه يغسل التي سقط خفها والرجل الأخرى أيضاً فلو وجد البرء و لم تسقط الجبيرة فيبطل المسح فيما إذا لم يضره إزالة الجبيرة، أما إذا ضره لشدة لصوقها به فلا. تتمة: في "جامع الجوامع : رجل به رمد فداواه وأمر أن لا يغسل فهو كالجبيرة، وفي "البرهان": لو انكسر ظفره فجعل عليه دواء أو علكا، فإن كان يضره نزعه مسح عليه وإن ضره المسح تركه وإن كان بأعضائه شقوق أمر عليها الماء إن قدر وإلا مسح عليها إن قدر وإلا تركها وغسل ما حولها، وإذا توضأ وأمر الماء على الدواء ثم سقط الدواء، إن سقط عن برء يجب غسل ذلك الموضع وإلا فلا. (فتح المعين) وإلا لا: وليس عليه إعادتها بعينها، حتى لو وضع غيرها لا تجب إعادته، لكنه أحسن واعلم أن السقوط ليس بقيد حتى لو بدلها قبل البرء لم يبطل المسح أيضاً، فيمضي على صلاته، أما إذا ترك المسح على الجبيرة فقد صح مطلقاً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: إن لم يضره لا يصح، وهذا مخالف لما قرروه من الفرق بين النجاسة والحدث بأن النجاسة يعفى عن قليلها والحدث لا يعفى عن قليله وقال في "الغاية": والصحيح أن المسح على الجبيرة واجب عنده، وليس بفرض حتى تجوز صلاته، بدونه وقيل لا خلاف بينهم؛ لأنهما إنما قالا بعدم جواز ترك المسح فيمن لا يضره المسح، وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بالجواز فيمن يضره. فتح المعين وقال في "المستخلص" : إن مسح الجبيرة عندهما واجب لا يجوز تركه إلا للضرورة، لهما: إنه معتبر بالمسح على الخف والجامع بينهما الحرج، ولأن النبي الأمر عليا بالمسح عليها، والأمر للوجوب، وعند أبي حنيفة : ليس بفرض، ولو ترك من غير عذر جاز؛ لأن خبر الواحد لا يثبت بالفرضية؛ ولأن ما تحتها لو كان باديا لا يجب عليه الغسل، فكذا مسحه في المجروح للجرح، وحديث علي في المكسور فلا يقاس عليه غيره. الخف والرأس : لأنهما جزءان من الوضوء، وهو لا يفتقر إلى النية، فجزؤه أولى. (مستخلص)
Wiping over the splint: [which are the sticks that set broken bones] The basis for the permissibility of wiping over these things is the hadith of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him) who said: 'One of my forearms was broken, so the Messenger of Allah (peace be upon him) commanded me to wipe over it.' Then this, although it is specifically about the splint, the ruling was known for wounds through textual indication. (Mustakhlas) Like washing, this does not include if there is a wound on the head, for its function is wiping, and it can be answered that it is a matter of predominant usage. In al-Mubtagha: Whoever has his entire head wounded, wiping is not obligatory upon him, because wiping is a substitute for washing, and there is no substitute for wiping. It is said: wajib, and the correct view is wujub. His statement: 'Wiping is a substitute for washing' is incorrect, because wiping on the head is original in itself, not a substitute, as is clear in al-Bahr al-Raiq. Without wudu because considering it would be a hardship, unlike the khuff. Over the entire bandage, whether there is a wound under it or not. If it falls off after healing, it is invalidated; otherwise not. Meaning the bandage. And no intention (niyyah) is required for wiping over the khuff and head. Over the entire bandage. And from Ibn Ziyad: If he wipes over the majority, it is valid; otherwise not, and this is the correct view. Meaning the ruling of permissibility is in covering the majority, and the fatwa is upon this. This is if removing the bandage and washing what is under it harms him. If removing does not harm the wound and also does not harm the wiping, then he must remove and wash around the wound, and wipe over the wound on the condition that he is able to untie and tie. If he is unable, such as being in a place where he cannot tie it himself and finds no one to tie it, then he must wipe over all of it or most of it. Miskin and others: al-‘isābah is that with which the wound is tied. [Ramz al-Haqā'iq: 30/1] 11 'An bar’ (after healing): al-bar’ is with a fatha according to the people of Hijaz, and with a damma according to others; 'an denotes the lam of causation, i.e., for the purpose of healing, as in the verse: 'And the request of forgiveness of Ibrahim for his father was only because of a promise he had made to him' (9:114), as in Mughni al-Labib. It is permissible that it means 'after', on the basis of the verse: 'You will surely ride layer after layer' (84:19), i.e., state after state. In the words of al-Qahistani, it suggests that 'an is causative. (Fath al-Mu'in) It becomes invalid due to the removal of the excuse; so he must wash that place if he is in a state of wudu, unlike the khuff, for he washes the khuff that fell off and the other foot as well. If healing occurs but the splint does not fall, then the wipe becomes invalid if removing the splint does not harm him. But if it harms him due to severe adhesion, then no. Supplement in Jami' al-Jawami': A man with ophthalmia treated himself and was told not to wash, so it is like the splint. In al-Burhan: If his nail broke and he placed medicine or gum on it, if removing it harms him, he wipes over it; if wiping harms him, he leaves it. If there are fissures on his limbs, he pours water over them if he can; otherwise he wipes over them; otherwise he leaves them and washes around them. If he performs wudu and pours water over the medicine, then the medicine falls, if it falls after healing, he must wash that spot; otherwise no. (Fath al-Mu'in) And 'otherwise no': he is not required to replace it with the same bandage; even if he replaces it with another, he need not repeat it, but it is better. Know that falling off is not a condition; even if he changes it before healing, the wipe is not invalidated either, so he proceeds with his prayer. As for leaving the wipe on the splint, it is absolutely valid according to Abu Hanifa. According to the two, if it does not harm him, it is not valid. This contradicts what they established regarding the difference between najasah and hadath: that little najasah is excused but little hadath is not. In al-Ghayah: The correct view is that wiping over the splint is wajib according to him, but not fard, so his prayer is valid without it. Some said there is no disagreement between them because the two only said the impermissibility of leaving the wipe for one whom the wipe does not harm, while Abu Hanifa only said permissibility for one whom the wipe harms. (Fath al-Mu'in) In al-Mustakhlas: According to both, wiping over the splint is wajib, it is not permissible to leave it except for necessity. Their evidence: it is analogized to wiping over the khuff, and the connecting factor is hardship. Also, the Prophet commanded Ali to wipe over it, and a command indicates obligation. According to Abu Hanifa, it is not fard, and if he leaves it without excuse, it is valid, because a khabar wahid does not establish fardiyyah. Also, if what is under it were exposed, he would not be required to wash, similarly in the case of a wound. The hadith of Ali is about a broken bone, so it cannot be analogized to others. The khuff and head: because they are parts of wudu, which does not require intention, so their parts are more deserving (of not requiring intention). (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 40

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of wiping over a splint (jabira) and wound bandage. It opens by citing the hadith of Ali (RA) as the basis: when his forearm was broken, the Prophet ordered him to wipe over the splint. This establishes the permissibility. The author notes that although the hadith is specific to a broken bone, the ruling extends to wounds by textual indication. The passage then delves into details: the wipe is like washing (ghusl) in that it is not time-limited and can be combined with washing. It does not require intention (niyyah). If the bandage covers a wound, the ruling applies whether or not there is a wound underneath. The key condition is that removing the bandage and washing the area must be harmful. If not, one must remove and wash. The extent of wiping: according to the stronger view (al-asahh), wiping over the majority (al-akthar) suffices, and this is the fatwa. The passage also discusses what happens when the bandage falls off: if it falls after healing (bar'), the wipe is invalidated and one must wash the area if in wudu; if before healing, it is not invalidated. Finally, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds that if one leaves the wipe entirely, the prayer is valid but sinful if no excuse? Actually, he says it is valid absolutely (even without excuse). The Sahibayn say if wiping does not harm, it is not valid to leave it. The author reconciles by noting they are discussing different scenarios (with or without harm). The relied-upon position is that wiping is wajib (obligatory) but not fard, meaning if omitted, the prayer is valid but the person is blameworthy. This concludes the detailed ruling on jabira.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabīra): Splints or sticks used to set broken bones.
العصابة (al-‘iṣābah): Bandage or cloth tied around a wound.
البرء (al-bar’): Healing or recovery from an injury.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Yes, because any amount suffices.

C) Yes, because the fatwa is that wiping the majority (al-akthar) is sufficient.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a valid alternative to washing when harmful; the relied-upon view makes it wajib, but not fard, so the prayer is valid if omitted, though the person is sinful.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Rulings on Wiping over the Splint and the Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Intra-Hanafi dispute on wiping the splint with conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for wiping over a splint according to the Hanafi school and explain the disagreement between Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn regarding its obligation.

Core Idea
Wiping the splint is wajib according to the Sahibayn; Abu Hanifa holds it is not fard, but the practical difference hinges on whether harm is present.

This lesson explores the rulings on wiping over a splint (jabirah) during wudu, a concession for those with wounds. The Hanafi school has an important internal dispute: Abu Hanifa considers wiping not fard, while the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) consider it wajib. We will also examine the conditions that determine whether wiping or washing is required.

Guided Path
1
State the general rule and conditions
First, understand the basic rule: wiping over the entire bandage is required if removing it would harm the wound. If not harmful, wash around the wound and wipe only the wound itself. If unable to tie the bandage, wipe over the majority or the entire bandage.
The text also introduces a separate ruling that intention is not required for wiping the khuff and head.
2
Identify the dispute: Abu Hanifa vs. Sahibayn
The core ikhtilaf: Abu Hanifa says leaving the wipe without excuse does not invalidate the prayer (the wipe is not fard). The Sahibayn say it is wajib; omitting it without necessity invalidates the prayer.
The dispute is recorded in al-Mustakhlas and other sources.
3
Analyze the proofs for each side
The Sahibayn use qiyas to wiping over khuff (hardship as the common factor) and a hadith of the Prophet ordering Ali (peace be upon him) to wipe over a splint, arguing that a command indicates wujub. Abu Hanifa responds that the hadith is a solitary report (khabar wahid) which cannot establish fardiyyah, and that if the wound were exposed, washing would not be obligatory, so wiping is likewise not obligatory.
The text also mentions a reconciliation attempt in al-Ghayah: perhaps the difference is based on whether harm is present.
4
Note the thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence)
According to Abu Hanifa, a person who prays without wiping (without excuse) has a valid prayer. According to the Sahibayn, that prayer is invalid and must be repeated if the person was aware of the ruling.
Later Hanafi fatwa tends to prefer the Sahibayn's view for caution, but this passage does not definitively tarjih.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة ٤٠ حكم الجرموق وغيره أي الجبيرة أي لأجل برء على كل العصابة كان تحتها جراحة أو لا، فإن سقطت عن برء بطل وإلا لا، أي العصابة ولا يفتقر إلى النية في مسح الخف والرأس. على كل العصابة وعن ابن زياد إن مسح على الأكثر جاز، وإلا فلا، وهو الأصح، أي الحكم بالجواز في استيعاب الأكثر وعليه الفتوى هذا إذا كان حل الخرقة وغسل ما تحتها يضره، وإن كان الحل لا يضر الجرح ولا يضر المسح أيضاً، فعليه النزع وغسل ما حول الجراحة، والمسح على الجراحة بشرط أن يتمكن من الحل والربط، وإذا لم يتمكن بأن كان في محل لا يقدر على ربطها بنفسه ولا يجد من يربطها فعليه المسح على كلها أو أكثرها. مسكين وغيره العصابة أي ما تشد بها الجراحة. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٠/١]

11 عن برء: البرء: بالفتح عند أهل الحجاز، وبالضم عند غيرهم، وعن" بمعنى لام التعليل، أي لأجل برء، كما في قوله تعالى: ﴿وَمَا كَانَ اسْتِغْفَارُ إِبْرَاهِيمَ لِأَبِيهِ إِلَّا عَنْ مَوْعِدَةٍ وَعَدَهَا إِيَّاهُ ﴾ (التوبة: ١١٤)، كذا في "مغني اللبيب"، ويجوز أن تكون بمعنى "بعد"، "، على حد قوله تعالى: لَتَرْكَبُنَّ طَبَقاً عَنْ طَبَقٍ ﴾ (الانشقاق:١٩)، أي حالة بعد حالة، وفي كلام القهستاني ما يفيد أن "عن" بمعنى الباء السببية. فتح المعين بطل لزوال العذر ، فيغسل موضعها إن كان متوضئا بخلاف الخف فإنه يغسل التي سقط خفها والرجل الأخرى أيضاً فلو وجد البرء و لم تسقط الجبيرة فيبطل المسح فيما إذا لم يضره إزالة الجبيرة، أما إذا ضره لشدة لصوقها به فلا. تتمة: في "جامع الجوامع : رجل به رمد فداواه وأمر أن لا يغسل فهو كالجبيرة، وفي "البرهان": لو انكسر ظفره فجعل عليه دواء أو علكا، فإن كان يضره نزعه مسح عليه وإن ضره المسح تركه وإن كان بأعضائه شقوق أمر عليها الماء إن قدر وإلا مسح عليها إن قدر وإلا تركها وغسل ما حولها، وإذا توضأ وأمر الماء على الدواء ثم سقط الدواء، إن سقط عن برء يجب غسل ذلك الموضع وإلا فلا. (فتح المعين)

وإلا لا: وليس عليه إعادتها بعينها، حتى لو وضع غيرها لا تجب إعادته، لكنه أحسن واعلم أن السقوط ليس بقيد حتى لو بدلها قبل البرء لم يبطل المسح أيضاً، فيمضي على صلاته، أما إذا ترك المسح على الجبيرة فقد صح مطلقاً عند أبي حنيفة، وعندهما: إن لم يضره لا يصح، وهذا مخالف لما قرروه من الفرق بين النجاسة والحدث بأن النجاسة يعفى عن قليلها والحدث لا يعفى عن قليله وقال في "الغاية": والصحيح أن المسح على الجبيرة واجب عنده، وليس بفرض حتى تجوز صلاته ،بدونه وقيل لا خلاف بينهم؛ لأنهما إنما قالا بعدم جواز ترك المسح فيمن لا يضره المسح، وإنما قال أبو حنيفة بالجواز فيمن يضره. فتح (المعين وقال في "المستخلص" : إن مسح الجبيرة عندهما واجب لا يجوز تركه إلا للضرورة، لهما: إنه معتبر بالمسح على الخف والجامع بينهما الحرج، ولأن النبي الهلال الأمر عليا بالمسح عليها، والأمر للوجوب، وعند أبي حنيفة : ليس بفرض، ولو ترك من غير عذر جاز؛ لأن خبر الواحد لا يثبت بالفرضية؛ ولأن ما تحتها لو كان باديا لا يجب عليه الغسل، فكذا مسحه في المجروح للجرح، وحديث علي في المكسور فلا يقاس عليه غيره.

الخف والرأس : لأنهما جزءان من الوضوء، وهو لا يفتقر إلى النية، فجزؤه أولى. (مستخلص)
Book of Purification 40. Ruling of the boot and other than it, i.e., the splint, i.e., for the sake of healing. Over the entire bandage, whether there was a wound under it or not. If it falls off after healing, the wipe is invalidated, otherwise not. i.e., the bandage. And intention is not required in wiping the khuff and the head. Over the entire bandage. And from Ibn Ziyad: if he wipes over the majority, it is permissible, otherwise not. And it is the most correct view, i.e., the ruling of permissibility in covering the majority, and upon it is the fatwa. This is if loosening the cloth and washing what is under it harms him. But if loosening does not harm the wound and also does not harm the wipe, then he must remove it and wash around the wound, and wipe over the wound provided he is able to loosen and tie. And if he is not able, such as if it is in a place he cannot tie himself and finds no one to tie it, then he must wipe over all of it or most of it. Miskin and others: the bandage, i.e., what the wound is tied with. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 30/1] 11. 'an bar' (after healing): al-bar' is with fath (a) by the people of Hijaz, and with damm (u) by others. And 'an' (from) is in the sense of lam al-ta'lil (causal lām), i.e., for the sake of healing, as in the verse of the Quran (9:114). Similarly in Mughni al-Labib. And it is permissible to be in the sense of 'after', as in the verse (84:19), i.e., state after state. And in the words of al-Qahistani, it indicates that 'an' is in the sense of the causative bā'. Fath al-Mu'in: It becomes invalid due to the removal of the excuse, so he washes that place if he was in a state of wudu, unlike the khuff, for he washes the foot whose khuff fell off and also the other foot. So if he finds healing and the splint does not fall off, the wipe becomes invalid if removing the splint does not harm him. But if it harms him due to its strong adhesion, then no. Completion: In Jami' al-Jawami': A man with ophthalmia, he treated it and was ordered not to wash it, so it is like the splint. In al-Burhan: If his nail breaks and he puts medicine or gum on it, if removal harms him, he wipes over it; if wiping harms him, he leaves it; if there are cracks on his limbs, he pours water over them if able, otherwise wipes over them if able, otherwise leaves them and washes around them. When he performs wudu and pours water over the medicine, then the medicine falls off, if it falls after healing, he must wash that place, otherwise no. (Fath al-Mu'in) And otherwise no: He is not required to repeat it [the wipe] in particular, so if he puts another, he is not required to repeat it, but it is better. Know that falling off is not a condition, so if he replaces it before healing, the wipe does not become invalid either, so he continues his prayer. As for leaving the wipe on the splint, it is valid absolutely according to Abu Hanifa. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad): if it does not harm him, it is not valid. This contradicts what they established regarding the difference between najasah and hadath: that a small amount of najasah is excused, but a small amount of hadath is not excused. And it is said in al-Ghayah: The correct view is that wiping over the splint is wajib (obligatory) according to him (Abu Hanifa? unclear), and it is not fard (farḍ) so that his prayer is valid without it. And it is said there is no disagreement between them, because they only said the impermissibility of leaving the wipe in one who is not harmed by the wipe, and Abu Hanifa only said permissibility in one who is harmed. Fath al-Mu'in. And it is said in al-Mustakhlas: Indeed, wiping over the splint is wajib according to them (the Sahibayn); it is not permissible to leave it except out of necessity. Their evidence: It is compared to wiping over the khuff, and the common factor is hardship. And because the Prophet (peace be upon him) ordered Ali to wipe over it, and a command indicates obligation. According to Abu Hanifa: It is not fard, and if he leaves it without an excuse, it is permissible, because a khabar wahid (solitary hadith) does not establish farḍiyyah (obligation), and because if what is under it were exposed, he would not be required to wash it, so likewise wiping over it for the wounded is for the wound, and the hadith of Ali about a broken bone cannot be analogized to others. The khuff and the head: because they are parts of wudu, and wudu does not require intention, so its part is more deserving. (Mustakhlas)
Source pages p. 41

Commentary
This passage continues the discussion on purification, specifically the ruling of wiping over a splint (jabirah) and related items like boots (jarmuq). The author first states the general ruling: wiping over the entire bandage is required, whether there is a wound underneath or not. If the bandage falls off after healing, the previous wipe is invalidated, and one must wash the area if in a state of wudu; otherwise, the wipe remains valid. The commentary clarifies that the word 'an in 'an bar' means 'for the sake of healing' or 'after', and provides linguistic evidence from the Quran. The text then explains conditions: if removing the bandage and washing underneath would harm the wound, wiping over the bandage is allowed. If removal is not harmful, one must remove it and wash the area. If one cannot tie the bandage oneself and finds no one to help, one must wipe over the entire bandage or most of it. The dispute between Abu Hanifa and the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) is discussed in detail. According to Abu Hanifa, if one leaves the wipe on the splint without any excuse, the prayer is still valid because it is not fard (obligatory). The Sahibayn hold that wiping over the splint is wajib (obligatory) and cannot be left except for necessity; otherwise, the prayer is invalid. Abu Hanifa argues that the solitary hadith on this matter does not establish a fard obligation, and that if the wound were exposed, washing would not be required, so wiping is not obligatory. The Sahibayn analogize it to wiping over the khuff, citing hardship and an order of the Prophet (peace be upon him) to Ali. The commentary reconciles some views, stating that the difference may be based on whether harm exists. The passage concludes with a note that intention is not required for wiping over the khuff and head, as these are parts of wudu, which itself does not require intention.

Key Terms
الجبيرة (al-jabīrah): A splint or bandage placed over a wound to protect it during healing.
البرء (al-bar'): Healing or recovery from a wound; when the wound has healed under the bandage.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks worn over the feet; wiping over them is permitted in wudu under certain conditions.
الحرج (al-ḥaraj): Hardship or difficulty; a legal cause for concessions.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the dispute mentioned in the passage, what is the ruling on leaving the wipe over the splint without any excuse according to Abu Hanifa?
A) The prayer is invalid because wiping is wajib.
B) The prayer is valid because wiping is not fard.
C) The prayer is invalid only if the person is harmed.
D) The prayer is valid only if the intention was made.

Key Takeaway
Wiping over a splint is a concession for wounds; the Hanafi school has an internal disagreement on whether it is wajib or not fard, with the majority later preferring wujub.

Taharah — Purification

Definition of Hayd: Blood from the Womb of an Adult Healthy Woman
Definition of hayd with conditions and intra-Hanafi dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the three components of the Hanafi definition of hayd (source, condition, duration) and distinguish hayd from istihadah, nifas, and other bleeding.

Core Idea
Hayd is blood that exits the womb to the external vulva – only that from a healthy adult woman.

In this lesson, we unpack the Hanafi definition of hayd as given in Kanz al-Daqa'iq. The definition is precise: hayd is blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood. Each term excludes specific types of bleeding. We will analyze the conditions and the intra-Hanafi disagreement about the descent of blood to the external versus internal vulva.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic and legal definition
The passage defines hayd as 'blood discharged by the womb'. Note that 'yandafuhu' implies falling to the external vulva. This is the core.
The term 'yandafuhu' is a loose usage; technically it means to shake off, but here it means to exit.
2
Analyse the condition 'free from disease'
Blood from nifas, wounds, or boils in the womb is excluded. The woman in nifas is considered ill.
This condition excludes blood that is not from a healthy reproductive system.
3
Analyse the condition 'free from childhood'
Blood from a minor girl is not hayd; it is istihadah. The restriction 'woman' already implies adulthood.
Some scholars consider this condition redundant, but it is stated explicitly.
4
Examine the requirement 'woman'
Non-human animals do not menstruate. The blood from a minor girl is also excluded by this term.
The definition uses 'woman' to indicate a mature female.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on internal vs external descent
Muhammad considers blood reaching the internal vulva as hayd; the majority (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf) require external descent. The fatwa follows the majority.
This affects whether blood that does not exit the body is considered hayd.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الحيض أي بيان أحكامه س ف ك هو دم ينفضه رحم امرأة سليمة عن داء وصغر، وأقله ثلاثة أيام . وعن وسببه ابتلاء كما الله هو منبت الولد في البطن باب الحيض: مناسبة إيراد هذا الباب عقب الأبواب المتقدمة أنه ذكر هناك حكم الطهارة بعد انقطاع الحيض والنفاس، ولم يذكر حكم امتدادهما وحقيقتهما، فبين في هذا الباب حكم الامتداد والحقيقة، وإنما لقب الباب بالحيض دون النفاس مع أن الباب مشتمل عليهما؛ لأنه أكثر وقوعاً من النفاس، والمصنف ذكر ضمير الحيض في تعريفه مذكراً مع أنه مؤنث سماعي؛ لأن استعمال التذكير فيه أكثر. (فتح، مسكين) دم ينفضه: هذا تعريف مبني على القول بأنه من الأنجاس وعلى القول بأنه من الأحداث فمانعيته شرعية بسبب الدم المذكور عما اشترط فيها الطهارة وعن الصوم والمسجد والقربان ويقال له نفاس وطمث بالمثلثة وبالمثناة، وبالسين المهملة ومعنى قوله ينفضه، أي يسقط إلى الفرج الخارج، وإن كان النفض في الأصل تحريك الشيء، ليسقط ما عليه من غبار، ففي كلام المصنف تسامح، فلو نزل الدم إلى الفرج الداخل لم يكن حيضاً في ظاهر الرواية، محمد أنه حيض، وكذا النفاس، وبالأول يفتى ولا تثبت الاستحاضة إلا بالنزول إلى الخارج بلا خلاف. لحواء عليها السلام حين تناولت من شجرة الخلد وبقي هو في بناتها إلى يوم التناد بذلك السبب، روت عائشة قالت : قال النبي في الحيض: "هذا شيء كتبه الله على بنات آدم". (فتح المعين) رحم امرأة خرج به دم الرعاف ودم الجراحات ودم الاستحاضة؛ لأنه دم عرق كما في الحديث، فلم يكن خارجاً من الرحم، وخرج أيضاً ما يخرج من دبر ،المرأة، وإن ندب إمساك زوجها واغتسالها منه، وبقيد "امرأة" خرج ما تراه الصغيرة وما يخرج من غير الآدمية كالأرنب والضبع والخفاش ولا يحيض غيرها من الحيوانات. (فتح المعين) عن داء: أي عن داء الولادة، خرج به دم النفاس، فإن النفساء في حكم المريضة حتى اعتبرت تبرعاتها . وخرج به أيضاً دم يخرج من جراحة أو دمل في الرحم. رمز الحقائق بتغير يسير: ٣١/١] وصغر العامل فيه محذوف، أي خالية عن الصغر، كما في علقتها تبنا وماء بارداً"، أي وسقيت، وهذا القيد مستدرك للاستغناء عنه بذكر المرأة؛ لأن المرأة اسم البالغة كالرجل اسم البالغ كذا في "المغرب"، وقال العيني: إن ما تراه الصغيرة استحاضة وليس بدم ،رحم، فخرج بالقيد الأول. (فتح) وأقله ثلاثة أيام لم يتعرض لذكر ليال إما اكتفاء بظاهر المذهب أن أقله ثلاثة أيام وثلاث ليال؛ لأن ذكر الأيام بلفظ الجمع يتناول ما يقابلها من الليالي، أو اختياراً لما روي عن أبي يوسف أن الشرط ليال تقع في هذه الأيام لا ثلاث ليال حتى لو رأت الدم عند طلوع الفجر يوم السبت وانقطع عند غروب الشمس يوم الاثنين يكون حيضاً، من الثلث وقال أبو يوسف أقله يومان وأكثر اليوم الثالث؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وقال الشافعي وأحمد أقله مقدر :
Chapter of Hayd (Menstruation): i.e., explanation of its rulings. [Abbreviations: س ف ك]. It is blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood. Its minimum is three days. And its cause is a trial from Allah. The womb is the origin of the child in the belly. Chapter of Hayd: The appropriateness of placing this chapter after the preceding chapters: because there the ruling of purification after the cessation of hayd and nifas was mentioned, but the ruling of their duration and reality was not mentioned, so in this chapter the ruling of duration and reality is explained. The chapter is named hayd and not nifas even though the chapter includes both, because hayd occurs more frequently than nifas. The author used the masculine pronoun for hayd in its definition even though it is a feminine noun by convention, because masculine usage is more common. (Fath, Miskin) Blood discharged: This definition is based on the view that it is from the impurities (najasat), and on the view that it is from the events (ahdath), so its prohibition is legal due to the mentioned blood from what requires purity, and from fasting, mosque, and sacrifice. It is also called nifas and tamth. The meaning of 'yandafuhu' (discharges) is that it falls to the external vulva, even though nafd originally means to shake something to remove dust, so the author's usage is loose. If the blood descends to the internal vulva, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah); Muhammad says it is hayd. Similarly for nifas. And the first view is given fatwa. Istihadah is only confirmed by descent to the external without disagreement. Hawwa (Eve) when she ate from the tree of immortality, and it remained in her daughters until the Day of Calling for that reason. Aisha narrated that the Prophet said regarding hayd: 'This is something that Allah wrote upon the daughters of Adam.' (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Womb of a woman' excludes the blood of nosebleed, wounds, and istihadah, because that is blood from a vein as in the hadith, so it is not from the womb. It also excludes what exits from the anus of a woman, even if her husband is encouraged to refrain and she performs ghusl. By the restriction 'woman' it excludes what a minor girl sees and what exits from non-human animals like rabbits, hyenas, bats; other animals do not menstruate. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Free from disease': i.e., free from the disease of childbirth, which excludes the blood of nifas, because the woman in nifas is considered ill such that her gifts are considered. Also excludes blood from a wound or boil in the womb. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq with slight change: 31/1) 'And childhood': the operative word is omitted, i.e., free from childhood, as in 'she fed it straw and cold water', i.e., and watered it. This restriction is redundant because mentioning 'woman' suffices, as woman is a term for a mature female just as man is a term for a mature male, as in al-Mughrib. Al-Ayni said: What a minor girl sees is istihadah and is not blood of the womb, so it is excluded by the first restriction. (Fath) 'Its minimum is three days': It did not mention nights, either because it relies on the apparent madhhab that its minimum is three days and three nights, since mentioning 'days' in plural includes their corresponding nights, or by choice according to what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the condition is nights that fall within these days, not three nights, such that if she sees blood at the break of dawn on Saturday and it stops at sunset on Monday, it is hayd. From the third. And Abu Yusuf said: Its minimum is two days and the majority of the third day, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: Its minimum is a set amount [cut off].
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on hayd (menstruation). The author first explains why this chapter is placed after the preceding ones: because earlier the rulings of purification after hayd and nifas were mentioned, but not their duration and reality. This chapter addresses that. The chapter is named 'hayd' even though it includes nifas, because hayd is more common. The definiens is 'blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood.' The word 'yandafuhu' means to fall to the external vulva; if the blood only reaches the internal vulva, it is not hayd in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), but Muhammad says it is. The definition excludes blood from nosebleeds, wounds, istihadah (chronic bleeding), and blood from a minor girl or animals. The minimum duration is three days according to Abu Hanifa. The text notes that he did not mention nights, likely because the plural 'days' includes the intervening nights as per the apparent madhhab. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf states that it is three days but the nights are not required to be full; for example, if blood starts at dawn Saturday and stops at sunset Monday, that counts as three days. Abu Yusuf's own view is that the minimum is two days and the majority of the third day. The passage also mentions the views of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, but the text cuts off before stating their exact opinion. The hadith from Aisha is quoted to show that hayd is a divine decree for women. The commentary from Fath al-Mu'in and other sources elaborates on these points.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayḍ): Blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood, with a minimum duration of three days.
الاستحاضة (al-istiḥāḍah): Chronic bleeding from a vein, not from the womb, that does not follow the pattern of hayd. It is distinguished from hayd by its source and does not prohibit acts like prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi definition in the passage, which of the following is NOT a condition for blood to be considered hayd?
A) The blood must come from the womb.
B) The woman must be free from disease.
C) The blood must exit to the external vulva.
D) The woman must be at least 12 years old.

Key Takeaway
Hayd is blood from the womb of a healthy adult woman that exits to the external vulva; if any condition is missing, it is not hayd.

Minimum Duration of Hayd: Three Days and the Intra-Hanafi Ikhtilaf
Discussion of minimum duration of hayd and intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the minimum duration of hayd and explain the difference between Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf.

Core Idea
The minimum hayd is three days and three nights; Abu Yusuf allows two days plus most of the third.

This lesson focuses on the minimum duration of hayd as stated in the text: 'Its minimum is three days.' We examine whether nights are included, and the intra-Hanafi difference where Abu Yusuf holds that two days plus the majority of the third suffices. Understanding this affects whether short bleeding episodes count as hayd.

Guided Path
1
Identify the statement of minimum
The text says 'وأقله ثلاثة أيام' (its minimum is three days). Note that it does not explicitly mention nights.
The author either relied on the apparent madhhab that days include nights, or preferred Abu Yusuf's interpretation that only days matter.
2
Understand the inclusion of nights
The commentator explains that mentioning 'days' in plural includes the corresponding nights, so the madhhab holds three full days and three nights.
This is the position of Abu Hanifa.
3
Explain Abu Yusuf's view
Abu Yusuf says the minimum is two days and the majority of the third day, because the majority has the ruling of the whole (الكثرة كالكل).
Under his view, if blood starts at dawn on day 1 and stops at sunset on day 3, it is hayd even if the third day is not complete.
4
Identify the practical consequence
If a woman sees blood for two full days and then only a few hours on the third, according to Abu Hanifa it is not complete hayd; according to Abu Yusuf it is.
The fatwa follows Abu Hanifa's view.

باب الحيض أي بيان أحكامه س ف ك هو دم ينفضه رحم امرأة سليمة عن داء وصغر، وأقله ثلاثة أيام . وعن وسببه ابتلاء كما الله هو منبت الولد في البطن باب الحيض: مناسبة إيراد هذا الباب عقب الأبواب المتقدمة أنه ذكر هناك حكم الطهارة بعد انقطاع الحيض والنفاس، ولم يذكر حكم امتدادهما وحقيقتهما، فبين في هذا الباب حكم الامتداد والحقيقة، وإنما لقب الباب بالحيض دون النفاس مع أن الباب مشتمل عليهما؛ لأنه أكثر وقوعاً من النفاس، والمصنف ذكر ضمير الحيض في تعريفه مذكراً مع أنه مؤنث سماعي؛ لأن استعمال التذكير فيه أكثر. (فتح، مسكين) دم ينفضه: هذا تعريف مبني على القول بأنه من الأنجاس وعلى القول بأنه من الأحداث فمانعيته شرعية بسبب الدم المذكور عما اشترط فيها الطهارة وعن الصوم والمسجد والقربان ويقال له نفاس وطمث بالمثلثة وبالمثناة، وبالسين المهملة ومعنى قوله ينفضه، أي يسقط إلى الفرج الخارج، وإن كان النفض في الأصل تحريك الشيء، ليسقط ما عليه من غبار، ففي كلام المصنف تسامح، فلو نزل الدم إلى الفرج الداخل لم يكن حيضاً في ظاهر الرواية، محمد أنه حيض، وكذا النفاس، وبالأول يفتى ولا تثبت الاستحاضة إلا بالنزول إلى الخارج بلا خلاف. لحواء عليها السلام حين تناولت من شجرة الخلد وبقي هو في بناتها إلى يوم التناد بذلك السبب، روت عائشة قالت : قال النبي في الحيض: "هذا شيء كتبه الله على بنات آدم". (فتح المعين) رحم امرأة خرج به دم الرعاف ودم الجراحات ودم الاستحاضة؛ لأنه دم عرق كما في الحديث، فلم يكن خارجاً من الرحم، وخرج أيضاً ما يخرج من دبر ،المرأة، وإن ندب إمساك زوجها واغتسالها منه، وبقيد "امرأة" خرج ما تراه الصغيرة وما يخرج من غير الآدمية كالأرنب والضبع والخفاش ولا يحيض غيرها من الحيوانات. (فتح المعين) عن داء: أي عن داء الولادة، خرج به دم النفاس، فإن النفساء في حكم المريضة حتى اعتبرت تبرعاتها . وخرج به أيضاً دم يخرج من جراحة أو دمل في الرحم. رمز الحقائق بتغير يسير: ٣١/١] وصغر العامل فيه محذوف، أي خالية عن الصغر، كما في علقتها تبنا وماء بارداً"، أي وسقيت، وهذا القيد مستدرك للاستغناء عنه بذكر المرأة؛ لأن المرأة اسم البالغة كالرجل اسم البالغ كذا في "المغرب"، وقال العيني: إن ما تراه الصغيرة استحاضة وليس بدم ،رحم، فخرج بالقيد الأول. (فتح) وأقله ثلاثة أيام لم يتعرض لذكر ليال إما اكتفاء بظاهر المذهب أن أقله ثلاثة أيام وثلاث ليال؛ لأن ذكر الأيام بلفظ الجمع يتناول ما يقابلها من الليالي، أو اختياراً لما روي عن أبي يوسف أن الشرط ليال تقع في هذه الأيام لا ثلاث ليال حتى لو رأت الدم عند طلوع الفجر يوم السبت وانقطع عند غروب الشمس يوم الاثنين يكون حيضاً، من الثلث وقال أبو يوسف أقله يومان وأكثر اليوم الثالث؛ لأن للأكثر حكم الكل، وقال الشافعي وأحمد أقله مقدر :
Chapter of Hayd (Menstruation): i.e., explanation of its rulings. [Abbreviations: س ف ك]. It is blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood. Its minimum is three days. And its cause is a trial from Allah. The womb is the origin of the child in the belly. Chapter of Hayd: The appropriateness of placing this chapter after the preceding chapters: because there the ruling of purification after the cessation of hayd and nifas was mentioned, but the ruling of their duration and reality was not mentioned, so in this chapter the ruling of duration and reality is explained. The chapter is named hayd and not nifas even though the chapter includes both, because hayd occurs more frequently than nifas. The author used the masculine pronoun for hayd in its definition even though it is a feminine noun by convention, because masculine usage is more common. (Fath, Miskin) Blood discharged: This definition is based on the view that it is from the impurities (najasat), and on the view that it is from the events (ahdath), so its prohibition is legal due to the mentioned blood from what requires purity, and from fasting, mosque, and sacrifice. It is also called nifas and tamth. The meaning of 'yandafuhu' (discharges) is that it falls to the external vulva, even though nafd originally means to shake something to remove dust, so the author's usage is loose. If the blood descends to the internal vulva, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah); Muhammad says it is hayd. Similarly for nifas. And the first view is given fatwa. Istihadah is only confirmed by descent to the external without disagreement. Hawwa (Eve) when she ate from the tree of immortality, and it remained in her daughters until the Day of Calling for that reason. Aisha narrated that the Prophet said regarding hayd: 'This is something that Allah wrote upon the daughters of Adam.' (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Womb of a woman' excludes the blood of nosebleed, wounds, and istihadah, because that is blood from a vein as in the hadith, so it is not from the womb. It also excludes what exits from the anus of a woman, even if her husband is encouraged to refrain and she performs ghusl. By the restriction 'woman' it excludes what a minor girl sees and what exits from non-human animals like rabbits, hyenas, bats; other animals do not menstruate. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Free from disease': i.e., free from the disease of childbirth, which excludes the blood of nifas, because the woman in nifas is considered ill such that her gifts are considered. Also excludes blood from a wound or boil in the womb. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq with slight change: 31/1) 'And childhood': the operative word is omitted, i.e., free from childhood, as in 'she fed it straw and cold water', i.e., and watered it. This restriction is redundant because mentioning 'woman' suffices, as woman is a term for a mature female just as man is a term for a mature male, as in al-Mughrib. Al-Ayni said: What a minor girl sees is istihadah and is not blood of the womb, so it is excluded by the first restriction. (Fath) 'Its minimum is three days': It did not mention nights, either because it relies on the apparent madhhab that its minimum is three days and three nights, since mentioning 'days' in plural includes their corresponding nights, or by choice according to what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the condition is nights that fall within these days, not three nights, such that if she sees blood at the break of dawn on Saturday and it stops at sunset on Monday, it is hayd. From the third. And Abu Yusuf said: Its minimum is two days and the majority of the third day, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. And al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said: Its minimum is a set amount [cut off].
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage opens the chapter on hayd (menstruation). The author first explains why this chapter is placed after the preceding ones: because earlier the rulings of purification after hayd and nifas were mentioned, but not their duration and reality. This chapter addresses that. The chapter is named 'hayd' even though it includes nifas, because hayd is more common. The definiens is 'blood discharged by the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood.' The word 'yandafuhu' means to fall to the external vulva; if the blood only reaches the internal vulva, it is not hayd in the apparent narration (zahir al-riwayah), but Muhammad says it is. The definition excludes blood from nosebleeds, wounds, istihadah (chronic bleeding), and blood from a minor girl or animals. The minimum duration is three days according to Abu Hanifa. The text notes that he did not mention nights, likely because the plural 'days' includes the intervening nights as per the apparent madhhab. However, a narration from Abu Yusuf states that it is three days but the nights are not required to be full; for example, if blood starts at dawn Saturday and stops at sunset Monday, that counts as three days. Abu Yusuf's own view is that the minimum is two days and the majority of the third day. The passage also mentions the views of al-Shafi'i and Ahmad, but the text cuts off before stating their exact opinion. The hadith from Aisha is quoted to show that hayd is a divine decree for women. The commentary from Fath al-Mu'in and other sources elaborates on these points.

Key Terms
أقل الحيض (aqall al-hayḍ): The minimum duration of menstruation: three full days and three nights according to the Hanafi madhhab.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (operative ruling) in the Hanafi school, what is the minimum duration of hayd?
A) Two days and the majority of the third day
B) Three full days without regard to nights
C) Three full days and three nights
D) Two full days and two nights

Key Takeaway
The minimum hayd is three full days and nights; any bleeding less than that is istihadah.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Definition and Duration of Hayd
Definition of hayd, minimum and maximum duration, and related scholarly disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of hayd, identify the minimum (3 days) and maximum (10 days) durations, and explain the intra-Hanafi and inter-madhhab differences regarding the minimum duration.

Core Idea
Hayd is blood from the womb of an adult woman, lasting at least 3 days and at most 10 days according to the relied-upon Hanafi position.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq defines hayd and its temporal boundaries. It is essential for distinguishing hayd from istihadah (irregular bleeding) and nifas (post-childbirth bleeding). The minimum and maximum durations are based on prophetic hadith, though there are scholarly differences within and outside the Hanafi school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal definition of hayd
Observe the elements: blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease and childhood. Note the exclusion of istihadah, wound blood, and blood from minors or animals. Also note the condition of external exit.
The definition includes both positive elements and exclusions.
2
Trace the proofs for the minimum and maximum durations
The minimum of three days is based on the hadith of Ali (though weak, strengthened by multiple chains). The maximum of ten days is based on the later view of Abu Hanifa. The hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh is used by Shafi'is for a one-day minimum.
Understand the distinction between thubut (transmission) and dalala (meaning) of the hadith.
3
Analyze the intra-Hanafi disagreements
Abu Yusuf held that two days and most of the third suffice. Muhammad considered blood reaching the internal vagina as hayd. The relied-upon position follows Abu Hanifa's later view: three full days and ten maximum.
Intra-madhhab differences are resolved by later authorities like al-Marghinani.
4
Compare the Hanafi position with other schools
Shafi'i/Hanbali: minimum one day; Maliki: no minimum; all except Hanafi have fifteen days maximum. The differing proofs and their interpretations are critical.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) affects women's acts of worship.
5
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a woman who sees blood for 2 days and then it stops; according to the mufta bihi, it is istihadah, not hayd. She should pray and fast, and perform wudu for each prayer after washing.
This is the practical outcome of understanding the minimum duration.

بيوم وليلة؛ لقوله عليها لفاطمة بنت أبي حبيش دم الحيض أسود يعرف، فإذا كان فأمسكي الصلاة، قال النووي: وهذه الصفة موجودة في اليوم والليلة ولنا قوله علي: "أقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام وأكثره عشرة أيام"، والحديث وإن كان ضعيفاً لكن تعددت طرقه، وذلك يرفع الحديث إلى الحسن، والمقدرات الشرعية ما لا تدرك بالرأي، وذهب مالك إلى أن أقله بقدر ما يوجد ولو ساعة؛ لأنه نوع حدث فلا يقدر أقله بشيء كسائر الأحداث والحجة عليه ما مر من الحديث. (فتح المعين) وأكثره عشرة: هذا قول أبي حنيفة آخراً، وقال أولا: خمسة عشر كمذهب الشافعي ومالك، لهما: ما روي عنه عالية "تمكث إحداكن شطرها لا تصلي"، ولنا قوله علية وأكثره عشرة، والجواب عن حديثه أنه قال ابن الجوزي: هذا حديث لا يعرف وقال النووي: حديث باطل وعلى تسليم الصحة، فيقال: ليس المراد بالشطر حقيقة، بل ما يقارب الشطر ؛ لأن في عمرها زمان الصغر، ومدة الحبل ،والإياس ولا تحيض في شيء من (فتح المعين سوى البياض: هو شيء كالخيط الأبيض يخرج بعد انقطاع الدم. (مسكين) حيض: ألوان الدم ستة: السواد والحمرة والصفرة والخضرة والكدرة والتربية المنسوب إلى التراب، فهذه الألوان كلها حيض إلا البياض الصافي؛ لما روي أن النساء كن يبعثن إلى عائشة لحجمها الخرقة أو القطنة فيها الكرسف فيه الصفرة من دم الحيض يسألنها عن الصلاة، فتقول لهن: "لا تعجلن حتى ترين القصة البيضاء يعني الجصة"، شبهت الرطوبة الصافية بعد الحيض بالجص، تريد بذلك الطهر من الحيض.
