The Book of Purification. 41. Definition of Hayd and its Duration. Chapter of Hayd: i.e., explanation of its rulings. So F K. It is blood discharged from the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood, and its minimum is three days. And about... Its cause is trial. As Allah. It is the growth place of the child in the womb. Chapter of Hayd: The appropriateness of introducing this chapter after the previous chapters is that there he mentioned the ruling of purification after the cessation of hayd and nifas, and he did not mention the ruling of their duration and reality, so in this chapter he explains the ruling of duration and reality. He only named the chapter Hayd without Nifas, although the chapter includes both, because it occurs more often than Nifas. The author mentioned the pronoun of Hayd in its definition as masculine, although it is feminine by hearing, because using the masculine is more common. (Fath, Miskin) Blood discharged: This definition is based on the statement that it is from impurity (anjas), and on the statement that it is from events (ahdath), so its preventative nature is legal due to the mentioned blood regarding what requires purification, and regarding fasting, mosque, and sacrifice. It is called nifas and tamth with the thā' and tā', and with the sīn. The meaning of his saying 'discharged' is that it falls to the external vulva, although originally 'nadd' means moving something to make the dust fall from it. In the author's speech there is laxity. If the blood descends to the internal vagina, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration; Muhammad says it is hayd, similarly nifas. The first is given fatwa, and istihadah is not established except by descending to the exterior without dispute. For Hawwa', peace be upon her, when she ate from the tree of eternity, and it remained in her daughters until the Day of Proclamation for that reason. Aisha narrated: The Prophet said about hayd: 'This is something Allah wrote upon the daughters of Adam.' (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Womb of a woman' excludes blood of nosebleed, wound blood, and istihadah blood because it is vein blood as in the hadith, so it is not from the womb. It also excludes what comes out of the woman's anus, even if her husband is recommended to withhold and she performs ghusl from it. By the restriction 'woman' it excludes what a minor girl sees and what comes from non-human animals like rabbits, hyenas, bats; none other than humans menstruate. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Free from disease' i.e., free from the disease of childbirth; it excludes the blood of nifas, for the woman in nifas is in the ruling of a patient such that her gifts are considered. It also excludes blood from a wound or boil in the womb. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq with slight change: 31/1) 'And childhood' its operator is omitted, i.e., free from childhood, as in 'she fed it hay and cold water', i.e., she watered. This restriction is extra, as it is dispensed with by mentioning 'woman' because 'woman' is the name for a female adult just as 'man' is for a male adult, as in al-Mughrib. Al-Ayni said: What a minor sees is istihadah, not womb blood, so it is excluded by the first restriction. (Fath) 'And its minimum is three days' he did not mention nights either because he relied on the apparent madhhab that its minimum is three days and three nights, since mentioning days in the plural includes their corresponding nights, or as a choice for what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the condition is nights that fall within these days, not three nights, such that if she sees blood at dawn on Saturday and it stops at sunset on Monday, it is hayd. From the third, and Abu Yusuf said its minimum is two days and most of the third, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said its minimum is estimated by a day and night, because of his saying to Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh: 'The blood of hayd is black, known; if it is that, then withhold prayer.' Al-Nawawi said: This description exists in a day and night. For us is his saying, 'The minimum of hayd is three days and its maximum is ten days.' The hadith, though weak, has multiple chains, which raises it to hasan. Legal estimations are not reached by opinion. Malik went to that its minimum is whatever exists, even an hour, because it is a type of event, so its minimum is not estimated like other events, and the proof against him is the hadith mentioned. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'And its maximum is ten': This is the later statement of Abu Hanifa. He first said fifteen, like the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and Malik. For them: what is narrated from 'Aliya: 'One of you stays half of it not praying.' For us is his saying 'and its maximum is ten.' The answer to his hadith is that Ibn al-Jawzi said: This hadith is not known, and al-Nawawi said: It is a false hadith. Even if accepted, it is said: The intended meaning of 'half' is not literally, but approximately, because in her life there is the time of childhood, the period of pregnancy, and menopause, and she does not menstruate in any of these. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Other than pure white': It is something like a white thread that emerges after the cessation of blood. (Miskin) 'Hayd': The colors of blood are six: black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy (attributed to dirt). All these colors are hayd except pure white; because it is narrated that women used to send to Aisha, according to her size, a cloth or cotton with a piece containing yellowness from menstrual blood, asking her about prayer. She would say to them: 'Do not hasten until you see the white discharge, meaning the gypsum.' She compared the clear moisture after hayd to gypsum, intending by that purity from hayd. (Fath, Miskin) 'It prevents prayer and fasting': i.e., their validity. Prayer, due to its indefinite form, also includes funeral prayer, and there is no doubt that prevention from a thing prevents its parts, hence she is prevented from prostration of recitation and prostration of thanks. (Fath) 'And she makes up for it but not the other': i.e., the menstruating woman makes up the fast after the cessation of hayd, and she does not make up the prayer; because of what is narrated from Mu'adha al-Adawiyya who said: 'I asked Aisha: Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast but not the prayer? She said: Are you a Haruriyya? I said: I am not a Haruriyya but I am asking. She said: That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.' And because in making up the prayer there is hardship due to its repetition every day and the repetition of hayd every month, unlike fasting, whose making up is not a hardship. Nifas is attached to hayd, so hardship attaches to her in making it up. The correct view is that making up the fast is obligatory with ease (at one's leisure) according to the majority, and according to Abu Bakr al-Razi, it is obligatory immediately. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling with proofs covering the definition, duration, colors, and prohibitions of hayd (menstruation). The source text is the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary from Fath al-Qadir and al-Miskin.

It begins by defining hayd as blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease (like nifas) and childhood. The blood must exit the external vagina; if it only reaches the internal vagina, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration, though Muhammad ibn al-Hasan considered it hayd. The definition excludes istihadah (irregular uterine bleeding), blood from wounds, and blood from minors or animals.

The minimum duration of hayd is three days and three nights, based on a hadith (though weak) from Ali. Abu Yusuf held two days and most of the third, while al-Shafi'i and Ahmad considered one day and night as minimum, citing a hadith where the Prophet describes hayd blood as black. The Hanafi response is that the black blood description is for distinguishing hayd from istihadah, not for setting a minimum duration. Malik set no minimum.

The maximum duration is ten days, according to Abu Hanifa's later view (he earlier held fifteen). Al-Shafi'i and Malik held fifteen days. The proof for ten is the hadith 'Aqallu al-haydi thalathatu ayyam wa aktharuhu 'asharah' (the minimum of hayd is three and the maximum ten). The opposing hadith about a woman staying half her life not praying is rejected as weak or misinterpreted.

All colors of blood during hayd—black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy—are considered hayd except pure white discharge, which indicates purity. This is based on the practice of women sending to Aisha to check for the white discharge before resuming prayer.

During hayd, prayer (including funeral prayer and prostrations) and fasting are prohibited. The fast must be made up later, but not the prayer. This ruling is based on Aisha's response to Mu'adha, stating that was the practice. The reason is that making up repeated prayers would cause excessive hardship due to frequent menstruation, whereas fasting is less burdensome. The make-up of fasts is to be done at ease (not immediately), according to the majority, though Abu Bakr al-Razi held it must be done immediately.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease and childhood, with minimum 3 days.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular uterine bleeding not meeting the criteria of hayd; it is from a vein, not the womb.
النفاس (al-nifas): Blood discharged after childbirth, treated similarly to hayd in many rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the maximum duration of hayd?
A) 10 days
B) 15 days
C) 7 days
D) indefinite

Key Takeaway
Hayd is defined by specific temporal and physical criteria; the Hanafi minimum is 3 days and maximum 10 days, and these parameters must be strictly applied in distinguishing hayd from istihadah.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
The Colors of Menstrual Blood
Colours of menstrual blood and the exception of pure white.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the six colors that constitute hayd and identify the exception of pure white discharge, and apply this to determine when a woman is pure.

Core Idea
All colors of discharge—black, red, yellow, green, muddy, earthy—are hayd except pure white, which indicates purity.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses a common confusion: what color counts as menstrual blood? Based on the practice of the Companions including Aisha, the ruling is that any color other than pure white is hayd. This has practical implications for when a woman may resume prayer and other acts.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling on colors
The passage clearly states: 'All colors except pure white are hayd.' This includes black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy.
There is no gradation; any non-white color is considered menstrual blood.
2
Understand the exception of pure white
Pure white discharge (qassah bayda') is the sign of purity (tuhr). It resembles a white thread and indicates that hayd has ended.
Women should wait until they see this before performing ghusl and resuming prayers.
3
Trace the proof from the practice of the Companions
Women used to send cloth with yellow discharge to Aisha, asking if they were pure. She told them not to hasten until they see the white discharge. This shows that yellow, even though not red or black, is still hayd.
This is a qawl al-Sahabi (statement of a companion) accepted as proof in the Hanafi school.
4
Apply the ruling to common scenarios
A woman who sees brownish or yellowish spotting within the 10-day period must still consider herself in hayd until she sees pure white or the maximum duration elapsed.
The color is decisive, not the consistency or smell.

باب الحيض: مناسبة إيراد هذا الباب عقب الأبواب المتقدمة أنه ذكر هناك حكم الطهارة بعد انقطاع الحيض والنفاس، ولم يذكر حكم امتدادهما وحقيقتهما، فبين في هذا الباب حكم الامتداد والحقيقة، وإنما لقب الباب بالحيض دون النفاس مع أن الباب مشتمل عليهما؛ لأنه أكثر وقوعاً من النفاس، والمصنف ذكر ضمير الحيض في تعريفه مذكراً مع أنه مؤنث سماعي؛ لأن استعمال التذكير فيه أكثر. بيوم وليلة؛ لقوله عليها لفاطمة بنت أبي حبيش دم الحيض أسود يعرف، فإذا كان فأمسكي الصلاة، قال النووي: وهذه الصفة موجودة في اليوم والليلة ولنا قوله علي: "أقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام وأكثره عشرة أيام"، والحديث وإن كان ضعيفاً لكن تعددت طرقه، وذلك يرفع الحديث إلى الحسن، والمقدرات الشرعية ما لا تدرك بالرأي، وذهب مالك إلى أن أقله بقدر ما يوجد ولو ساعة؛ لأنه نوع حدث فلا يقدر أقله بشيء كسائر الأحداث والحجة عليه ما مر من الحديث. The Book of Purification. 41. Definition of Hayd and its Duration. Chapter of Hayd: i.e., explanation of its rulings. So F K. It is blood discharged from the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood, and its minimum is three days. And about... Its cause is trial. As Allah. It is the growth place of the child in the womb. Chapter of Hayd: The appropriateness of introducing this chapter after the previous chapters is that there he mentioned the ruling of purification after the cessation of hayd and nifas, and he did not mention the ruling of their duration and reality, so in this chapter he explains the ruling of duration and reality. He only named the chapter Hayd without Nifas, although the chapter includes both, because it occurs more often than Nifas. The author mentioned the pronoun of Hayd in its definition as masculine, although it is feminine by hearing, because using the masculine is more common. (Fath, Miskin) Blood discharged: This definition is based on the statement that it is from impurity (anjas), and on the statement that it is from events (ahdath), so its preventative nature is legal due to the mentioned blood regarding what requires purification, and regarding fasting, mosque, and sacrifice. It is called nifas and tamth with the thā' and tā', and with the sīn. The meaning of his saying 'discharged' is that it falls to the external vulva, although originally 'nadd' means moving something to make the dust fall from it. In the author's speech there is laxity. If the blood descends to the internal vagina, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration; Muhammad says it is hayd, similarly nifas. The first is given fatwa, and istihadah is not established except by descending to the exterior without dispute. For Hawwa', peace be upon her, when she ate from the tree of eternity, and it remained in her daughters until the Day of Proclamation for that reason. Aisha narrated: The Prophet said about hayd: 'This is something Allah wrote upon the daughters of Adam.' (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Womb of a woman' excludes blood of nosebleed, wound blood, and istihadah blood because it is vein blood as in the hadith, so it is not from the womb. It also excludes what comes out of the woman's anus, even if her husband is recommended to withhold and she performs ghusl from it. By the restriction 'woman' it excludes what a minor girl sees and what comes from non-human animals like rabbits, hyenas, bats; none other than humans menstruate. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Free from disease' i.e., free from the disease of childbirth; it excludes the blood of nifas, for the woman in nifas is in the ruling of a patient such that her gifts are considered. It also excludes blood from a wound or boil in the womb. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq with slight change: 31/1) 'And childhood' its operator is omitted, i.e., free from childhood, as in 'she fed it hay and cold water', i.e., she watered. This restriction is extra, as it is dispensed with by mentioning 'woman' because 'woman' is the name for a female adult just as 'man' is for a male adult, as in al-Mughrib. Al-Ayni said: What a minor sees is istihadah, not womb blood, so it is excluded by the first restriction. (Fath) 'And its minimum is three days' he did not mention nights either because he relied on the apparent madhhab that its minimum is three days and three nights, since mentioning days in the plural includes their corresponding nights, or as a choice for what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the condition is nights that fall within these days, not three nights, such that if she sees blood at dawn on Saturday and it stops at sunset on Monday, it is hayd. From the third, and Abu Yusuf said its minimum is two days and most of the third, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said its minimum is estimated by a day and night, because of his saying to Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh: 'The blood of hayd is black, known; if it is that, then withhold prayer.' Al-Nawawi said: This description exists in a day and night. For us is his saying, 'The minimum of hayd is three days and its maximum is ten days.' The hadith, though weak, has multiple chains, which raises it to hasan. Legal estimations are not reached by opinion. Malik went to that its minimum is whatever exists, even an hour, because it is a type of event, so its minimum is not estimated like other events, and the proof against him is the hadith mentioned. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'And its maximum is ten': This is the later statement of Abu Hanifa. He first said fifteen, like the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and Malik. For them: what is narrated from 'Aliya: 'One of you stays half of it not praying.' For us is his saying 'and its maximum is ten.' The answer to his hadith is that Ibn al-Jawzi said: This hadith is not known, and al-Nawawi said: It is a false hadith. Even if accepted, it is said: The intended meaning of 'half' is not literally, but approximately, because in her life there is the time of childhood, the period of pregnancy, and menopause, and she does not menstruate in any of these. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Other than pure white': It is something like a white thread that emerges after the cessation of blood. (Miskin) 'Hayd': The colors of blood are six: black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy (attributed to dirt). All these colors are hayd except pure white; because it is narrated that women used to send to Aisha, according to her size, a cloth or cotton with a piece containing yellowness from menstrual blood, asking her about prayer. She would say to them: 'Do not hasten until you see the white discharge, meaning the gypsum.' She compared the clear moisture after hayd to gypsum, intending by that purity from hayd. (Fath, Miskin) 'It prevents prayer and fasting': i.e., their validity. Prayer, due to its indefinite form, also includes funeral prayer, and there is no doubt that prevention from a thing prevents its parts, hence she is prevented from prostration of recitation and prostration of thanks. (Fath) 'And she makes up for it but not the other': i.e., the menstruating woman makes up the fast after the cessation of hayd, and she does not make up the prayer; because of what is narrated from Mu'adha al-Adawiyya who said: 'I asked Aisha: Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast but not the prayer? She said: Are you a Haruriyya? I said: I am not a Haruriyya but I am asking. She said: That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.' And because in making up the prayer there is hardship due to its repetition every day and the repetition of hayd every month, unlike fasting, whose making up is not a hardship. Nifas is attached to hayd, so hardship attaches to her in making it up. The correct view is that making up the fast is obligatory with ease (at one's leisure) according to the majority, and according to Abu Bakr al-Razi, it is obligatory immediately. (Fath, Miskin)

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling with proofs covering the definition, duration, colors, and prohibitions of hayd (menstruation). The source text is the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary from Fath al-Qadir and al-Miskin.

The proof for ten is the hadith 'Aqallu al-haydi thalathatu ayyam wa aktharuhu 'asharah' (the minimum of hayd is three and the maximum ten). The opposing hadith about a woman staying half her life not praying is rejected as weak or misinterpreted.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease and childhood, with minimum 3 days.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular uterine bleeding not meeting the criteria of hayd; it is from a vein, not the womb.
النفاس (al-nifas): Blood discharged after childbirth, treated similarly to hayd in many rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) Black
B) Red
C) Yellow
D) Pure white

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, all colors of bleeding from the uterus during the menstrual period are hayd, and only pure white discharge signals purity.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
5 min
Prohibitions and Make-up of Ibadat During Hayd
Prohibition of prayer and fasting during hayd, and the obligation to make up fasting only.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state which acts are prohibited during hayd (prayer, fasting, and their parts) and which must be made up (fasting only), and explain the rationale based on the hadith of Aisha.

Core Idea
Prayer and fasting are prohibited during hayd; only fasting must be made up, not prayer, because of the hardship it would cause.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq addresses the practical implications of being in a state of hayd: a woman must avoid prayer (including funeral prayer and prostrations) and fasting. However, she is only required to make up the fasts, not the prayers, based on the practice during the Prophet's time as reported by Aisha.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts prohibited
The passage states that hayd prevents both prayer and fasting. Prayer includes funeral prayer and prostration of recitation and thanks.
Prohibition means the acts are not valid if performed.
2
Identify the make-up requirement
The passage then specifies that the fasts must be made up, but not the prayers. This is a concession from hardship.
Only obligatory fasts (like Ramadan) need to be made up; voluntary fasts are not required to be made up.
3
Trace the proof
The proof is the hadith of Mu'adha quoting Aisha: 'We were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.'
This is a clear textual evidence for the ruling.
4
Understand the wisdom
The hardship of making up many prayers due to frequent menstruation is cited. Fasting is less burdensome because it occurs only once a year.
This wisdom helps explain the ruling but is not the cause; the ruling is based on divine command.
5
Note the timing of make-up
The make-up of fasts is to be done at ease (ala al-tarakhi) according to the majority, not necessarily immediately.
Abu Bakr al-Razi held it must be done immediately, but the mufta bihi is that it can be delayed within the year before the next Ramadan.

The Book of Purification. 41. Definition of Hayd and its Duration. Chapter of Hayd: i.e., explanation of its rulings. So F K. It is blood discharged from the womb of a woman free from disease and childhood, and its minimum is three days. And about... Its cause is trial. As Allah. It is the growth place of the child in the womb. Chapter of Hayd: The appropriateness of introducing this chapter after the previous chapters is that there he mentioned the ruling of purification after the cessation of hayd and nifas, and he did not mention the ruling of their duration and reality, so in this chapter he explains the ruling of duration and reality. He only named the chapter Hayd without Nifas, although the chapter includes both, because it occurs more often than Nifas. The author mentioned the pronoun of Hayd in its definition as masculine, although it is feminine by hearing, because using the masculine is more common. (Fath, Miskin) Blood discharged: This definition is based on the statement that it is from impurity (anjas), and on the statement that it is from events (ahdath), so its preventative nature is legal due to the mentioned blood regarding what requires purification, and regarding fasting, mosque, and sacrifice. It is called nifas and tamth with the thā' and tā', and with the sīn. The meaning of his saying 'discharged' is that it falls to the external vulva, although originally 'nadd' means moving something to make the dust fall from it. In the author's speech there is laxity. If the blood descends to the internal vagina, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration; Muhammad says it is hayd, similarly nifas. The first is given fatwa, and istihadah is not established except by descending to the exterior without dispute. For Hawwa', peace be upon her, when she ate from the tree of eternity, and it remained in her daughters until the Day of Proclamation for that reason. Aisha narrated: The Prophet said about hayd: 'This is something Allah wrote upon the daughters of Adam.' (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Womb of a woman' excludes blood of nosebleed, wound blood, and istihadah blood because it is vein blood as in the hadith, so it is not from the womb. It also excludes what comes out of the woman's anus, even if her husband is recommended to withhold and she performs ghusl from it. By the restriction 'woman' it excludes what a minor girl sees and what comes from non-human animals like rabbits, hyenas, bats; none other than humans menstruate. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Free from disease' i.e., free from the disease of childbirth; it excludes the blood of nifas, for the woman in nifas is in the ruling of a patient such that her gifts are considered. It also excludes blood from a wound or boil in the womb. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq with slight change: 31/1) 'And childhood' its operator is omitted, i.e., free from childhood, as in 'she fed it hay and cold water', i.e., she watered. This restriction is extra, as it is dispensed with by mentioning 'woman' because 'woman' is the name for a female adult just as 'man' is for a male adult, as in al-Mughrib. Al-Ayni said: What a minor sees is istihadah, not womb blood, so it is excluded by the first restriction. (Fath) 'And its minimum is three days' he did not mention nights either because he relied on the apparent madhhab that its minimum is three days and three nights, since mentioning days in the plural includes their corresponding nights, or as a choice for what is narrated from Abu Yusuf that the condition is nights that fall within these days, not three nights, such that if she sees blood at dawn on Saturday and it stops at sunset on Monday, it is hayd. From the third, and Abu Yusuf said its minimum is two days and most of the third, because the majority has the ruling of the whole. Al-Shafi'i and Ahmad said its minimum is estimated by a day and night, because of his saying to Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh: 'The blood of hayd is black, known; if it is that, then withhold prayer.' Al-Nawawi said: This description exists in a day and night. For us is his saying, 'The minimum of hayd is three days and its maximum is ten days.' The hadith, though weak, has multiple chains, which raises it to hasan. Legal estimations are not reached by opinion. Malik went to that its minimum is whatever exists, even an hour, because it is a type of event, so its minimum is not estimated like other events, and the proof against him is the hadith mentioned. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'And its maximum is ten': This is the later statement of Abu Hanifa. He first said fifteen, like the madhhab of al-Shafi'i and Malik. For them: what is narrated from 'Aliya: 'One of you stays half of it not praying.' For us is his saying 'and its maximum is ten.' The answer to his hadith is that Ibn al-Jawzi said: This hadith is not known, and al-Nawawi said: It is a false hadith. Even if accepted, it is said: The intended meaning of 'half' is not literally, but approximately, because in her life there is the time of childhood, the period of pregnancy, and menopause, and she does not menstruate in any of these. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'Other than pure white': It is something like a white thread that emerges after the cessation of blood. (Miskin) 'Hayd': The colors of blood are six: black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy (attributed to dirt). All these colors are hayd except pure white; because it is narrated that women used to send to Aisha, according to her size, a cloth or cotton with a piece containing yellowness from menstrual blood, asking her about prayer. She would say to them: 'Do not hasten until you see the white discharge, meaning the gypsum.' She compared the clear moisture after hayd to gypsum, intending by that purity from hayd. (Fath, Miskin) 'It prevents prayer and fasting': i.e., their validity. Prayer, due to its indefinite form, also includes funeral prayer, and there is no doubt that prevention from a thing prevents its parts, hence she is prevented from prostration of recitation and prostration of thanks. (Fath) 'And she makes up for it but not the other': i.e., the menstruating woman makes up the fast after the cessation of hayd, and she does not make up the prayer; because of what is narrated from Mu'adha al-Adawiyya who said: 'I asked Aisha: Why does the menstruating woman make up the fast but not the prayer? She said: Are you a Haruriyya? I said: I am not a Haruriyya but I am asking. She said: That used to happen to us, and we were commanded to make up the fast and not commanded to make up the prayer.' And because in making up the prayer there is hardship due to its repetition every day and the repetition of hayd every month, unlike fasting, whose making up is not a hardship. Nifas is attached to hayd, so hardship attaches to her in making it up. The correct view is that making up the fast is obligatory with ease (at one's leisure) according to the majority, and according to Abu Bakr al-Razi, it is obligatory immediately. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 42

Commentary
This passage is a comprehensive ruling with proofs covering the definition, duration, colors, and prohibitions of hayd (menstruation). The source text is the matn of Kanz al-Daqa'iq with commentary from Fath al-Qadir and al-Miskin.

It begins by defining hayd as blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease (like nifas) and childhood. The blood must exit the external vagina; if it only reaches the internal vagina, it is not hayd according to the apparent narration, though Muhammad ibn al-Hasan considered it hayd. The definition excludes istihadah (irregular uterine bleeding), blood from wounds, and blood from minors or animals.

The minimum duration of hayd is three days and three nights, based on a hadith (though weak) from Ali. Abu Yusuf held two days and most of the third, while al-Shafi'i and Ahmad considered one day and night as minimum, citing a hadith where the Prophet describes hayd blood as black. The Hanafi response is that the black blood description is for distinguishing hayd from istihadah, not for setting a minimum duration. Malik set no minimum.

The maximum duration is ten days, according to Abu Hanifa's later view (he earlier held fifteen). Al-Shafi'i and Malik held fifteen days. The proof for ten is the hadith 'Aqallu al-haydi thalathatu ayyam wa aktharuhu 'asharah' (the minimum of hayd is three and the maximum ten). The opposing hadith about a woman staying half her life not praying is rejected as weak or misinterpreted.

All colors of blood during hayd—black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy—are considered hayd except pure white discharge, which indicates purity. This is based on the practice of women sending to Aisha to check for the white discharge before resuming prayer.

During hayd, prayer (including funeral prayer and prostrations) and fasting are prohibited. The fast must be made up later, but not the prayer. This ruling is based on Aisha's response to Mu'adha, stating that was the practice. The reason is that making up repeated prayers would cause excessive hardship due to frequent menstruation, whereas fasting is less burdensome. The make-up of fasts is to be done at ease (not immediately), according to the majority, though Abu Bakr al-Razi held it must be done immediately.

Key Terms
الحيض (al-hayd): Blood discharged from the womb of an adult woman free from disease and childhood, with minimum 3 days.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular uterine bleeding not meeting the criteria of hayd; it is from a vein, not the womb.
النفاس (al-nifas): Blood discharged after childbirth, treated similarly to hayd in many rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the hadith of Aisha, how are women commanded regarding missed prayers and fasts due to hayd?
A) They must make up both.
B) They must make up the prayers but not the fasts.
C) They must make up the fasts but not the prayers.
D) They need not make up either.

Key Takeaway
Hayd prohibits prayer and fasting; only fasting must be made up, based on explicit prophetic practice.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Duration of Menstruation and Colors of Blood
Defines duration and colors of menstrual blood with proofs and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on the minimum and maximum duration of menstruation and identify which colors of discharge are considered menstrual blood.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, menstruation is defined by both duration (3–10 days) and color (anything except pure white).

This passage clarifies the boundaries of menstruation (hayd) and irregular bleeding (istihadah). The Hanafi school relies on Prophetic hadith to set a minimum of three days and a maximum of ten; any bleeding outside this range is not counted as hayd. Additionally, the color of the discharge matters: only pure white indicates purity; all other colors are considered menstrual blood. Understanding these rules is essential for determining a woman's ritual obligations.

Guided Path
1
Identify the duration rules
From the text, extract the minimum (3 days) and maximum (10 days) of hayd. Note that any bleeding less than 3 or more than 10 is istihadah (irregular bleeding).
The maximum of 10 days is Abu Hanifa's later view; he initially held 15 days.
2
Examine the proofs
The Hanafi proof for the minimum is the hadith 'The minimum of menstruation is three days' (strengthened by multiple chains). For the maximum, the same hadith states 'and its maximum is ten days.' The hadith of Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh about black blood is also cited.
The hadith is considered weak in transmission but elevated to hasan by multiple chains.
3
Study the inter-madhhab dispute
Imam Malik argued that any amount of blood, even an hour, is hayd by analogy (qiyas) with other forms of hadath. The Hanafi response: the hadith specifying three days takes precedence over analogy in worship matters.
The practical difference: in the Maliki school, a 2-day bleeding is hayd; in Hanafi, it is istihadah.
4
List the colors of menstrual blood
The text enumerates six colors: black, red, yellow, green, muddy (kudrah), and earthy (turbiyah). All are considered hayd except pure white discharge (qissah bayda).
This ruling is based on the practice of the Companions, transmitted by A'isha.
5
Identify the sign of purity
The passage describes the white discharge as a clear sign that menstruation has ended. Women are advised not to pray until they see this white discharge.
This sign is agreed upon by all schools; Hanafis emphasize it to distinguish hayd from istihadah.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ما يحرم على الحائض فعله وأكثره عشرة، وما نقص أو زاد استحاضة، وما سوى البياض الخالص حيض. لقوله عليها لفاطمة بنت أبي حبيش: "دم الحيض أسود يعرف، فإذا كان فأمسكي الصلاة". قال النووي: وهذه الصفة موجودة في اليوم والليلة. ولنا قوله عليه السلام: "أقل الحيض ثلاثة أيام وأكثره عشرة أيام". والحديث وإن كان ضعيفاً لكن تعددت طرقه، وذلك يرفع الحديث إلى الحسن. والمقدرات الشرعية ما لا تدرك بالرأي. وذهب مالك إلى أن أقله بقدر ما يوجد ولو ساعة؛ لأنه نوع حدث فلا يقدر أقله بشيء كسائر الأحداث. والحجة عليه ما مر من الحديث. (فتح المعين) وأكثره عشرة: هذا قول أبي حنيفة آخراً، وقال أولاً: خمسة عشر كمذهب الشافعي ومالك. لهما: ما روي عن عائشة "تمكث إحداكن شطرها لا تصلي". ولنا قوله عليه السلام: وأكثره عشرة. والجواب عن حديثه أنه قال ابن الجوزي: هذا حديث لا يعرف، وقال النووي: حديث باطل. وعلى تسليم الصحة، فيقال: ليس المراد بالشطر حقيقة، بل ما يقارب الشطر؛ لأن في عمرها زمان الصغر ومدة الحبل والإياس، ولا تحيض في شيء من ذلك. (فتح المعين) وسوى البياض: هو شيء كالخيط الأبيض يخرج بعد انقطاع الدم. (مسكين) حيض: ألوان الدم ستة: السواد والحمرة والصفرة والخضرة والكدرة والتربية، المنسوب إلى التراب. فهذه الألوان كلها حيض إلا البياض الصافي؛ لما روي أن النساء كن يبعثن إلى عائشة بحجم الخرقة أو القطنة فيها الكرسف فيه الصفرة من دم الحيض يسألنها عن الصلاة، فتقول لهن: "لا تعجلن حتى ترين القصة البيضاء" يعني الجصة. شبهت الرطوبة الصافية بعد الحيض بالجص، تريد بذلك الطهر من الحيض. (فتح، مسكين)
What is prohibited for the menstruating woman: And its maximum is ten, and what is less or more is istihadah, and what is other than pure white is menstruation. Due to his saying, peace be upon him, to Fatima bint Abi Hubaysh: 'The blood of menstruation is black, known, so when it is that, then refrain from prayer.' Al-Nawawi said: This description exists in the day and night. And for us is his saying, peace be upon him: 'The minimum of menstruation is three days and its maximum is ten days.' And the hadith, even if weak, its multiple chains elevate it to hasan. And the legal determinations are not reached by opinion. Malik held that its minimum is whatever exists, even an hour, because it is a type of hadath, so its minimum is not limited like other hadath. The proof against him is the hadith mentioned. (Fath al-Mu'in) And its maximum is ten: This is Abu Hanifa's later opinion; he initially said fifteen like Shafi'i and Malik. They have what is narrated from A'isha: 'One of you stays half of it not praying.' And we have his saying, peace be upon him: 'And its maximum is ten.' The response to their hadith: Ibn al-Jawzi said this hadith is unknown, and al-Nawawi said it is false. And assuming its authenticity, 'half' is not meant literally but approximately, because in her life there is the time of childhood, pregnancy, and menopause, and she does not menstruate in any of that. (Fath al-Mu'in) And besides whiteness: it is something like a white thread that comes out after the blood stops. (Miskin) Menstruation: The colors of blood are six: black, red, yellow, green, muddy, and earthy (attributed to dust). All these colors are menstruation except pure white; because it is narrated that women used to send to A'isha a piece of cloth or cotton with yellow from menstrual blood asking about prayer, and she would say to them: 'Do not be hasty until you see the white discharge' meaning gypsum. She compared the clear moisture after menstruation to gypsum, intending thereby purity from menstruation. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a ruling-with-proof discussing the duration of menstruation (hayd) and its distinction from non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah). The author states that the maximum duration of hayd is ten days; any bleeding less than three days or more than ten is considered istihadah (irregular bleeding). Only pure white discharge is not considered menstrual blood. The proof for the minimum of three days is a hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) narrated by multiple chains, which though individually weak, collectively reach the level of hasan. Imam Malik opposed this, arguing that any amount, even an hour, should be considered hayd by analogy with other forms of ritual impurity (hadath). The Hanafi response is that the hadith specifying three days takes precedence. Regarding the maximum, Abu Hanifa initially held it to be fifteen days (like Shafi'i and Malik), but later retracted to ten days. The proof for ten is the same hadith. The objection that a hadith from A'isha mentions 'half' (shatr) is refuted by noting the hadith's weakness and interpreting 'half' loosely to mean approximately half, considering periods of childhood, pregnancy, and menopause when menstruation does not occur. The passage then defines menstrual colors: any color except pure white—whether black, red, yellow, green, muddy, or earthy—is considered hayd. This is based on the practice of the Companions, as transmitted by A'isha, who advised women to wait until they see clear white discharge to confirm purity.

Key Terms
حيض (hayḍ): Menstrual blood that occurs within the minimum (3 days) and maximum (10 days) period.
استحاضة (istiḥāḍah): Irregular bleeding that falls short of 3 days or exceeds 10 days.
القصة البيضاء (al-qiṣṣah al-bayḍāʾ): The clear white discharge indicating the end of menstruation.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the minimum duration of menstruation in the Hanafi school?
A) One day and one night
B) Three days
C) Ten days
D) No minimum

Key Takeaway
Menstruation in Hanafi fiqh is defined by a minimum of 3 days, a maximum of 10, and any color except pure white.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
8 min
Prayer, Fasting, and Their Makeup During Menstruation
Rulings on prayer and fasting during menstruation with proof.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer and fasting during menstruation, explain why prayer is not made up while fasting is, and identify the dispute regarding the timing of making up fasts.

Core Idea
Prayer is invalid during menstruation and never made up; fasting is invalid but must be made up with delay.

One of the most distinctive rulings in female fiqh is that a menstruating woman does not make up missed prayers. This lesson unpacks the evidence and wisdom behind that, and clarifies the obligation to make up fasting, including the scholarly difference on whether it must be done immediately.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two core rulings
State that prayer is invalid and not made up; fasting is invalid but must be made up. Note that funeral prayer and prostrations are also included in the prohibition.
The prohibition of prayer includes its components (sujud al-tilawah, sujud al-shukr).
2
Examine the proof
Read the hadith of Aisha (ra) narrated by Mu'adhah al-Adawiyyah. Identify the explicit command to make up fasting and the absence of command for prayer.
The hadith is the primary textual evidence.
3
Understand the wisdom
The reason given in the text: making up prayers would cause hardship due to daily repetition, while making up fasts is only once a year (or spread out). Postpartum bleeding is analogous.
The 'hardship' (haraj) principle is a common ta'lil in Hanafi fiqh.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
The majority (including al-Marghinani) hold that making up fasts is obligatory on delay (ala al-tarakhi). Abu Bakr al-Razi held it is immediate. Identify the thamarah (practical difference).
The mufta bihi is the majority view.
5
Apply to common scenarios
If a woman misses five prayers and five fasts due to menstruation, she must make up only the fasts. She can make them up anytime before the next Ramadan.
Delay without excuse may incur fidyah in some views, but the basic obligation remains.

(فتح) وقال في "المستخلص" : يمنع الحيض دخول المسجد؛ لقوله عليها: "فإني لا أحل المسجد لحائض ولا لجنب"، وهو بإطلاقه حجة على الشافعي في إباحة الدخول على وجه العبور. والطواف أي يمنع حل الطواف لا صحته، وإنما ذكر الطواف مع أنه إذا منع عن دخول المسجد لا تتمكن الحائض من الطواف لأنه فيه؛ لئلا يتوهم أ أنه لما جاز لها الوقوف مع أنه أقوى أركان الحج فلأن يجوز لها الطواف أولى، أو يتوهم جواز دخول المسجد لضرورة الطواف، فأزال ذلك الوهم. عيني وغيره) وقربان: مجاز عن المباشرة . من إطلاق السبب وإرادة المسبب. (مسكين) مسته: أي يمنع مس سواء مس تمام القرآن أو سورة منه. إلا بغلاف: [هو الجلد المنفصل كالخريطة، ويكره مسه بالكم، وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. (مسكين)] والمراد الغلاف الذي لا يدخل في بيع المصحف إلا بشرط، وأما غلاف المشرز فلا يجوز مسه، وكذا لا يجوز المس بكمه؛ لأنه تبع له، أما كتب الشريعة فيجوز أخذها بالكم للضرورة، ولا بأس بدفع المصحف إلى الصبيان لحفظ القرآن (مستخلص) وقال في "الفتح": ولا بأس لجنب وحائض بزيارة القبور وأكل وشرب بعد المضمضة وغسل اليد، وأما قبلها فيكره.
It prevents prayer and fasting, and she makes up the latter but not the former. Prayer, due to its indefinite form, includes funeral prayer as well. There is no doubt that the prevention of something includes its parts, hence she is prevented from prostration of recitation and prostration of thanks. (Fath) And she makes it up without it: meaning the menstruating woman makes up fasting after menstruation ends, and she does not make up prayer; due to what is narrated from Mu'adhah al-'Adawiyyah: she said, 'I asked A'isha: Why does the menstruating woman make up fasting but not prayer?' She said, 'Are you a Haruriyyah?' I said, 'I am not a Haruriyyah, but I am asking.' She said, 'That used to happen to us, so we were commanded to make up fasting and were not commanded to make up prayer.' And because in making up prayer there is hardship due to its repetition every day and the repetition of menstruation every month, unlike fasting, for making it up is not a hardship. Postpartum bleeding is attached to menstruation, so hardship applies in its making up. The correct view is that making up fasting is obligatory with delay according to the majority, and according to Abu Bakr al-Razi: immediately. (Fath, Miskin). And entering the mosque, and circumambulation, and approaching what is under the waist-wrapper, and reciting the Quran, and touching it except with a cover. The prevention of hadath (minor impurity) prevents touching, meaning the smaller one, i.e., touching the Quran, not reciting it. Entering the mosque: absolutely, whether for passage or not. Al-Shafi'i permitted the menstruating woman to enter the mosque for passage. (Miskin) 'Mosque' means the customary place of worship, so it includes the Ka'bah but not the mosque of the house. It indicates that one with impurity on his body should not enter the mosque. In al-Khazanah: if someone passes wind in the mosque, some saw no harm, some said if needed he should exit, which is more correct. If one has a wet dream in the mosque, he should perform tayammum and exit if not afraid, and sit with tayammum if afraid, but he should not pray or recite. (Fath) And it is said in al-Mustakhlas: Menstruation prevents entering the mosque due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman nor for a junub.' This is an absolute proof against al-Shafi'i regarding permissibility of passing through. Circumambulation: meaning it prevents its validity, not its correctness. It is mentioned even though if prevented from entering the mosque she cannot perform tawaf because it is inside, lest one misunderstand that since she is permitted to stand (at Arafat) which is a stronger pillar, then she should be permitted to do tawaf, or misunderstand the permissibility of entering the mosque for necessity of tawaf. So that misunderstanding is removed. (Ayni wa ghayruh) And 'qurban' is a metaphor for direct contact, from using cause for effect. (Hamawi) 'What is under the waist-wrapper': this restricts qurban to what is under the waist-wrapper, so it excludes the saying of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) who said: avoid the place of blood because the harm is there, and enjoy her above the navel without a waist-wrapper. As for qurban (direct contact), it is prohibited due to the verse: 'And do not approach them until they are pure' (2:222). As for what is under the waist-wrapper, due to the verse: 'So keep away from women during menstruation' (2:222). This necessitates avoidance of all her body except that above the waist-wrapper is permitted due to the hadith of A'isha who said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to command me to put on a waist-wrapper and then he would touch me. So what is under the waist-wrapper remained on prohibition. And 'reciting the Quran': due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite anything of the Quran.' This is a proof against Malik regarding the menstruating woman, and its absolute wording includes less than a verse, so it is a proof against al-Tahawi in his permissibility. As for touching the Quran, due to the verse: 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). (Mustakhlas) And recitation etc. is absolute. Al-Tahawi said: reciting less than a verse is permissible. Malik said: It is permissible for the menstruating woman to recite the Quran, but not for the junub. (Miskin) 'Mussah' (touching it): i.e., it prevents touching whether the entire Quran or a surah. Except with a cover: meaning a separate leather case like a pouch. Touching it with the sleeve is makruh, and this is the correct view and the fatwa. (Miskin) The intended cover is one not included in the sale of the mushaf except by condition. As for a stitched cover, touching it is not permissible. Likewise, touching with the sleeve is not allowed because the sleeve is attached to him. As for books of shari'ah, it is permissible to take them with the sleeve for necessity. There is no harm in giving the mushaf to children to memorize the Quran. (Mustakhlas) And it is said in al-Fath: There is no harm for a junub or menstruating woman to visit graves, eat and drink after rinsing the mouth and washing the hands; before that it is makruh.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the prohibitions for a menstruating woman (ha'id). It lists acts that become invalid or prohibited during menstruation. The first prohibition is prayer (salah), including funeral prayer, sujud al-tilawah, and sujud al-shukr. She must not pray, but she does not need to make up missed prayers after purity. Fasting, however, is also invalid but must be made up later. The proof is the hadith of A'isha: women were commanded to make up fasting but not prayer. The reason given is that making up prayers would cause hardship due to their frequency, while making up fasts is easier. The obligation of making up fasts is on delay (ala al-tarakhi), not immediate, according to most scholars. The second set of prohibitions includes: entering the mosque (even for passing through), circumambulation (tawaf), intimate contact (qurban) below the waist-wrapper, reciting the Quran, and touching the Quran without a cover. For each, the author provides evidence and addresses opposing views. For mosque entry, the hadith 'I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman or a junub' is cited against Shafi'i who allows passing through. For circumambulation, it is prevented due to impurity; the author clarifies that tawaf is invalid while in a state of hadath. For intimate contact, verses from Surah al-Baqarah (2:222) are cited prohibiting approach until purity, and the permission for above the waist-wrapper based on a hadith of A'isha. For Quran recitation, the hadith forbids recitation for both ha'id and junub; this refutes Malik who permits it for ha'id and al-Tahawi who permits less than a verse. For touching the Quran, the verse 'None touch it except the purified' prohibits touching without a separate cover. Touching with the sleeve or a stitched cover is makruh. The passage concludes with additional rulings: a junub or ha'id may visit graves, eat/drink after rinsing mouth and washing hands, but it is makruh before that.

Key Terms
قضاء الصوم على التراخي (qadāʾ al-ṣawm ʿalā al-tarākhī): Making up missed fasts is obligatory but can be delayed until before the next Ramadan.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which statement is correct according to the Hanafi school regarding menstruation?
A) A menstruating woman must make up both prayer and fasting.
B) She must make up only prayer, not fasting.
C) She must make up only fasting, not prayer.
D) She must make up neither.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman is exempt from prayer without make-up but must make up missed fasts, with the majority allowing delay.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Other Prohibitions: Mosque, Tawaf, Intercourse, Quran
Enumeration of prohibitions for menstruation: mosque, tawaf, intercourse, Quran recitation, touching.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the five additional prohibitions for a menstruating woman, cite their evidence, and distinguish the Hanafi position on mosque entry from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman is prohibited from entering the mosque, performing tawaf, intercourse, reciting Quran, and touching the Quran; each prohibition is based on explicit texts.

Beyond prayer and fasting, a menstruating woman faces several other prohibitions related to the mosque, the Quran, and intimate relations. This lesson examines each prohibition, its proof, and the scholarly differences that arise.

Guided Path
1
List the prohibitions
Identify the five additional prohibitions from the text: mosque entry, tawaf, intercourse (qurban), Quran recitation, and touching the Quran.
The text also discusses exceptions: a separate cover for touching, and interaction above the waist-wrapper.
2
Examine the proofs
For each prohibition, note the evidence: hadith for mosque entry, verse for intercourse, hadith for recitation, and verse for touching. Understand the absolute nature of these texts.
The hadith for mosque entry is general; the Quran verse for intercourse uses the verb 'la taqrabu' (do not approach).
3
Address the Shafi'i difference
The text explicitly refutes al-Shafi'i who allows passing through the mosque. The Hanafi position is based on the absolute wording of the hadith.
The dispute is a clear thamarah al-khilaf with practical consequences.
4
Understand the exceptions
Touching the Quran is allowed with a separate cover (ghilaf munfasil). Intercourse is prohibited but activities above the waist-wrapper are permitted based on the hadith of Aisha.
Muhammad al-Shaybani's view on avoiding only the place of blood is excluded; the Hanafi position is more restrictive.
5
Distinguish recitation from touching
Recitation and touching are separate prohibitions. Some scholars (Malik, al-Tahawi) allowed recitation with conditions, but the Hanafi school prohibits it absolutely.
The hadith 'la taqra' al-haid wa la al-junub' is the primary proof.

(فتح) و تقضيه دونها أي تقضي الحائض الصوم بعد انقطاع الحيض، ولا تقضي الصلاة؛ لما روي عن معاذة العدوية قالت: "سألت عائشة ما بال الحائض تقضي الصوم دون الصلاة؟" فقالت: "أحرورية أنت"؟ فقلت: "لست بحرورية ولكني أسال، فقالت: "كان" يصيبنا ذلك، فكنا نؤمر بقضاء الصوم ولا نؤمر بقضاء الصلاة"؛ ولأن في قضائها الصلاة حرجاً بتكررها في كل يوم، وتكرر الحيض في كل شهر، بخلاف الصوم فإن في قضائه ليس بحرج، والنفاس ملحق بالحيض فيلحقها الحرج في قضائها، والأصح أن قضاء الصوم يجب على التراخي . عند الأكثر، وعند أبي بكر الرازي: يجب على الفور. (فتح، مسكين) ك فرد ك ف د ودخول مسجد، والطواف، وقربان ما تحت الإزار، وقراءة القرآن، ومسه إلا بغلاف، ومنع أي ويمنع الحدث المس، أي الأصغر أي مس القرآن لا قراءته ودخول مسجد: [مطلقاً سواء كان على وجه العبور أم لا، وقال الشافعي يباح دخول المسجد للحائض على وجه العبور.(مسكين)] أي موضع العبادة المعهودة، فيشمل الكعبة دون مسجد البيت، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يدخل المسجد من على بدنه نجاسة. وفي "الخزانة" : إذا فسا في المسجد لم ير بعضهم به بأسا، وقال بعضهم: إن احتاج إليه يخرج منه، وهو الأصح، ولو احتلم في المسجد تيمم وخرج إن لم يخف، وجلس مع التيمم إن خاف إلا أنه لا يصلي ولا يقرأ. (فتح) وقال في "المستخلص" : يمنع الحيض دخول المسجد؛ لقوله عليها: "فإني لا أحل المسجد لحائض ولا لجنب"، وهو بإطلاقه حجة على الشافعي في إباحة الدخول على وجه العبور. والطواف أي يمنع حل الطواف لا صحته، وإنما ذكر الطواف مع أنه إذا منع عن دخول المسجد لا تتمكن الحائض من الطواف لأنه فيه؛ لئلا يتوهم أ أنه لما جاز لها الوقوف مع أنه أقوى أركان الحج فلأن يجوز لها الطواف أولى، أو يتوهم جواز دخول المسجد لضرورة الطواف، فأزال ذلك الوهم. عيني وغيره) وقربان: مجاز عن المباشرة . من إطلاق السبب وإرادة المسبب. (حموي) ما تحت الإزار : قيد القربان بـ"ما تحت الإزار "؛ ليخرج قول محمد فإنه قال: يجتنب موضع الدم؛ لأن الأذى فيه، ويستمتع بها بما دون السرة بلا إزار، أما القربان - أي المباشرة - فممنوع؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۲۲)، وأما ما تحت الإزار؛ فلقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ (البقرة: ٢٢٢)، فإنه يوجب الاجتناب من كل بدنها غير أن ما فوق الإزار مرخص لحديث عائشة لها فإنها قالت: كان النبي عليه يأمرني أن أتزر ثم يباشرني، فبقي ما تحت الإزار على الحرمة، وقوله: قراءة القرآن؛ فلقوله عليه: "لا تقرأ الحائض والجنب شيئاً من القرآن"، وهو حجة على مالك في الحائض، وهو بإطلاقه يتناول ما دون الآية، فيكون حجة على الطحاوي في إباحته، وأما مس القرآن؛ فلقوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَمَسُّهُ إِلَّا الْمُطَهَّرُونَ ﴾ (الواقعة: ۷۹)، (مستخلص) وقراءة إلخ: مطلقاً وقال الطحاوي: يباح قراءة ما دون الآية، وقال مالك: يجوز للحائض قراءة القرآن دون الجنب. (مسكين) مسته: أي يمنع مس سواء مس تمام القرآن أو سورة منه. إلا بغلاف: [هو الجلد المنفصل كالخريطة، ويكره مسه بالكم، وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. (مسكين)] والمراد الغلاف الذي لا يدخل في بيع المصحف إلا بشرط، وأما غلاف المشرز فلا يجوز مسه، وكذا لا يجوز المس بكمه؛ لأنه تبع له، أما كتب الشريعة فيجوز أخذها بالكم للضرورة، ولا بأس بدفع المصحف إلى الصبيان لحفظ القرآن (مستخلص) وقال في "الفتح": ولا بأس لجنب وحائض بزيارة القبور وأكل وشرب بعد المضمضة وغسل اليد، وأما قبلها فيكره.
It prevents prayer and fasting, and she makes up the latter but not the former. Prayer, due to its indefinite form, includes funeral prayer as well. There is no doubt that the prevention of something includes its parts, hence she is prevented from prostration of recitation and prostration of thanks. (Fath) And she makes it up without it: meaning the menstruating woman makes up fasting after menstruation ends, and she does not make up prayer; due to what is narrated from Mu'adhah al-'Adawiyyah: she said, 'I asked A'isha: Why does the menstruating woman make up fasting but not prayer?' She said, 'Are you a Haruriyyah?' I said, 'I am not a Haruriyyah, but I am asking.' She said, 'That used to happen to us, so we were commanded to make up fasting and were not commanded to make up prayer.' And because in making up prayer there is hardship due to its repetition every day and the repetition of menstruation every month, unlike fasting, for making it up is not a hardship. Postpartum bleeding is attached to menstruation, so hardship applies in its making up. The correct view is that making up fasting is obligatory with delay according to the majority, and according to Abu Bakr al-Razi: immediately. (Fath, Miskin). And entering the mosque, and circumambulation, and approaching what is under the waist-wrapper, and reciting the Quran, and touching it except with a cover. The prevention of hadath (minor impurity) prevents touching, meaning the smaller one, i.e., touching the Quran, not reciting it. Entering the mosque: absolutely, whether for passage or not. Al-Shafi'i permitted the menstruating woman to enter the mosque for passage. (Miskin) 'Mosque' means the customary place of worship, so it includes the Ka'bah but not the mosque of the house. It indicates that one with impurity on his body should not enter the mosque. In al-Khazanah: if someone passes wind in the mosque, some saw no harm, some said if needed he should exit, which is more correct. If one has a wet dream in the mosque, he should perform tayammum and exit if not afraid, and sit with tayammum if afraid, but he should not pray or recite. (Fath) And it is said in al-Mustakhlas: Menstruation prevents entering the mosque due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman nor for a junub.' This is an absolute proof against al-Shafi'i regarding permissibility of passing through. Circumambulation: meaning it prevents its validity, not its correctness. It is mentioned even though if prevented from entering the mosque she cannot perform tawaf because it is inside, lest one misunderstand that since she is permitted to stand (at Arafat) which is a stronger pillar, then she should be permitted to do tawaf, or misunderstand the permissibility of entering the mosque for necessity of tawaf. So that misunderstanding is removed. (Ayni wa ghayruh) And 'qurban' is a metaphor for direct contact, from using cause for effect. (Hamawi) 'What is under the waist-wrapper': this restricts qurban to what is under the waist-wrapper, so it excludes the saying of Muhammad (al-Shaybani) who said: avoid the place of blood because the harm is there, and enjoy her above the navel without a waist-wrapper. As for qurban (direct contact), it is prohibited due to the verse: 'And do not approach them until they are pure' (2:222). As for what is under the waist-wrapper, due to the verse: 'So keep away from women during menstruation' (2:222). This necessitates avoidance of all her body except that above the waist-wrapper is permitted due to the hadith of A'isha who said: The Prophet, peace be upon him, used to command me to put on a waist-wrapper and then he would touch me. So what is under the waist-wrapper remained on prohibition. And 'reciting the Quran': due to his saying, peace be upon him: 'The menstruating woman and the junub should not recite anything of the Quran.' This is a proof against Malik regarding the menstruating woman, and its absolute wording includes less than a verse, so it is a proof against al-Tahawi in his permissibility. As for touching the Quran, due to the verse: 'None touch it except the purified' (56:79). (Mustakhlas) And recitation etc. is absolute. Al-Tahawi said: reciting less than a verse is permissible. Malik said: It is permissible for the menstruating woman to recite the Quran, but not for the junub. (Miskin) 'Mussah' (touching it): i.e., it prevents touching whether the entire Quran or a surah. Except with a cover: meaning a separate leather case like a pouch. Touching it with the sleeve is makruh, and this is the correct view and the fatwa. (Miskin) The intended cover is one not included in the sale of the mushaf except by condition. As for a stitched cover, touching it is not permissible. Likewise, touching with the sleeve is not allowed because the sleeve is attached to him. As for books of shari'ah, it is permissible to take them with the sleeve for necessity. There is no harm in giving the mushaf to children to memorize the Quran. (Mustakhlas) And it is said in al-Fath: There is no harm for a junub or menstruating woman to visit graves, eat and drink after rinsing the mouth and washing the hands; before that it is makruh.
Source pages p. 43

Commentary
This passage is a detailed commentary on the prohibitions for a menstruating woman (ha'id). It lists acts that become invalid or prohibited during menstruation. The first prohibition is prayer (salah), including funeral prayer, sujud al-tilawah, and sujud al-shukr. She must not pray, but she does not need to make up missed prayers after purity. Fasting, however, is also invalid but must be made up later. The proof is the hadith of A'isha: women were commanded to make up fasting but not prayer. The reason given is that making up prayers would cause hardship due to their frequency, while making up fasts is easier. The obligation of making up fasts is on delay (ala al-tarakhi), not immediate, according to most scholars. The second set of prohibitions includes: entering the mosque (even for passing through), circumambulation (tawaf), intimate contact (qurban) below the waist-wrapper, reciting the Quran, and touching the Quran without a cover. For each, the author provides evidence and addresses opposing views. For mosque entry, the hadith 'I do not permit the mosque for a menstruating woman or a junub' is cited against Shafi'i who allows passing through. For circumambulation, it is prevented due to impurity; the author clarifies that tawaf is invalid while in a state of hadath. For intimate contact, verses from Surah al-Baqarah (2:222) are cited prohibiting approach until purity, and the permission for above the waist-wrapper based on a hadith of A'isha. For Quran recitation, the hadith forbids recitation for both ha'id and junub; this refutes Malik who permits it for ha'id and al-Tahawi who permits less than a verse. For touching the Quran, the verse 'None touch it except the purified' prohibits touching without a separate cover. Touching with the sleeve or a stitched cover is makruh. The passage concludes with additional rulings: a junub or ha'id may visit graves, eat/drink after rinsing mouth and washing hands, but it is makruh before that.

Key Terms
قربان ما تحت الإزار (qurbān mā taḥta al-izār): Intimate contact between husband and wife below the waist-wrapper, i.e., sexual intercourse.
مس المصحف بغلاف (mass al-muṣḥaf bighilāf): Touching the Quran with a separate cover (e.g., a leather case) is permitted; without it, it is prohibited.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following is NOT prohibited for a menstruating woman according to the Hanafi school?
A) Entering the mosque for passing through
B) Touching the Quran with a separate cover
C) Reciting the Quran
D) Performing tawaf

Key Takeaway
Beyond prayer and fasting, menstruation prohibits mosque entry, tawaf, intercourse, and Quran recitation/touching, each with clear evidence and scholarly nuance.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
Prohibitions for a Menstruating Woman: Rulings and Proofs
Listing prohibitions with proofs and rebuttals

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the six prohibitions for a menstruating woman, identify the Quranic and hadith proofs for each, and explain the Hanafi position on mosque entry and the intra-Hanafi disagreement on direct contact.

Core Idea
A menstruating woman is prohibited from six acts: intercourse, mosque entry, tawaf, direct contact below navel, Quran recitation, and touching the mushaf without a cover.

This lesson enumerates the prohibitions specific to a menstruating woman according to the Hanafi school. Each prohibition is grounded in explicit Quranic verses or authentic hadith. The text also addresses inter-madhhab differences, particularly with al-Shafi'i on mosque entry and with al-Tahawi on reciting less than a verse, as well as an intra-Hanafi difference between Imam Muhammad and the majority regarding the extent of permissible contact.

Guided Path
1
Identify the six prohibitions
Read the passage and list the six acts that are prohibited for a menstruating woman: intercourse, entering a mosque, performing tawaf, approaching what is under the waist-wrapper (direct contact), reciting the Quran, and touching the Quran except with a cover.
These are the main rulings, each supported by evidence.
2
Locate the dalil for each prohibition
For each prohibition, find the specific Quranic verse or hadith cited. For example, the prohibition of entering a mosque is based on the hadith 'I do not make the mosque permissible for a menstruating woman or a junub.' Note the source and wording.
The text provides both Quranic and hadith proofs.
3
Analyze the Hanafi textual interpretation
Understand how the absolute wording of certain proofs is used to reject exceptions. For instance, the hadith on mosque entry is absolute and covers even passing through, which is the Hanafi argument against al-Shafi'i.
This step is key to understanding Hanafi usul.
4
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Identify the difference between Imam Muhammad and the majority (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf). Imam Muhammad permits enjoyment above the navel without a waist-wrapper, while the majority prohibits all direct contact. The text favors the majority.
The mufta bihi is the majority position.
5
Synthesize the mufta bihi position
Combine the information to state the operative ruling for fatwa: the six prohibitions are absolute, with the majority view on direct contact being the relied-upon opinion.
This prepares you for applying the rulings in practice.

كتاب الطهارة
ما يحرم على الحائض فعله
الجماع، ودخول مسجد، والطواف، وقربان ما تحت الإزار، وقراءة القرآن، ومسه إلا بغلاف، ومنع
أي ويمنع الحدث المس،
أي الأصغر أي مس القرآن لا قراءته
ودخول مسجد: [مطلقاً سواء كان على وجه العبور أم لا، وقال الشافعي يباح دخول المسجد للحائض على وجه العبور.(مسكين)] أي موضع العبادة المعهودة، فيشمل الكعبة دون مسجد البيت، وفيه إشارة إلى أنه لا يدخل المسجد من على بدنه نجاسة. وفي "الخزانة" : إذا فسا في المسجد لم ير بعضهم به بأسا، وقال بعضهم: إن احتاج إليه يخرج منه، وهو الأصح، ولو احتلم في المسجد تيمم وخرج إن لم يخف، وجلس مع التيمم إن خاف إلا أنه لا يصلي ولا يقرأ. (فتح) وقال في "المستخلص" : يمنع الحيض دخول المسجد؛ لقوله عليها: "فإني لا أحل المسجد لحائض ولا لجنب"، وهو بإطلاقه حجة على الشافعي في إباحة الدخول على وجه العبور. والطواف أي يمنع حل الطواف لا صحته، وإنما ذكر الطواف مع أنه إذا منع عن دخول المسجد لا تتمكن الحائض من الطواف لأنه فيه؛ لئلا يتوهم أ أنه لما جاز لها الوقوف مع أنه أقوى أركان الحج فلأن يجوز لها الطواف أولى، أو يتوهم جواز دخول المسجد لضرورة الطواف، فأزال ذلك الوهم. عيني وغيره) وقربان: مجاز عن المباشرة . من إطلاق السبب وإرادة المسبب. (حموي)
ما تحت الإزار : قيد القربان بـ"ما تحت الإزار "; ليخرج قول محمد فإنه قال: يجتنب موضع الدم؛ لأن الأذى فيه، ويستمتع بها بما دون السرة بلا إزار، أما القربان - أي المباشرة - فممنوع؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَلَا تَقْرَبُوهُنَّ حَتَّى يَطْهُرْنَ ﴾ (البقرة: ۲۲۲)، وأما ما تحت الإزار؛ فلقوله تعالى: ﴿فَاعْتَزِلُوا النِّسَاءَ فِي الْمَحِيضِ (البقرة: ٢٢٢)، فإنه يوجب الاجتناب من كل بدنها غير أن ما فوق الإزار مرخص لحديث عائشة لها فإنها قالت: كان النبي عليه يأمرني أن أتزر ثم يباشرني، فبقي ما تحت الإزار على الحرمة، وقوله: قراءة القرآن؛ فلقوله عليه: "لا تقرأ الحائض والجنب شيئاً من القرآن"، وهو حجة على مالك في الحائض، وهو بإطلاقه يتناول ما دون الآية، فيكون حجة
القرآن مطلقاً .
على الطحاوي في إباحته، وأما مس القرآن؛ فلقوله تعالى: ﴿لا يَمَسُّهُ إِلَّا الْمُطَهَّرُونَ ﴾ (الواقعة: ۷۹)، (مستخلص) وقراءة إلخ: مطلقاً وقال الطحاوي: يباح قراءة ما دون الآية، وقال مالك: يجوز للحائض قراءة القرآن دون الجنب. (مسكين) مسته: أي يمنع مس سواء مس تمام القرآن أو سورة منه. إلا بغلاف: [هو الجلد المنفصل كالخريطة، ويكره مسه بالكم، وهو الصحيح وعليه الفتوى. (مسكين)] والمراد الغلاف الذي لا يدخل في بيع المصحف إلا بشرط، وأما غلاف المشرز فلا يجوز مسه، وكذا لا يجوز المس بكمه؛ لأنه تبع له، أما كتب الشريعة فيجوز أخذها بالكم للضرورة، ولا بأس بدفع المصحف إلى الصبيان لحفظ القرآن (مستخلص) وقال في "الفتح": ولا بأس لجنب وحائض بزيارة القبور وأكل وشرب بعد المضمضة وغسل اليد، وأما قبلها فيكره.
من
The Book of Purification. What is prohibited for a menstruating woman: intercourse, entering a mosque, tawaf, approaching what is under the waist-wrapper, reciting the Quran, and touching it except with a cover. And it prevents... i.e. the minor impure event prevents touching, i.e., touching the Quran not reciting it. And entering a mosque: [absolutely, whether for passing through or not, and al-Shafi'i said it is permissible for a menstruating woman to enter a mosque for passing through. (Miskin)] i.e., the customary place of worship, so it includes the Ka'bah but not the mosque of the house. And in it is an indication that one with impurity on his body does not enter the mosque. And in al-Khazanah: If one passes wind in the mosque, some saw no harm, and some said if he needs to leave he may leave, and that is the most correct. And if he has a wet dream in the mosque, he performs tayammum and leaves if he does not fear, and sits with tayammum if he fears, but he does not pray or recite. (Fath) And al-Mustakhlas said: Menstruation prevents entering the mosque due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'I do not make the mosque permissible for a menstruating woman or a junub.' And its absolute wording is proof against al-Shafi'i in permitting entering for passing through. As for tawaf, it means it prevents the permissibility of tawaf, not its validity. And tawaf is mentioned even though if entering the mosque is prevented, the menstruating woman cannot perform tawaf because it is in it; to avoid the misunderstanding that when standing at Arafat is permitted despite being the strongest pillar of Hajj, so tawaf should be more permissible, or to avoid the misunderstanding of permitting entering the mosque for the necessity of tawaf. So he removed that misunderstanding. (Ayni and others) And 'qurban' is a metaphor for direct contact, by naming the cause and intending the effect. (Hamawi) 'What is under the waist-wrapper' restricts 'approaching' to what is under the waist-wrapper to exclude the statement of Muhammad, for he said: he avoids the place of blood because the harm is in it, and he may enjoy her above the navel without a waist-wrapper. But approaching (i.e., direct contact) is prohibited due to His statement: 'And do not approach them until they are pure' (al-Baqarah: 222). And what is under the waist-wrapper is due to His statement: 'So keep away from women during menstruation' (al-Baqarah: 222). For it necessitates avoidance from her entire body, except that above the waist-wrapper is granted a concession due to the hadith of Aisha, may Allah be pleased with her: 'The Prophet, peace be upon him, would command me to tie the waist-wrapper and then he would have direct contact with me.' So what is under the waist-wrapper remained prohibited. And regarding reciting the Quran, it is due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'A menstruating woman and a junub should not recite anything from the Quran.' And it is proof against Malik regarding the menstruating woman, and its absolute wording includes less than a verse, so it is proof against al-Tahawi who permits it. And as for touching the Quran, it is due to His statement: 'None touch it except the purified' (al-Waqi'ah: 79). (Mustakhlas) And reciting etc.: absolutely. And al-Tahawi said: reciting less than a verse is permissible. And Malik said: a menstruating woman may recite the Quran, but not a junub. (Miskin) 'Touching it' means it prevents touching, whether touching the entire Quran or a surah of it. 'Except with a cover' [it is the separate skin, like a pouch, and it is disliked to touch it with the sleeve, and that is correct and the fatwa is upon it. (Miskin)] And what is meant is the cover that is not included in the sale of the mushaf except conditionally. As for a sewn cover, it is not permissible to touch it, and likewise it is not permissible to touch with his sleeve because it is a follow-up. As for books of Shariah, it is permissible to take them with the sleeve out of necessity, and there is no harm in giving the mushaf to boys to memorize the Quran. (Mustakhlas) And al-Fath said: There is no harm for a junub or menstruating woman to visit graves, eat and drink after rinsing the mouth and washing the hands. Before that it is disliked.
Source pages p. 44

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proofs from the Book of Purification, specifically enumerating what is prohibited for a menstruating woman. The author lists six prohibitions: sexual intercourse, entering a mosque, tawaf (circumambulation of the Ka'bah), approaching what is under the waist-wrapper (i.e., direct contact above the navel is permitted but below is not), reciting the Quran, and touching the Quran without a cover. Each prohibition is supported by textual evidence from the Quran and Sunnah, and the author refutes opposing views, including those of al-Shafi'i (who permits entering a mosque for passing through), al-Tahawi (who permits reciting less than a verse), and Malik (who permits reciting for a menstruating woman but not a junub). The author also clarifies that touching the Quran with a cover (such as a separate leather pouch) is permissible, but touching with a sleeve is disliked. The passage then concludes with a permission from al-Fath for a junub or menstruating woman to eat and drink after rinsing their mouth and washing hands, but it is disliked before that. This passage demonstrates the Hanafi reliance on primary sources and their systematic response to inter-madhhab differences.

Key Terms
قربان (qurban): Metaphor for direct sexual contact (mubashara), not limited to intercourse.
ما تحت الإزار (ma tahta al-izar): The area under the waist-wrapper, i.e., the lower half in relation to the waist (below the navel).
غلاف (ghilaf): A separate cover for the mushaf, such as a leather pouch, that is not attached to the book.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is a menstruating woman prohibited from entering the mosque?
A) Only when she intends to stay, but passing through is allowed.
B) Absolutely, even for passing through.
C) She may enter if she needs to attend a class.
D) She may enter but must wear a cover.

Key Takeaway
A menstruating woman must refrain from six specific acts; each prohibition is firmly grounded in Quran and Sunnah, and the Hanafi school applies these proofs absolutely, rejecting exceptions that other schools allow.
