Taharah — Purification
intermediate
8 min
The Definition of Intervening Purity and Its Twelve Rulings
Defining intervening purity and listing its rulings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of al-tahr al-mutakhallil and list the twelve rulings of menstruation, distinguishing the four specific rulings from the eight shared with postpartum bleeding.

Core Idea
The intervening purity is legally hayd/nifas, carrying all associated prohibitions and obligations.

In this lesson, we unpack the concept of 'intervening purity' (al-tahr al-mutakhallil) — a period of apparent cleanliness that falls between two bleeding episodes within the overall duration of hayd or nifas. The author clarifies that such a gap is not considered true purity; rather, it is legally treated as part of the menstrual or postpartum period. He then enumerates the twelve rulings that flow from hayd, four of which are unique to menstruation and eight shared with nifas, providing a comprehensive legal framework.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Act and Its Ruling
Recognize that 'intervening purity' is a period of no bleeding between two bleeding episodes, and it is legally classified as hayd or nifas, not as true purity.
The text states: والطهر المتخلل بين الدمين في المدة حيض ونفاس
2
Understand the Underlying Principle
The ruling is based on the idea that the blood 'is in its place' (الدم في موضعه), meaning the underlying bleeding state continues; the gap is subordinate to the surrounding blood.
This principle appears in the dispute section but underlies the unconditional view.
3
List the Four Rulings Specific to Hayd
Memorize the four rulings that apply only to menstruation: completion of ‘idda, istibra (ascertaining pregnancy), determining puberty, and distinguishing between sunna and bid‘a divorce.
These are unique because they depend on the actual occurrence of menses.
4
List the Eight Rulings Shared with Nifas
Identify the eight rulings common to both hayd and nifas: abandoning prayer without making it up, fasting made up, prohibition of entering mosque, tawaf, reciting Quran, touching mushaf, intercourse, and obligation of ghusl upon cessation.
The eighth ruling is obligatory ghusl when the bleeding stops.
5
Apply the Ruling on Intercourse Timing
After the maximum hayd (10 days), intercourse is permissible even if bleeding continues; after the minimum (3 days) but before 10, ghusl or passage of a prayer time is required.
This is a practical consequence of the definition of intervening purity.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
الطهر المتخلل
س م ط س م ط والطهر المتخلّلُ بين الدمين في المدّة حيض ونفاس، وأقل الطهر .
أي مدة الحيض والنفاس
أي في مدة النفاس الفاصل بين الدمين
مختص
ومنعهما الجنابة والنفاس إنما أفرد النفاس بعد قوله : وقراءة القرآن ومسه؛ لئلا يتوهم أن ذلك الحكم .
بالحيض، فإن النفاس في معناه ألا ترى أنه عليها قال: "لا يمس القرآن إلا الطاهر والطهارة معدومة في النفساء بدليل حرمة وطئها، ثم اعلم أن الحيض فيه اثنا عشر حكماً، أربعة منها تختص بالحيض، وهي: انقضاء العدة، والاستبراء والحكم ،ببلوغها والفصل بين طلاق السنة والبدعة، وثمانية يشترك فيها الحيض والنفاس، وهي: ترك الصلاة لا إلى قضاء، والصوم إلى قضاء، وحرمة الدخول في المسجد، وحرمة الطواف بالبيت، وحرمة قراءة القرآن، وحرمة مس المصحف، وحرمة جماعها والثامن: وجوب الغسل عند انقطاعهما. (مستخلص) والنفاس: إلا قراءة الآيات المشتملة على دعاء أو ذكر، إن كانت بنية الدعاء بتصرم: الصرم: القطع، قال الله تعالى: ﴿لَيَصْرِ مُنَّهَا مُصْبِحِينَ ﴾ (القلم:۱۷)، أي ليقطعن ثمرها والتصرم الانقطاع، ثم في العبارة نظر؛ لأن حل الوطء بعد تمام العشرة لا يتوقف على الانقطاع، بل يحل الوطء بتمام العشرة، سواء انقطع أو لا؛ لأن ما بعدها استحاضة، لكن أخرج الكلام مخرج العادة، فإن تمام العشرة قل ما يخلو عن الانقطاع. (مستخلص) لأكثره: أي بعد عشرة أيام، فاللام بمعنى "بعد" ما في قوله تعالى: ﴿أَقِمِ الصَّلاةَ لِدُلُوكِ الشَّمْسِ﴾ (الإسراء:۷۸) أي
بعد دلوكها، وقوله علي : صوموا لرؤيته ، أي بعد رؤيته، وقال زفر والشافعي: توطأ بلا غسل.
حتى تغتسل : أي انقطع الدم بعد مضي أقل مدة الحيض قبل تمام العشرة وهو عادتها لا توطأ. (مسكين) أدنى وقت صلاة أي مكتوبة ولهذا قال في "الدر": لو طهرت في وقت العيد لابد أن يمضي وقت الظهر، أي يمضي عليها قدر أن تقدر للاغتسال والتحريمة بأن انقطع في آخر الوقت، أو يمضي عليها وقت صلاة تصير الصلاة ديناً في ذمتها، وفيه إيماء إلى أن المرأة لو كانت نصرانية مثلاً لا يحل وطئها قبل الغسل؛ إذ الصلاة لم تصر ديناً في ذمتها، وفي تخصيص الوطء بالذكر إشارة إلى أن الحكم بطهارة الحائض والنفساء بمضي الوقت المذكور إنما هو في حق الوطء، فأما في قراءة القرآن فلا (فتح) والطهر : أي الحيض الذي هو دم حكماً لا حقيقة.(فتح) الدمين المكتنفين للظهر أعم . من أن يكون في الحيض أو النفاس. (فتح)
حيض ونفاس: مطلقا عندهما، وعند محمد: الطهر إذا تخلل بين الدمين في الحيض إن كان أقل من ثلاثة أيام لم يفصل بحال، سواء كان أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما أو لم يكن؛ لأن الدم في موضعه فكان أولى بالاعتبار، وإن كان
ثلاثة أيام، فإن كان أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما لم يفصل أيضاً، وإن زاد الطهر عليهما فصل. والفتوى على مذهبه،
The Book of Purification. The Intervening Purity. ... And the intervening purity between the two bleedings within the duration is menstruation and postpartum bleeding, and the minimum of purity... meaning the period of menstruation and postpartum bleeding, meaning in the postpartum period the separation between the two bleedings is specific. And both (menstruation and postpartum bleeding) prevent... only postpartum bleeding is singled out after his statement: 'and reciting the Quran and touching it' lest one imagine that the ruling is specific to menstruation. Indeed, postpartum bleeding is similar. Do you not see that he, peace be upon him, said: 'None touches the Quran except the pure.' And purity is absent in the postpartum woman as evidenced by the prohibition of intercourse with her. Then know that menstruation has twelve rulings. Four are specific to menstruation: completion of the waiting period, istibra (ascertaining pregnancy), the ruling of her reaching puberty, and distinguishing between sunna and bid'a divorce. And eight are shared by menstruation and postpartum bleeding: abandoning prayer without making it up, fasting made up, prohibition of entering the mosque, prohibition of tawaf around the House, prohibition of reciting Quran, prohibition of touching the mushaf, prohibition of intercourse, and the eighth: obligation of ghusl upon their cessation. (Mustakhlas) And postpartum bleeding: except reciting verses containing supplication or remembrance if intended as supplication. 'Tasarrum' means cutting, Allah said: 'They will certainly cut off their fruit in the morning' (al-Qalam: 17), i.e., cut off its fruit, and tasarrum means cessation. Then in the wording there is consideration because the permissibility of intercourse after ten days is not dependent on cessation; rather intercourse becomes permissible after ten days, whether it stops or not, because what follows is istihada. But the speech is made in the manner of habit, for ten days rarely lack cessation. (Mustakhlas) 'For its maximum' means after ten days. The lam is in the sense of 'after', as in His statement: 'Establish prayer at the declining of the sun' (al-Isra: 78), i.e., after its decline, and his statement, peace be upon him: 'Fast upon seeing it,' i.e., after seeing it. And Zufar and al-Shafi'i said: she is had intercourse without ghusl. 'Until she bathes' means if the blood stops after the minimum period of menstruation before ten days and it is her habit, she is not had intercourse. (Miskin) 'The minimum time of a prayer' means an obligatory prayer. Hence al-Durr said: if she becomes pure at the time of Eid, it is necessary that the time of Zuhr passes, i.e., enough time passes for her to be able to bathe and say the opening takbir, if it stops at the end of the time, or enough time for a prayer to become due in her liability. And in it is an indication that if the woman were a Christian, for example, intercourse would not be permissible before ghusl since prayer did not become due in her liability. And the specification of intercourse indicates that the ruling of purity of the menstruating and postpartum woman by the passage of the mentioned time is only regarding intercourse; as for reciting the Quran, no. (Fath) And 'al-tahr' means the bleeding that is legally considered as menstruation, not in reality. (Fath) 'The two bleedings surrounding the intervening purity' are general, whether in menstruation or postpartum bleeding. (Fath) Menstruation and postpartum bleeding: absolutely according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad?). And according to Muhammad: the intervening purity if it occurs between two bleedings in menstruation, if it is less than three days, it does not separate at all, whether it is less than the two bleedings or equal to them or not; because the blood is in its place so it is more deserving of consideration. If it is three days, then if it is less than the two bleedings or equal to them, it also does not separate, and if the purity exceeds them, it separates. And the fatwa is upon his school.
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This passage defines the 'intervening purity' (al-tahr al-mutakhallil) between two instances of bleeding. The author clarifies that the period of purity between two bleedings within the duration of menstruation or postpartum bleeding is legally considered part of the menstrual or postpartum period. The passage then enumerates twelve rulings of menstruation: four specific to hayd (completion of idda, istibra, puberty determination, distinguishing divorce types) and eight shared with nifas (abandoning prayer without makeup, making up fasts, prohibition of entering mosque, tawaf, reciting Quran, touching mushaf, intercourse, and obligation of ghusl after cessation). For postpartum bleeding, reciting verses with supplication is allowed if intended as dhikr. The author then addresses the permissibility of intercourse after menses. According to the correct view, intercourse becomes permissible after ten days (maximum of hayd) even if bleeding has not stopped, because after ten days it is istihada. However, if bleeding stops within the minimum period (three days) and she has a habit, she must perform ghusl or wait until a prayer time passes. The ruling about passing of prayer time is specifically for intercourse, not for reciting Quran. Finally, the passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad holds that if the intervening purity is less than three days, it does not separate the two bleedings; if exactly three days and less than or equal to the bleedings, it also does not separate; only if the purity exceeds the bleedings does it separate. The fatwa is according to Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tahr al-mutakhallil): A period of purity that occurs between two instances of bleeding within the overall duration of hayd/nifas, legally considered part of the menstrual or postpartum period.
تصرم (tasarrum): Cessation of bleeding, derived from the root meaning to cut off.
عدة (idda): Waiting period after divorce or death, which is counted by menstrual cycles.
استبراء (istibra'): Ascertaining that a woman is not pregnant, often by waiting for one menstrual cycle.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, how many rulings are shared between hayd and nifas?
A) Four
B) Eight
C) Twelve
D) Six

Key Takeaway
The intervening purity is legally considered part of hayd or nifas, carrying all associated rulings, including prohibition of prayer, fasting, and intercourse.

The Intra-Hanafi Dispute on the Intervening Purity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on when intervening purity separates bleedings

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa/Abu Yusuf and Imam Muhammad regarding the intervening purity, and apply the mufta bihi position to concrete cases.

Core Idea
Intervening purity unconditionally hayd? Or only if purity exceeds bleedings? Fatwa follows Muhammad.

This lesson dives into a nuanced disagreement within the Hanafi school on whether an intervening period of purity always counts as hayd or only under certain conditions. While Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf treat any gap as hayd unconditionally, Imam Muhammad introduces a detailed criterion based on the duration of the gap relative to the surrounding bleeding episodes. The text concludes that the fatwa follows Imam Muhammad's view, making his position the operative one for practice.

Guided Path
1
State the Positions of Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf
They hold that any intervening purity is unconditionally considered hayd or nifas, regardless of its duration relative to the bleedings.
The text says: حيض ونفاس مطلقا عندهما
2
State Imam Muhammad's First Condition
If the intervening purity is less than 3 days, it never separates the two bleedings; all is hayd.
The text: إن كان أقل من ثلاثة أيام لم يفصل بحال
3
State Imam Muhammad's Second Condition
If the purity is exactly 3 days, it does not separate if it is less than or equal to the bleedings; it only separates if it exceeds the bleedings.
The text: إن كان أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما لم يفصل أيضاً، وإن زاد الطهر عليهما فصل
4
Apply the Rule to a Scenario
Example: 2 days bleeding, 3 days purity, 2 days bleeding. Here purity (3) is equal to bleedings (2+2=4? No, each bleeding is 2? Actually compare to the surrounding bleedings individually? The text says 'أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما' meaning less than the two bleedings or equal to them. The two bleedings are 2 and 2; the purity is 3, which is more than each? More than each? Actually it's more than each individually but less than total? The exact comparison is ambiguous but the standard interpretation: compare purity to each bleeding separately? Many scholars say compare to the total? The standard Hanafi interpretation: 'الدمين' refers to the two bleedings collectively? Actually the text says 'أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما' meaning less than the two bleedings or equal to them. The 'two bleedings' likely means the sum of both? Or each? Most commentaries say the comparison is with each bleeding individually. So if purity exceeds each bleeding, it separates. Here each bleeding is 2, purity is 3, so it exceeds, so it separates. Thus the first 2 days are hayd, the 3 days are tahr (pure), the last 2 days are hayd. So only 2+2=4 days hayd, not 7. The unconditional view would make all 7 days hayd.
The thamarah al-khilaf: the number of hayd days differs, affecting idda, fasting, etc.
5
Memorize the Mufta Bihi Position
The text explicitly states that the fatwa is according to Imam Muhammad's school.
والفتوى على مذهبه

For postpartum bleeding, reciting verses with supplication is allowed if intended as dhikr. The author then addresses the permissibility of intercourse after menses. According to the correct view, intercourse becomes permissible after ten days (maximum of hayd) even if bleeding has not stopped, because after ten days it is istihada. However, if bleeding stops within the minimum period (three days) and she has a habit, she must perform ghusl or wait until a prayer time passes. The ruling about passing of prayer time is specifically for intercourse, not for reciting Quran. Finally, the passage presents a dispute within the Hanafi school: Imam Muhammad holds that if the intervening purity is less than three days, it does not separate the two bleedings; if exactly three days and less than or equal to the bleedings, it also does not separate; only if the purity exceeds the bleedings does it separate. The fatwa is according to Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tahr al-mutakhallil): A period of purity between two bleedings within the duration of hayd/nifas.
مطلقا (mutlaqan): Unconditionally, absolutely.
يفصل (yafsilu): It separates (i.e., the purity breaks the continuity of hayd).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (Imam Muhammad's view), when does an intervening purity of exactly 3 days separate the two bleedings?
A) Always, regardless of the bleeding durations.
B) Only if it is less than the bleedings.
C) Only if it exceeds the bleedings.
D) Never, if it is exactly 3 days.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi in the Hanafi school is Imam Muhammad's view: an intervening purity of 3 days only separates the bleedings if it exceeds their durations.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate

The Intervening Purity (al-Tuhr al-Mutakhallil) in Hayd and Nifas
Intra-Hanafi dispute on intervening purity

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the intervening purity in hayd and nifas, explain the intra-Hanafi dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad, and identify the mufta bihi position.

Core Idea
An interval of purity between two bloods is considered hayd/nifas only if it is less than three days or does not exceed the blood periods; otherwise, it separates them.

This lesson tackles the concept of the intervening purity (al-tuhr al-mutakhallil) in menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The Hanafi school has a nuanced position on when a clear interval between two blood episodes is legally considered part of the menstrual or postpartum state. Understanding this determines a woman's ritual purity status and associated prohibitions. The passage presents a key intra-Hanafi dispute between the three senior disciples and settles on Imam Muhammad's view as the operative fatwa.

Guided Path
1
Identify the core issue
The passage asks: When a woman experiences two separate episodes of bleeding with a clear interval of purity in between, is that interval legally considered part of hayd/nifas or not? The answer affects whether she must refrain from prayer, fasting, etc.
This is not about continuous bleeding but about breaks between blood.
2
State the position of Abu Hanifa and Sahibayn
According to Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf (the Sahibayn), any interval between two bloods, regardless of duration, is considered part of the hayd/nifas period. This is the default rule: the woman remains in the state of hayd/nifas throughout.
They prioritize the bloods over the purity.
3
State Imam Muhammad's position
Imam Muhammad disagrees: the intervening purity must be evaluated. If it is less than three days, it does not separate the bloods (the whole period remains hayd/nifas). If it is three days or more, then it only separates if the purity duration exceeds both the preceding and following blood periods. Otherwise, it still does not separate.
Muhammad gives weight to the purity if it is substantial.
4
Identify the mufta bihi (operative ruling)
The fatwa is on Imam Muhammad's position. This is the view relied upon for legal practice today.
This tarjih is stated explicitly in the text.
5
Apply the rule to the given examples
Work through the two examples: (1) Hayd: one day blood, eight days purity, one day blood. Under Muhammad, the purity (8 days) exceeds both bloods (1 day each), so it separates; the bloods are not hayd but istihadah. Under Sahibayn, the entire ten days are hayd. (2) Nifas: one day blood, 38 days purity, one day blood. Under Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, only the first blood is nifas; purity and second blood are istihadah. Under Abu Hanifa, all 40 days are nifas because the purity is within the 40-day maximum.
Note the difference between hayd (max 10 days) and nifas (max 40 days).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
الطهر المتخلّلُ بين الدمين في المدّة حيض ونفاس، وأقل الطهر . أي مدة الحيض والنفاس . أي في مدة النفاس الفاصل بين الدمين مختص ومنعهما الجنابة والنفاس إنما أفرد النفاس بعد قوله : وقراءة القرآن ومسه؛ لئلا يتوهم أن ذلك الحكم . بالحيض، فإن النفاس في معناه ألا ترى أنه عليها قال: "لا يمس القرآن إلا الطاهر والطهارة معدومة في النفساء بدليل حرمة وطئها، ثم اعلم أن الحيض فيه اثنا عشر حكماً، أربعة منها تختص بالحيض، وهي: انقضاء العدة، والاستبراء والحكم ،ببلوغها والفصل بين طلاق السنة والبدعة، وثمانية يشترك فيها الحيض والنفاس، وهي: ترك الصلاة لا إلى قضاء، والصوم إلى قضاء، وحرمة الدخول في المسجد، وحرمة الطواف بالبيت، وحرمة قراءة القرآن، وحرمة مس المصحف، وحرمة جماعها والثامن: وجوب الغسل عند انقطاعهما. (مستخلص) والنفاس: إلا قراءة الآيات المشتملة على دعاء أو ذكر، إن كانت بنية الدعاء بتصرم: الصرم: القطع، قال الله تعالى: ﴿لَيَصْرِ مُنَّهَا مُصْبِحِينَ ﴾ (القلم:۱۷)، أي ليقطعن ثمرها والتصرم الانقطاع، ثم في العبارة نظر؛ لأن حل الوطء بعد تمام العشرة لا يتوقف على الانقطاع، بل يحل الوطء بتمام العشرة، سواء انقطع أو لا؛ لأن ما بعدها استحاضة، لكن أخرج الكلام مخرج العادة، فإن تمام العشرة قل ما يخلو عن الانقطاع. (مستخلص) لأكثره: أي بعد عشرة أيام، فاللام بمعنى "بعد" ما في قوله تعالى: ﴿أَقِمِ الصَّلاةَ لِدُلُوكِ الشَّمْسِ﴾ (الإسراء:۷۸) أي بعد دلوكها، وقوله علي : صوموا لرؤيته ، أي بعد رؤيته، وقال زفر والشافعي: توطأ بلا غسل. حتى تغتسل : أي انقطع الدم بعد مضي أقل مدة الحيض قبل تمام العشرة وهو عادتها لا توطأ. (مسكين) أدنى وقت صلاة أي مكتوبة ولهذا قال في "الدر": لو طهرت في وقت العيد لابد أن يمضي وقت الظهر، أي يمضي عليها قدر أن تقدر للاغتسال والتحريمة بأن انقطع في آخر الوقت، أو يمضي عليها وقت صلاة تصير الصلاة ديناً في ذمتها، وفيه إيماء إلى أن المرأة لو كانت نصرانية مثلاً لا يحل وطئها قبل الغسل؛ إذ الصلاة لم تصر ديناً في ذمتها، وفي تخصيص الوطء بالذكر إشارة إلى أن الحكم بطهارة الحائض والنفساء بمضي الوقت المذكور إنما هو في حق الوطء، فأما في قراءة القرآن فلا (فتح) والطهر : أي الحيض الذي هو دم حكماً لا حقيقة.(فتح) الدمين المكتنفين للظهر أعم . من أن يكون في الحيض أو النفاس. (فتح) حيض ونفاس: مطلقا عندهما، وعند محمد: الطهر إذا تخلل بين الدمين في الحيض إن كان أقل من ثلاثة أيام لم يفصل بحال، سواء كان أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما أو لم يكن؛ لأن الدم في موضعه فكان أولى بالاعتبار، وإن كان ثلاثة أيام، فإن كان أقل من الدمين أو مثلهما لم يفصل أيضاً، وإن زاد الطهر عليهما فصل. والفتوى على مذهبه، أحكام الطهر والاستحاضة صورة الحيض: امرأة رأت دما يوماً وطهراً ثمانية أيام ويوماً دماً ثم انقطع فليس شيء من ذلك حيضاً ع عند محمد؛ لأن الطهر غلب الدمين خلافاً لهما، وصورة النفاس رأت بعد الولادة يوماً دماً، وثمانية وثلاثين يوماً طهراً، ويوماً دماً، فالأربعون نفاس عند أبي حنيفة، وعند محمد وأبي يوسف: نفاسها الدم الأول. (فتح، مسكين)
The intervening purity between two bloods in the duration [of hayd and nifas] is hayd and nifas. And the minimum purity [i.e., the duration of hayd and nifas, i.e., in the duration of nifas] is specific to the intervening purity between the two bloods. And janabah and nifas prevent both [i.e., reading Quran and touching Quran]. He only mentioned nifas separately after his statement, lest one think that ruling applies to hayd alone. Indeed, nifas is similar to it. Do you not see that he said: 'No one touches the Quran except the pure.' And purity is absent in the woman in nifas, by evidence of the prohibition of intercourse with her. Then know that hayd has twelve rulings: four are specific to hayd (completion of idda, istibra', ruling of maturity, distinction between sunni and bid'i divorce) and eight are shared between hayd and nifas (abandonment of prayer without make-up, abandonment of fasting with make-up, prohibition of entering mosque, prohibition of tawaf around Kaaba, prohibition of reciting Quran, prohibition of touching mushaf, prohibition of intercourse, and the eighth: obligation of ghusl after cessation). (Mustakhlas) But for nifas: except reciting verses that include supplication or remembrance, if intended as supplication. Tagarrum: cutting. Allah said: 'They will cut its fruit in the morning' (Qalam:17), i.e., they cut its fruit. Tagarrum is cutting. Then in the expression there is consideration; because the permissibility of intercourse after ten complete days does not depend on cessation, rather it is permissible after ten complete days, whether it stops or not; because what comes after is istihadah. But he expressed it in terms of habit, for ten complete days rarely lack cessation. (Mustakhlas) 'Li aktharihi' means after ten days, so the lam is 'after' as in His statement: 'Establish prayer for the declining of the sun' (Isra:78), i.e., after its decline, and his statement: 'Fast for its sighting', i.e., after its sighting. Zufr and Shafi'i said: She may be had intercourse with without ghusl. 'Hatta taghtasil' (until she ghusl) means if blood stopped after minimum hayd before ten days and it is her habit, she may not be had intercourse with. (Miskin) 'Adna waqt salat' means a prescribed prayer. Hence he said in al-Durr: If she becomes pure during the time of Eid, it is necessary that the time of Zuhr pass, i.e., time enough for her to prepare for ghusl and takbirat tahrima if it stopped at the end of the time, or time for a prayer becomes a debt upon her. It implies that if the woman was Christian, for example, intercourse is not permissible before ghusl because prayer did not become a debt upon her. And specifying intercourse indicates that the ruling of purity of the menstruating and postpartum woman by the passing of that time is only regarding intercourse, not regarding recitation of Quran. (Fath) 'al-Tuhr' means hayd which is blood in ruling not reality. (Fath) 'al-damayni al-muktanifayni li al-tuhr' is general, whether in hayd or nifas. (Fath) Hayd and nifas: absolutely according to them [Abu Yusuf and Muhammad], but according to Muhammad: if the intervening purity between two bloods in hayd is less than three days, it does not separate at all, whether it is less than the two bloods or equal or not; because the blood is in its place and thus more deserving of consideration. And if it is three days, then if it is less than the two bloods or equal, it does not separate either. But if the purity exceeds them, it separates. And the fatwa is on his school. The rulings of purity and istihadah: Example of hayd: a woman saw blood for one day, then purity for eight days, then blood for one day, and then it stopped. None of that is hayd according to Muhammad because the purity overcame the two bloods, contrary to them. Example of nifas: she saw after childbirth blood for one day, then purity for 38 days, then blood for one day. According to Abu Hanifa, the 40 days are nifas. According to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, her nifas is the first blood only. (Fath, Miskin)
Source pages p. 45

Commentary
This is a detailed discussion of the intervening purity (tuhr mutakhallil) between two blood episodes in menstruation (hayd) and postpartum bleeding (nifas). The passage opens by stating that such an interval is considered part of hayd or nifas in terms of legal rulings. It then explains that janabah and nifas prevent recitation and touching of the Quran, but nifas is mentioned separately to avoid confusion. The author lists twelve rulings of hayd, four specific to hayd and eight shared with nifas. The text then addresses a critical point: after ten days maximum of hayd, the blood becomes istihadah (irregular bleeding), and intercourse becomes permissible regardless of whether the blood has stopped. This is a point of disagreement: Zufr and al-Shafi'i hold that intercourse is permissible without ghusl, while the Hanafi position requires ghusl after the end of the maximum period. The discussion also includes the condition that if the woman's habit is less than ten days, she must wait until the blood stops and then perform ghusl. The text then delves into the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the intervening purity: According to Sahibayn, any interval between two bloods is considered part of hayd/nifas, regardless of its length. But according to Imam Muhammad, if the interval is less than three days, it does not separate the two bloods; if it is three days or more, it separates only if it exceeds both blood periods. The fatwa (operative ruling) is on Muhammad's position. The passage closes with two examples: one for hayd where purity dominates, making even the blood periods non-menstrual (according to Muhammad), and one for nifas where Abu Hanifa counts the full 40 days as nifas (including the purity interval), while the Sahibayn count only the first blood. The examples are explained in the commentary (Fath, Miskin).

Key Terms
الطهر المتخلل (al-tuhr al-mutakhallil): An interval of purity between two episodes of bleeding (hayd or nifas) that is legally considered part of the menstrual/postpartum state for some rulings.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum; it occurs when bleeding exceeds the maximum duration of hayd (10 days) or nifas (40 days).
الغسل (al-ghusl): Full-body ritual purification required after cessation of hayd or nifas; in this context, it is required before intercourse if the woman's habit has not been exceeded.
الفتوى على مذهبه (al-fatwa cala madhhabihi): The fatwa is on his school (i.e., Imam Muhammad's position is the operative ruling).

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi mufta bihi, what is the ruling on an intervening purity of 3 days between two bloods of 2 days each?
A) The purity separates them, so the bloods are separate hayd periods.
B) The purity does not separate them because it does not exceed both bloods.
C) The purity is considered hayd.
D) The entire period is istihadah.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi mufta bihi on intervening purity: an interval of purity separates two bloods only if it is three days or more and exceeds both the preceding and following blood periods; otherwise, the entire span is considered one continuous hayd or nifas period.

Taharah — Purification

Minimum Purity Interval and the Ruling of Istihadah
Rulings on minimum purity and definition of istihadah

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the minimum purity interval between two hayd periods, identify the proof, and apply the Hanafi definition of istihadah to determine whether a woman must pray and fast.

Core Idea
Istihadah is like a runny nose – it does not stop prayer, fasting, or marriage.

In this lesson, we examine the fundamental ruling that a woman experiencing chronic bleeding (istihadah) is not excused from worship. We begin by establishing the minimum interval of purity between two menstrual periods, which is 15 days by consensus, and then define istihadah as blood that falls short of or exceeds normal menstrual cycles. Understanding these boundaries is essential to distinguishing between menstruation and non‑menstrual bleeding.

Guided Path
1
Identify the minimum purity interval
The text states that the minimum interval between two hayd periods is 15 days. Identify the proof: ijma of the Companions and a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri.
The hadith is considered sound despite minor criticism.
2
Define istihadah
Istihadah is blood that is less than the minimum of hayd (3 days) or exceeds the maximum (10 days for hayd, 40 for nifas). Recognize that it is categorized separately from hayd.
The text likens it to a persistent nosebleed.
3
State the ruling on worship during istihadah
Istihadah does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. The hadith 'Perform wudu and pray even if blood drops on the mat' explicitly establishes prayer; the other rulings are derived by indication.
This applies regardless of the amount or duration of bleeding.
4
Apply the ruling to a scenario
Given a woman who bleeds for 12 days, classify the blood beyond 10 as istihadah. She must pray and fast on days 11–12.
This distinguishes her from a menstruating woman who abstains from prayer.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

(ط،ع) نصب العادة استثناء من قوله ولا حد لأكثره ، يعني إذا استمر بها الدم واحتيج إلى نصب العادة لانقضاء العدة وغيرها، فعند أبي عصمة: لا يقدر طهرها بشيء، وعند عامة العلماء: طهرها مقدر، واعلم أن هذا شامل لثلاث مسائل : الأولى : امرأة بلغت مستحاضة، فيقدر حيضها بعشرة من كل شهر، وباقيه طهر، والثانية: امرأة لها عادة في الطهر والحيض ثم استمر بها الدم فحيضها وطهرها ما رأت من قبل، وعدتها بحسبه، والثالثة: مسألة وتسمى المتحيرة، وهي صاحب العادة إذا استمر دمها، وقد نسيت أيام حيضها أولها وآخرها، ودورها في كل شهر، فإنها تتحرى وتمضي على أكثر رأيها وحاصله أنها متى تيقنت بالحيض في وقت تركت العبادة؛ وإلا تحرّت، فإن لم يستقر رأيها على شيء، بل ترددت بين الحيض والطهر توضأت لكل صلاة، وهو الأصح، ولا توطأ بالتحري وتصوم رمضان ثم تقضي عشرين يوماً إن علمت أن ابتداءه ليلاً؛ لجواز أن حيضها في كل شهر عشرة أيام، فإن قضت عشرة يجوز حصولها في الحيض فتقضي عشرة أخرى، وإن علمته نهاراً قضت اثنين وعشرين يوماً؛ لأن أكثر ما فسد من صومها في الشهر أحد عشر يوماً، فتقضي ضعفه احتياطاً، وإن لم تعلم شيئاً مع التردد المذكور فعامة المشايخ على العشرين، وقيل: اثنين وعشرين احتياطا الجواز أن يكون بالنهار، ويقدر طهرها في حق انقضاء العدة بشهرين وعليه الفتوى. (فتح ملخصا) المضللة الاستمرار أي استمرار الدم فيقدر طهرها للضرورة بشهرين وعليه الفتوى فتنقضي عدتها بسبعة أشهر. ودم الاستحاضة: هو الذي ينقص عن ثلاثة أيام أو تزيد على عشرة أو على أكثر النفاس. رمز الحقائق: ٣٦/١] وصلاة: لقوله عليه: "توضئي وصلي وإن قطر الدم على الحصير" فثبت به حكم الصلاة، وحكم الوطء والصوم دلالة رمز الحقائق: ٣٦/١] والنفاس أي وأكثر أيام النفاس، ولها عادة أقل من الأكثر. (ط)
Fifteen days, and there is no limit for its maximum except for the setting of a habit in time of continuity. For the sake of completing the idda. And blood of istihadah is like a persistent nosebleed; it does not prevent fasting, prayer, or intercourse. And if the blood exceeds the maximum of hayd or nifas, then what exceeds her habit (is istihadah). Example of hayd: a woman saw blood for one day, purity for eight days, then blood for one day, and then it stopped. None of that is hayd according to Muhammad because the purity overcame the two bloods, contrary to them. Example of nifas: she saw after childbirth blood for one day, then purity for 38 days, then blood for one day. According to Abu Hanifa, the 40 days are nifas. According to Muhammad and Abu Yusuf, her nifas is only the first blood. (Fath, Miskin) Fifteen days by consensus of the Companions; because it is the duration of necessity, so it became like the duration of residence. Abu Twala narrated from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and Ja'far ibn Muhammad from his father from his grandfather that he said: 'The minimum of hayd is three, its maximum is ten, and the minimum between two hayd periods is fifteen days.' The hadith, though al-'Ayni said: there is speech about it, is safe from criticism. (Fath) And there is no limit because it may extend for years and may consume a lifetime, so it cannot be estimated. Then she prays and performs as long as there is purity. (T, A) 'Nasb al-'adah' (setting the habit) is an exception to his statement 'and there is no limit for its maximum', meaning if bleeding continues and needs to set a habit for idda etc., then according to Abu 'Ismah: her purity is not estimated by anything, and according to the generality of scholars: her purity is estimated. Know that this includes three issues: First: a woman who reaches puberty as a mustahadah, so her hayd is estimated as ten days each month, and the rest is purity. Second: a woman who has a habit of purity and hayd, then bleeding continues, so her hayd and purity are what she saw before, and her idda is accordingly. Third: the case called al-mutahayyirah (the confused one), who has a habit but bleeding continues and she has forgotten her hayd days, its beginning and end, and its cycle each month. She must make a reasonable estimation (taharr) and proceed on her strongest opinion. In short, whenever she is certain of hayd at a time, she leaves worship; otherwise she estimates. If she cannot settle on an opinion but fluctuates between hayd and purity, she performs wudu for each prayer—this is the most correct—and she is not to be had intercourse with by estimation, and she fasts Ramadan, then makes up twenty days if she knows it began at night; because it is possible her hayd each month is ten days, so if she made up ten, it may have occurred in hayd, so she makes up another ten. If she knows it began during the day, she makes up twenty-two days; because the maximum spoiled from her fast in a month is eleven days, so she makes up double as precaution. If she knows nothing with the mentioned fluctuation, then the majority of mashayikh are on twenty, and it is said: twenty-two as precaution because it could be during the day. And her purity is estimated for idda as two months, and upon this is the fatwa. (Fath summarized) 'al-Mudallalah'? (Mudallalah means the one confused?) Continuation means the bleeding continues, so her purity is estimated for necessity as two months, and upon this is the fatwa. So her idda ends with seven months. And blood of istihadah: it is what is less than three days or exceeds ten days or exceeds the maximum of nifas. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 36/1) And prayer: because of his saying: 'Perform wudu and pray even if blood drops on the mat.' So the ruling of prayer is established by text, and the rulings of intercourse and fasting are established by indication. (Ramz al-Haqa'iq 36/1) And nifas i.e., the maximum days of nifas, and she has a habit less than the maximum. (T)
Source pages p. 46

Commentary
This passage focuses on two key rulings: the minimum interval of purity between two menstrual periods (15 days, by ijma of the Companions) and the detailed rules of istihadah (chronic bleeding). The 15-day minimum is supported by a hadith from Abu Sa'id al-Khudri and has no maximum limit except when a habit must be established for idda purposes. The text then defines istihadah as blood that falls short of the minimum (3 days) or exceeds the maximum (10 for hayd, 40 for nifas). Istihadah is likened to a persistent nosebleed: it does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse. The discussion moves to three scenarios of mustahadah (chronic bleeder): (1) a girl who reaches puberty as a mustahadah—her hayd is estimated as 10 days per month, with the rest purity; (2) a woman with established habit who then experiences continuous bleeding—her hayd and purity remain as per her prior habit; (3) the perplexed woman (mutahayyirah) who has forgotten her habit—she must rely on cautious estimation, performing wudu for each prayer, and making up fasts with extra days as a precaution. For idda, her purity is estimated as two months, so her idda ends after seven months (three periods of purity?). The text also clarifies that the hadith about wudu and prayer for the mustahadah explicitly establishes the ruling for prayer, and by indication for intercourse and fasting. Rulings from nifas (maximum days) and smaller habit are also mentioned.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustahadah): A woman who experiences chronic bleeding (istihadah) that is not menstrual or postpartum.
الاستحاضة (istihadah): Chronic vaginal bleeding that is not menstrual or postpartum, resulting from a vein rupture in the uterus.

Key Terms from Source Passage

C) 20 days
D) There is no minimum.

Key Takeaway
The minimum purity interval is 15 days, and istihadah does not prevent prayer, fasting, or intercourse.

Rulings for the Mustahadah: Three Scenarios and Estimation
Detailed rules for mustahadah, including three scenarios and estimation for idda

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish the three scenarios of mustahadah and apply the rules of estimation for prayer, fasting, and idda.

Core Idea
A confused mustahadah makes wudu for each prayer and makes up 20 days of fasting – because precaution beats uncertainty.

When bleeding becomes continuous, the Hanafi school provides detailed guidance based on whether the woman has a known habit, is a new case, or has forgotten her habit. These scenarios involve estimation (tagdir) and precaution (ihtiyat). In this lesson, we unpack the three cases and the rules for her prayers, fasts, and idda.

Guided Path
1
Recognize the three scenarios of mustahadah
The text lists: (1) a woman who reaches puberty already experiencing istihadah; (2) a woman with an established habit who then becomes mustahadah; (3) the confused woman (mutahayyirah) who has forgotten her habit.
The first two are simpler; the third requires the most precaution.
2
Apply the rule for estimation of hayd and purity
For scenario 1: her hayd is estimated as 10 days per month, the rest is purity. For scenario 2: her hayd and purity are what she observed before the continuous bleeding. For scenario 3: she must make a reasonable estimation (taharr) and act on her strongest opinion.
If no opinion prevails, she is in a state of continuous fluctuation.
3
Determine the rulings for prayer and fasting
She performs wudu for each prayer (al-asahh). She fasts Ramadan normally, then makes up fasts. The number depends on whether she knows the bleeding started at night (20 make-up days) or during the day (22 make-up days). If unknown, the fatwa is 20 days.
The precaution is to double the potential missed days.
4
Calculate idda for the mustahadah
For idda, her purity is estimated as two months (60 days). Therefore, her idda ends after three such purity intervals? Actually, the text says idda ends with seven months, meaning she must observe three purity periods of two months each? The fatwa: purity estimated as two months, so idda ends after three purities = 6 months? Wait text says seven months. Reason: First two months maybe is one purity? Clarify: The estimation of purity for idda is two months. So if she has to wait three purities (three months? No, the text says 'sebaat ashhur' i.e. seven months). Probably: one purity period is two months, so three purities = six months, plus the initial hayd? Actually, we need not dive too deep here; just state the fatwa.
The fatwa: purity estimated as two months; idda ends at seven months.
5
Apply the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on the example of nifas
The text gives an example: a woman sees blood for one day after birth, then 38 days purity, then blood again. Abu Hanifa says all 40 days (first blood + pure + second blood) are nifas. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad say only the first blood is nifas. This shows the principle that purity can overcome two bloods in Muhammad's view.
The example illustrates the rule 'if purity overcomes the bloods, then neither is considered hayd/nifas' according to Muhammad.

Distinguishing Hayd from Istihadah: Women with and without a Habit
Ruling on istihadah and definitions for women with and without habit

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to define istihadah, apply the Hanafi rules for distinguishing hayd from istihadah for women with and without a habit, and state the maximum durations for hayd and nifas.

Core Idea
Hayd has a maximum of ten days; any blood beyond that or beyond a woman's established habit is istihadah.

This lesson unpacks the Hanafi rules for identifying istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). The passage first gives a summary ruling for a beginner (mubtadi'ah) and for those with continuous impurities, then details how to classify bleeding for women with a regular habit and those without. Understanding these distinctions is crucial for determining when a woman must perform wudu (but not ghusl) and when she can pray and fast.

Guided Path
1
Identify the legal categories
Recognize the three categories: hayd (menstruation), istihadah (chronic bleeding), and nifas (postpartum bleeding). The passage defines them by duration and habit.
2
Analyze the rule for women with a habit (dhat al-'adah)
If a woman has a regular habit (e.g., 7 days), any blood beyond that habit but within 10 days is hayd; if she exceeds 10 days, the excess over 10 is istihadah. The same principle applies to nifas with a 40-day maximum.
The habit can be established by two consistent cycles (original) or by one cycle according to Abu Yusuf.
3
Analyze the rule for a beginner (mubtadi'ah)
For a woman experiencing menstruation for the first time, her hayd is fixed at 10 days maximum. If she bleeds beyond 10, the excess is istihadah.
The Hanafi ruling differs from the Shafi'i school which holds either one day and night or the custom of her female relatives.
4
Understand the types of habit
The passage distinguishes between an original habit (two consistent cycles) and an established habit (different cycles). This affects how we determine her current hayd if bleeding becomes irregular.
Abu Yusuf's view that habit is established after one occurrence leads to different calculations.
5
Apply to other continuous impurities
The same wudu requirement applies to mustahadah and those with chronic urine drip, intestinal gas, etc. They must make wudu for each fard time and can pray both fard and nafl with that wudu.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
أحكام الطهر والاستحاضة: استحاضة، ولو مبتدأة فحيضها عشرة ونفاسها أربعون وتتوضأ المستحاضة، ومن به كانت المرأة من كل شهر سلس البول، أو استطلاق البطن، أو انفلات ريح، أو رعاف دائم، أو جرح لا يرقأ لوقت كل فرض، ويصلون به فرضا ونقلا، لا يسكن ولا ينقطع
استحاضة: هذا في حق ذات العادة، مثلاً إذا كان عادتها كل شهر سبعة أيام، فرأت اثني عشر يوماً، فالزائد على السبعة استحاضة، وكذلك إذا كانت أربعة أو خمسة أو ستة، وتجاوزت العشرة بيوم وما فوقه، فالزائد استحاضة وإن لم يتجاوز عن العشرة فالكل حيض، وكذلك في النفاس إذا كانت عادتها خمسة وثلاثين يوماً مثلاً، فرأت خمسة وأربعين يوماً، فالعشرة استحاضة. 
مبتدأة بكسر الدال وفتحها اسم فاعل أو مفعول أي المرأة التي ابتدأت الحيض، أو الحيض ابتدأها، فحيضها عشرة أيام، وقال الشافعي في قول حيضها يوم وليلة، وفي قول: يعتبر حيضها بنساء عشيرتها، ثم اعلم أن العادة في المبتدأة أيضاً نوعان: أصلية وجعلية فالأولى: أن ترى دمين وطهرين متفقين متواليين، كما إذا رأت ثلاثة دماً وخمسة عشر طهراً ثم رأت كذلك، ثم استمر بها الدم، والثانية: أن ترى دمين وطهرين مختلفين، فعند أبي يوسف: أيام حيضها وطهرها هو المرئي أولاً، وهذا القول مبني على أن العادة تثبت عنده بمرة، واختلف على قولهما، فقيل: هو كقول الثاني، وقيل: أقل المرئيين. 
أربعون يوماً، والزائد على العشرة في الحيض وعلى الأربعين في النفاس استحاضة.
The Book of Purification. Rulings of purity and istihadah: Istihadah, and if she is a beginner, her hayd is ten and her nifas is forty, and the mustahadah performs wudu, and whoever suffers from continuous dribbling of urine, or intestinal incontinence, or passing wind, or persistent nosebleed, or a wound that does not stop bleeding, he performs wudu for the time of every fard, and they pray with it fard and nafl, it does not stop nor cease. Istihadah: This applies to one with a habit. For example, if her habit is seven days each month, and she sees twelve days, then the excess over seven is istihadah. Similarly if her habit is four, five, or six, and she exceeds ten by a day or more, the excess is istihadah; if she does not exceed ten, all is hayd. Similarly in nifas, if her habit is thirty-five days, and she sees forty-five, then the ten [excess] is istihadah. 'Mubtadi'ah' (beginner): with kasr or fatha of the dal, ism fa'il or maf'ul, i.e., the woman who began menstruation, or menstruation began her; her hayd is ten days. Al-Shafi'i said in one opinion her hayd is a day and a night, and in another opinion it is based on the women of her tribe. Know that the habit for the beginner is also of two types: original and established. The first: that she sees two bloods and two pure periods that are consistent and consecutive, like if she sees three days blood and fifteen days purity, and then sees similarly, then the blood continues. The second: that she sees two bloods and two pure periods that are different. According to Abu Yusuf, her days of hayd and purity are what she saw first. This opinion is based on the principle that habit is established with one occurrence. There is disagreement on his two companions: it is said he holds like the second, and it is said the lesser of the two seen. Forty days, and the excess over ten in hayd and over forty in nifas is istihadah.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage opens the section on istihadah (chronic non-menstrual bleeding). The text first gives a summary: a beginner (mubtadi'ah) has a maximum hayd of ten days and nifas of forty days. The mustahadah and others with continuous invalidators (like urine drip, intestinal gas, etc.) must make wudu specifically for the time of each obligatory prayer, and with that wudu they may pray both fard and nafl. The main body then defines istihadah for a woman with a regular habit (dhat al-'adah). If she sees blood beyond her normal habit, even if within ten days, the excess is istihadah. But if she exceeds ten days overall, the excess over ten is istihadah. The same principle applies to nifas: the habit is considered; if she exceeds forty days, the excess is istihadah. Next, the text explains the term 'mubtadi'ah' (beginner) linguistically and legally. According to the Hanafi school, her hayd is exactly ten days. This differs from Imam al-Shafi'i who holds either one day and night or the custom of her female relatives. The passage then elaborates on the types of habit for a beginner: original (two consistent cycles) and established (different cycles). Abu Yusuf's view is that the habit is established after one occurrence, and there is further detail on how to determine her days. Finally, it reiterates the maximum limits: excess over ten in hayd and over forty in nifas is istihadah.

Key Terms
استحاضة (istihādah): Continuous vaginal bleeding that is not menstrual; occurs when bleeding exceeds the maximum hayd or a woman's habit.
مبتدأة (mubtadi'ah): A woman who experiences menstruation for the first time.
العادة (al-'ādah): The regular pattern of menstruation in terms of duration and timing, established by at least two observations.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If a mubtadi'ah (beginner) sees blood for nine days, how is it classified according to the Hanafi school?
A) All nine days are hayd because it is within ten days.
B) The first day and night are hayd, the rest is istihadah.
C) It depends on the custom of her female relatives.
D) The first three days are hayd, the rest is istihadah.

Key Takeaway
The key is to understand that istihadah is any blood beyond the woman's habit or the maximum (10 for hayd, 40 for nifas).

Wudu for the Mustahadah: Scope and Proof
Ruling with proof on wudu scope for excused persons

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on how many prayers a mustahadah may pray with one wudu, identify the dalil, and explain the Hanafi rebuttal to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
A mustahadah's wudu suffices for all prayers within one time period – the evidence is unambiguous.

The mustahadah (woman with chronic non-menstrual bleeding) and those with similar conditions like urine incontinence face a continuous state of hadath. This lesson clarifies how the Hanafi school derives the ruling that one wudu serves for multiple fard and nafl prayers within a single prayer time, based on a clear prophetic command. We also examine the Shafi'i counter-argument and the Hanafi response.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage rules that the mustahadah performs wudu for each fard time (li-waqti kulli fard). Note that this wudu is restricted to wudu only – istinja' is not required. Determine the hukm level: is this wudu obligatory (wajib) or recommended?
The command 'tawadda'ī' (perform wudu) indicates obligation in Hanafi usul.
2
Locate the dalil
The author cites the hadith: 'Tawadda'ī li-waqti kulli ṣalāh' (Perform wudu for the time of every prayer). Identify the type of dalil (Quran, Sunnah, etc.) and its transmission and meaning certainty.
This is a hadith ahad, zanni al-thubut but considered qati' al-dalala in the Hanafi view.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah
The key phrase is 'li-waqti kulli ṣalāh'. The lam (lām) is interpreted as 'for the time of' linking wudu to the time period, not to each individual prayer. This yields the ruling: one wudu per time suffices for all prayers within that time.
The Hanafis argue this version is muhkam (unambiguous) compared to the variant 'li-kulli ṣalāh'.
4
Analyze the Shafi'i objection and Hanafi response
Imam al-Shafi'i relies on the hadith to Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh: 'Tawadda'ī li-kulli ṣalāh' (wudu for every prayer). The Hanafis respond that 'li-kulli ṣalāh' is ambiguous – the lam can be borrowed for time – so it is interpreted in light of the unambiguous version.
This is a classic example of handling conflicting narrations: the muhkam (unambiguous) overrides the mutashabih (ambiguous).
5
Determine the practical consequence (thamarah al-khilaf)
A mustahadah who performs wudu at the start of Dhuhr time can pray Dhuhr, Asr, and any nafl with that same wudu according to Hanafi. According to Shafi'i, she would need a new wudu for Asr. This difference affects daily practice.
Note: Imam Malik's view that wudu is also required for nafl is noted but not the mufta bihi.

Source Text

سلس البول: السلس بفتح اللام نفس الخارج، وبكسرها الذي لا ينقطع تقاطر بوله؛ لضعف مثانته أو لغلبة البرودة. رمز الحقائق: ۳۷/۱] لوقت كل فرض متعلق بقوله تتوضأ وعند الشافعي: لكل فرض؛ لقوله عليها لفاطمة بنت أبي حبيش: "توضئي لكل صلاة"، ولنا قوله عليها للمستحاضة: "تتوضأ لوقت كل صلاة" وهو المراد بالأول؛ لأن اللام تستعار للوقت فكان الأخذ بما روينا أولى؛ لأنه محكم وما رواه الشافعي محتمل، فحملناه على المحكم، وعند مالك: تتوضأ لكل نفل أيضاً. (فتح المعين) ويصلون به إلخ أي يصلون بذلك الوضوء ما شاؤوا من الفرائض والنوافل، وقال الشافعي: ليس لهم أن يصلوا به إلا فرضا واحدا، ولهم أن يصلوا من النفل ما شاؤوا؛ لأنه تبع للفرض [تبيين الحقائق: ۱۸۱/۱]
And the mustahadah performs wudu — restricted to wudu because istinja' (washing the private parts) is not obligatory upon her. Similarly for one with intestinal incontinence or continuous dripping of urine. And they differed concerning washing the garment: some said she should wash it for every prayer, some said no. The chosen position for fatwa is that if it is such that if she washes it, it would become impure before finishing the prayer, then it is not permissible to omit washing it; otherwise it is permissible. And by 'wudu' is meant purification (taharah) to include tayammum; he mentioned wudu because it is the nobler of the two types. 'Sals al-bawl' (dribbling urine): with fathah on the lam is the actual outflow; with kasrah is the person whose urine drips continuously due to weakness of the bladder or predominance of cold. 'For the time of every fard' is attached to 'she performs wudu'. According to al-Shafi'i, it is for every fard due to his statement (peace be upon him) to Fatimah bint Abi Hubaysh: 'Perform wudu for every prayer.' Our proof is his statement (peace be upon him) to the mustahadah: 'Perform wudu for the time of every prayer.' And this is what is meant by the first (narration), because the lam (in 'li-kulli salat') can be borrowed for time, so adopting what we narrated is better because it is unambiguous (muhkam), and what al-Shafi'i narrated is probable, so we interpret it in light of the unambiguous. According to Malik, she performs wudu for every nafl as well. 'And they pray with it, etc.' means they pray with that wudu as many fards and nafls as they wish. Al-Shafi'i said: they may not pray with it except one fard, but they may pray as many nafls as they wish because they are subsidiary to the fard.
Source pages p. 47

Commentary
This passage is a commentary (sharh) expanding the ruling that the mustahadah and those with similar chronic conditions perform wudu for each fard time. It clarifies that istinja' is not obligatory for the mustahadah because the bleeding is continuous and washing would be futile. The text then discusses the garment: the preferred view is that if washing the garment would not prevent further contamination during prayer, it is not required to wash it for each prayer. The term 'wudu' here includes tayammum if water is unavailable or harmful. A definition of 'sals al-bawl' is given. The crux of the dispute with al-Shafi'i concerns the wording of the hadith: the Hanafi school relies on the version 'for the time of every prayer' (li-waqti kulli salat) which is considered unambiguous (muhkam), versus Shafi'i's version 'for every prayer' (li-kulli salat). The Hanafis interpret the latter as meaning the same but bearing a possible alternative meaning. Consequently, with one wudu, the mustahadah can pray multiple fard prayers within one time period, as long as the wudu is not invalidated by exit of the time (as discussed in the next lesson). Malik's opinion that she must also perform wudu for nafl prayers is noted. Finally, the passage mentions that according to Shafi'i, one wudu suffices for only one fard and multiple nafls, while the Hanafi position is that the same wudu suffices for any number of prayers within the time.

Key Terms
المستحاضة (al-mustaḥāḍah): A woman experiencing chronic non-menstrual bleeding (istihadah).
سلس البول (sals al-bawl): Continuous dribbling of urine due to a medical condition.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the basis for the ruling that a mustahadah may pray multiple fard prayers with one wudu?
A) The hadith 'Tawadda'ī li-kulli ṣalāh'.
B) The hadith 'Tawadda'ī li-waqti kulli ṣalāh'.
C) Analogy to the regular wudu.
D) Consensus of the companions.

Key Takeaway
A mustahadah's wudu is per time period, not per prayer – one wudu suffices for all prayers within that time.

When Does the Ma'dhur's Wudu Become Invalid?
Intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf on invalidation of wudu for the excused

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the three Hanafi positions on when the wudu of an excused person becomes invalid and apply the mufta bihi (exit of time) to practical scenarios.

Core Idea
The ma'dhur's wudu is tied to the prayer time; it ends at exit, not entry.

The excused person (ma'dhur) faces a continuous invalidator of wudu, such as urine drip or constant gas. The Hanafi school agrees that his wudu is linked to the prayer time, but a notable intra-madhhab dispute exists about the precise moment it becomes invalid. This lesson unpacks the three positions, their rationales, and the practical consequences for daily worship.

Guided Path
1
Identify the excused person
Define who qualifies as ma'dhur: someone who experiences a continuous invalidator of wudu such that they never have a clean period long enough to perform wudu and pray a fard salat without the invalidator occurring.
This condition is a prerequisite for all the positions discussed.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the three views: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad – invalidated by exit of the prayer time; Zufar – invalidated by entry of the next prayer time; Abu Yusuf – invalidated by both entry and exit.
The majority (Imam & Muhammad) is the relied-upon view.
3
Trace the reasoning behind each position
For each view, understand the legal analogy: Imam uses the idea that time is a substitute for performance; Zufar emphasizes that need arises only at entry; Abu Yusuf restricts need to the time boundaries.
Refer to the hanafi_position_box for detailed proofs.
4
Apply the practical difference
Work through concrete scenarios: wudu for Fajr (invalid at sunrise according to majority, remains valid till Dhuhr entry according to Zufar); wudu before zawal for Duha (usable for Dhuhr according to Imam and Muhammad, not according to others).
This step reveals the thamarah al-khilaf (practical fruit of the dispute).

Source Text

فقط: أي عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند زفر بالدخول، وعند أبي يوسف بخروج الوقت ودخوله معا، وجه مذهب الإمام ومحمد أن الوقت أقيم مقام الأداء شرعا، فلا بد من تقديم الطهارة على الأداء حقيقة؛ ولأن الشارع أجاز إشغال الوقت كله بالأداء، ولا يمكن ذلك إلا بتقديم الطهارة، ولأبي يوسف: أن الحاجة مقصورة على الوقت فلا تعتبر قبل الوقت ولا بعده، ولزفر : اعتبار الطهارة مع المنافي للحاجة إلى الأداء، ولا حاجة قبل الوقت، والمراد بالبطلان من الخروج ظهور الحدث السابق عند خروج الوقت، فإضافة البطلان إليه مجاز؛ لأنه لا تأثير للخروج في الانتقاض حقيقة. وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيمن توضأ وقت الفجر يبطل بطلوع الشمس عند علمائنا الثلاثة، أي الإمام وصاحبيه؛ لأنه خرج الوقت بطلوعها خلافاً لزفر، لأن البطلان عنده دخول الوقت ولم يوجد؛ فلهذا لا يبطل، سبب ولو توضاً قبل الزوال ولو لعيد أو صلاة ضحى يصلي الظهر عندهما؛ لعدم خروج وقت صلاة مكتوبة، فإنه المراد بالوقت على الأصح، خلافاً لأبي يوسف وزفر؛ لوجود دخول الوقت، ولو توضأ للظهر في وقته وصلاه، ثم توضأ في وقت الظهر للعصر لا يصلي به العصر عند الكل، أما عند أبي يوسف وزفر فلوجود دخول الوقت، وكذا عند الإمام ومحمد على الأصح؛ لأن هذه طهارة وقعت للظهر حتى لو ظهر فساد الظهر جاز له أداؤها بها، فلا تبقى بعد خروج وقت الظهر، وفي رواية له أن يصلي به العصر؛ لأن وضوءه للعصر في وقت الظهر کوضوئه للظهر قبل الزوال. (فتح، مسكين مع تغير) يوجد فيه: [ أي في ذلك الوقت، وهذا شرط ثبوت العذر، يعني لا يجد في وقت الصلاة زماناً يتوضأ ويصلّي فيه الحدث، وشرط انقطاع العذر خلو وقت كامل عنه (ط)] وإذا طرأ العذر في خلال الوقت قبل صلاة فرضه ينتظر إلى آخر الوقت، فإذا لم ينقطع صلّى قبل خروج الوقت، فإذا دخل الوقت الثاني وانقطع ودام الانقطاع إلى وقت صلاة أخرى توضأ وأعاد الصلاة؛ لأن بدوام انقطاع العذر وقتاً كاملاً تبين أنه صحيح صلى صلاة المعذورين، وإن لم ينقطع وقت الصلاة الثانية حتى خرج الوقت جازت الصلاة. تتمة: يجب رد عذره أو تقليله ما أمكن ولو بصلاته مؤمياً، يعني بأنه لو كان بحيث لو جلس لا يسيل ولو قام يسيل يجلس ،وجوبا، وبرده لا يبقى ذا عذر بخلاف الحائض؛ لأن اتصافها بالحيض لا ينفك عنها في المدة، وإن انقطع في بعض الأوقات. (كذا في الدرر والبحر)
And it (the wudu) is invalidated only by its exit (of the time), and this is when no time of fard passes except that the event (invalidator) occurs in it. Meaning their wudu [is for] the time. Meaning the ruling of the excused ones. From the prayer with which he is afflicted. Explanation of nifas. And nifas is blood that follows (childbirth). By its exit. Means. 'Only': i.e., according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad. According to Zufar, by its entry. According to Abu Yusuf, by both exit and entry together. The reasoning of the imam and Muhammad is that the time has been legally set as a substitute for performance, so purification must precede performance in reality; and because the Lawgiver allowed occupying the entire time with performance, and that is only possible by preceding purification. According to Abu Yusuf: need is restricted to the time, so it is not considered before or after. According to Zufar: purification is considered only when there is a conflicting need to perform, and there is no need before the time. The intended meaning of 'invalidated by exit' is the appearance of the prior event at the exit of time; attributing invalidation to exit is metaphorical because exit has no real effect on nullification. The practical consequence of this difference appears in one who performed wudu at the time of Fajr: it is invalidated at sunrise according to our three scholars (i.e., the Imam and his two companions) because the time exits with sunrise, contrary to Zufar, because invalidation in his view is at entry of time and that did not occur; so it does not invalidate. And if one performed wudu before zawal even for Eid or Duha prayer, he can pray Dhuhr according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad) because no time of an obligatory prayer has exited; that is the intended meaning of 'time' according to the most correct view, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Zufar due to entry of time. And if one performed wudu for Dhuhr in its time and prayed it, then he performed wudu in Dhuhr time for Asr, he cannot pray Asr with it according to all. According to Abu Yusuf and Zufar due to entry of time, and likewise according to the Imam and Muhammad in the correct view because this purification was for Dhuhr such that if Dhuhr becomes invalid, he may perform it with it, so it does not remain after exit of Dhuhr time. In one transmission from him (Abu Hanifa) he may pray Asr with it because his wudu for Asr in Dhuhr time is like his wudu for Dhuhr before zawal. 'Yujadu fihi': i.e., in that time, and this is the condition for establishing the excuse, meaning he does not find in the prayer time a period to perform wudu and pray without the event. And the condition for cessation of the excuse is a complete time free from it. And if the excuse arises during the time before his fard prayer, he waits until the end of the time; if it does not cease, he prays before the time exits. Then if the second time enters and it ceases and the cessation lasts until another prayer time, he performs wudu and repeats the prayer because by the continuous cessation for a complete time, it becomes clear that he prayed the prayer of the excused correctly. And if it does not cease during the second prayer time until the time exits, the prayer is valid. Supplement: He must prevent or reduce his excuse as much as possible, even by praying with gestures (imu'an), meaning if he is such that if he sits it does not flow and if he stands it flows, he sits (obligatorily). By preventing it, he is no longer excused, unlike a menstruating woman because her description of menstruation does not separate from her during the period, even if it stops at times.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is a commentary that delves into an intra-Hanafi dispute about when exactly the wudu of an excused person (sahib al-'udhr) becomes invalid. The base ruling says it is invalidated by 'its exit' meaning the exit of the prayer time. Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that the wudu ends with the exit of the time for which it was performed. Zufar holds it is invalidated by the entry of the next time. Abu Yusuf holds both exit and entry together. The reasoning: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad analogize the time to the performance itself; since the Lawgiver allows the entire time to be used for prayer, the purification must precede the prayer and thus is tied to the time. Abu Yusuf argues that the need is only during the time, so it is not valid before or after. Zufar says purification is only needed when there is an actual need to perform, which arises only at the entry of the time. The practical effect is illustrated: if one performs wudu at Fajr time, it becomes invalid at sunrise according to Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf (due to exit), but Zufar says it remains valid because the next time (Dhuhr) has not entered. Similarly, wudu before zawal for Eid or Duha can be used for Dhuhr according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad because no fard time has exited, but Abu Yusuf and Zufar reject because a new time has entered. If one performs wudu for Dhuhr, prays it, then performs another wudu in Dhuhr time intending Asr, that wudu is not valid for Asr; the consensus is that it is for Dhuhr only, but there is a transmission that Abu Hanifa allowed it. The passage then discusses conditions for the excuse to be established: one must not have a gap in the time sufficient to perform wudu and pray without the invalidator. If the excuse occurs during a time, one waits until the end; if it does not cease, one prays anyway. If it ceases for a full time, one must repeat the previous prayer. Finally, it notes that one must minimize the excuse (e.g., by sitting if sitting prevents flow). This is different from a menstruating woman because her state persists even if bleeding stops temporarily.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhūr): A person with a continuous invalidator of wudu (like urine drip, gas, etc.) such that they never have a clean period long enough to pray.
خروج الوقت (khurūj al-waqt): The exit of the prayer time; the moment when the time for a particular fard ends.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi (relied-upon) Hanafi position, what invalidates the wudu of an excused person?
A) The entry of the next prayer time.
B) The exit of the current prayer time.
C) The occurrence of a new invalidator.
D) The completion of the prayer.

Key Takeaway
The wudu of an excused person is time-bound; the majority Hanafi view holds it becomes invalid at the exit of the prayer time, not at entry or by a new invalidator.

The Linguistic and Legal Definition of Nifas
Defining nifas linguistically and legally

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the linguistic and legal definitions of nifas and distinguish it from pre-birth bleeding.

Core Idea
Nifas is blood that follows childbirth — bleeding before birth is not nifas.

In this lesson, we examine the foundational definition of nifas (postpartum bleeding). The text provides both the linguistic root and the precise legal meaning. Understanding this definition is crucial because it determines the rulings that apply to a woman after childbirth, such as the maximum duration of forty days and the prohibition of prayer and fasting.

Guided Path
1
Identify the linguistic root
Analyze the derivation from the verb 'nafisat' (to give birth) and its connection to 'nafs' (blood).
The term originates from the same root as 'blood'.
2
State the legal definition
The text defines nifas legally as 'blood that follows the child' (دم يعقب الولد).
3
Note the nominalization
Nifas is an ism al-masdar (verbal noun) like hayd, indicating it is a category of blood.
This parallels the term for menstruation.
4
Distinguish from similar terms
Nifas is exclusively post-birth; bleeding before birth (even if close to delivery) is not nifas but istihadah or other.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنفاس: لغة: بالكسر من "نفست "المرأة بضم النون وفتحها إذا ولدت فهي نفساء، وهو من النفس يعني الدم، وشرعاً: "دم يعقب الولد" تسمية بالمصدر كالحيض.
And nifas: linguistically, with kasrah on the nun, from 'nafisat' (with dammah and fathah on the nun) meaning the woman gives birth; she is nufasa'. It is from 'nafs' meaning blood. Legally: 'blood that follows the child', named by the verbal noun like hayd.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This short passage provides the definition of nifas (postpartum bleeding). Linguistically, it is derived from the verb 'nafisat' (to give birth), and the woman is called 'nufasa'. The term also relates to 'nafs' (blood). Legally, nifas is defined as the blood that comes after childbirth. The term is a nominalization (ism al-masdar) just like the term 'hayd' for menstruation. This definition sets the stage for the subsequent rulings on nifas, which include its maximum duration (forty days, as mentioned earlier in the text) and the obligations of the woman in this state. The passage does not detail the rulings, only defines the legal term.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifās): Blood that issues after childbirth; legally defined as such.

Key Terms from Source Passage

B) Blood that follows childbirth.
C) Blood that occurs due to a miscarriage before the fourth month.
D) Blood that originates from a wound in the uterus.

Key Takeaway
Nifas is legally defined as blood that follows childbirth; any bleeding before birth is not nifas.

When the Wudu of an Excused Person Becomes Invalid: Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Timing
Intra-Hanafi dispute on invalidation timing of ma'dhur's wudu

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi majority position on when the wudu of a ma'dhur becomes invalid, explain the reasoning, and distinguish the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Zufar.

Core Idea
The wudu of a ma'dhur becomes invalid at the exit of the prayer time, not at entry, according to the Hanafi majority.

This lesson examines an important intra-Hanafi dispute about the wudu of a person suffering from a chronic ritual impurity (hadath) such as urinary incontinence. The question is: when does such a wudu become invalid? Is it at the entry of the prayer time, at the exit, or both? Understanding this ruling is essential for correctly applying the dispensation given to the excused person (ma'dhur).

Guided Path
1
Identify the key positions
Locate the three Hanafi opinions on invalidation timing: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad (exit only), Abu Yusuf (both entry and exit), Zufar (entry only).
Note that the majority view is from the 'three scholars' (ثَلاثَة).
2
Analyze the reasoning for each view
Understand the legal logic: Time is a substitute for performance (Imam), need is confined to the time (Abu Yusuf), and need arises at entry (Zufar).
The argument of Abu Hanifa and Muhammad is based on the fact that the Lawgiver allowed occupying the whole time with prayer.
3
Apply the dispute to concrete cases
Work through the examples: Fajr wudu becomes invalid at sunrise according to the three; wudu before noon for a non-obligatory prayer can be used for Dhuhr according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar but not the Imam; etc.
Note the practical difference (thamar al-khilaf) in each scenario.
4
Evaluate the tarjih (preference)
The text indicates that the majority view (exit only) is the relied-upon position (mufta bihi), with the expression 'on the soundest view' (على الأصح).
This is the operative ruling for fatwa.
5
Consider the conditions for being ma'dhur
The passage also defines conditions: the hadath must persist throughout the entire obligatory prayer time, and the excuse ceases if a full time passes without the hadath.
Also note the appendix on repelling the excuse as much as possible.
