ويبطل بخروجه فقط، وهذا إذا لم يمض عليهم وقت فرض إلا وذلك الحدث يوجد فيه. أي وضوؤهم الوقت أي حكم المعذورين من الصلاة الذي ابتلي به. يعني فقط: أي عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد وعند زفر بالدخول، وعند أبي يوسف بخروج الوقت ودخوله معا، وجه مذهب الإمام ومحمد أن الوقت أقيم مقام الأداء شرعا، فلا بد من تقديم الطهارة على الأداء حقيقة؛ ولأن الشارع أجاز إشغال الوقت كله بالأداء، ولا يمكن ذلك إلا بتقديم الطهارة، ولأبي يوسف: أن الحاجة مقصورة على الوقت فلا تعتبر قبل الوقت ولا بعده، ولزفر : اعتبار الطهارة مع المنافي للحاجة إلى الأداء، ولا حاجة قبل الوقت، والمراد بالبطلان من الخروج ظهور الحدث السابق عند خروج الوقت، فإضافة البطلان إليه مجاز؛ لأنه لا تأثير للخروج في الانتقاض حقيقة. وفائدة الخلاف تظهر فيمن توضأ وقت الفجر يبطل بطلوع الشمس عند علمائنا الثلاثة، أي الإمام وصاحبيه؛ لأنه خرج الوقت بطلوعها خلافاً لزفر، لأن البطلان عنده دخول الوقت ولم يوجد؛ فلهذا لا يبطل، سبب ولو توضاً قبل الزوال ولو لعيد أو صلاة ضحى يصلي الظهر عندهما؛ لعدم خروج وقت صلاة مكتوبة، فإنه المراد بالوقت على الأصح، خلافاً لأبي يوسف وزفر؛ لوجود دخول الوقت، ولو توضأ للظهر في وقته وصلاه، ثم توضأ في وقت الظهر للعصر لا يصلي به العصر عند الكل، أما عند أبي يوسف وزفر فلوجود دخول الوقت، وكذا عند الإمام ومحمد على الأصح؛ لأن هذه طهارة وقعت للظهر حتى لو ظهر فساد الظهر جاز له أداؤها بها، فلا تبقى بعد خروج وقت الظهر، وفي رواية له أن يصلي به العصر؛ لأن وضوءه للعصر في وقت الظهر کوضوئه للظهر قبل الزوال. (فتح، مسكين مع تغير) يوجد فيه: [ أي في ذلك الوقت، وهذا شرط ثبوت العذر، يعني لا يجد في وقت الصلاة زماناً يتوضأ ويصلّي فيه الحدث، وشرط انقطاع العذر خلو وقت كامل عنه (ط)] وإذا طرأ العذر في خلال الوقت قبل صلاة فرضه ينتظر إلى آخر الوقت، فإذا لم ينقطع صلّى قبل خروج الوقت، فإذا دخل الوقت الثاني وانقطع ودام الانقطاع إلى وقت صلاة أخرى توضأ وأعاد الصلاة؛ لأن بدوام انقطاع العذر وقتاً كاملاً تبين أنه صحيح صلى صلاة المعذورين، وإن لم ينقطع وقت الصلاة الثانية حتى خرج الوقت جازت الصلاة. تتمة: يجب رد عذره أو تقليله ما أمكن ولو بصلاته مؤمياً، يعني بأنه لو كان بحيث لو جلس لا يسيل ولو قام يسيل يجلس ،وجوبا، وبرده لا يبقى ذا عذر بخلاف الحائض؛ لأن اتصافها بالحيض لا ينفك عنها في المدة، وإن انقطع في بعض الأوقات.
And it becomes invalid only by its exit, and this is if no time of an obligatory prayer passes upon them except that event exists in it. That is, their wudu is for the time, i.e., the ruling of the excused persons concerning the prayer with which they are afflicted. It means 'only': i.e., according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad, and according to Zufar by entry, and according to Abu Yusuf by exit of time and its entry together. The reasoning of the Imam and Muhammad is that time has been legally established as a substitute for performance, so it is necessary to precede purity over performance in reality; and because the Lawgiver permitted occupying the entire time with performance, and that is not possible except by preceding purity. For Abu Yusuf: need is restricted to the time, so it is not considered before the time nor after it. For Zufar: considering purity together with what contradicts the need for performance, and there is no need before the time. The intended meaning of invalidation by exit is the appearance of the previous event at the time of exit, so the attribution of invalidation to it is metaphorical; because exit has no effect on breaking the purity in reality. The benefit of the dispute appears in the case of one who performs wudu at the time of Fajr; it becomes invalid with sunrise according to our three scholars, i.e., the Imam and his two companions; because the time exits with sunrise, contrary to Zufar, because according to him invalidation is by entry and it did not occur; hence it does not become invalid. Reason: and if he performed wudu before noon even for Eid or Duha prayer, he may pray Dhuhr with it according to them two; because the time of an obligatory prayer has not exited, for that is what is meant by time according to the most correct view, contrary to Abu Yusuf and Zufar; due to the occurrence of entry. And if he performed wudu for Dhuhr in its time and prayed it, then performed wudu in Dhuhr time for Asr, he may not pray Asr with it according to all. As for Abu Yusuf and Zufar, due to the occurrence of entry; and likewise according to Imam and Muhammad in the most correct view; because this purity occurred for Dhuhr such that if Dhuhr becomes invalid, it is permissible for him to perform it with it, so it does not remain after Dhuhr time exits. In one narration from him, he may pray Asr with it; because his wudu for Asr in Dhuhr time is like his wudu for Dhuhr before noon. (Fath, Miskin with change) In it: [i.e., in that time, and this is a condition for establishing the excuse, meaning that he does not find in the prayer time a period in which he can perform wudu and pray without the event, and the condition for the excuse to cease is the absence of a complete time from it. (T)] And if the excuse occurs during the time before an obligatory prayer, he waits until the end of the time; if it does not cease, he prays before the time exits; then when the second time enters and the excuse ceases and the cessation continues to another prayer time, he performs wudu and repeats the prayer; because by the continuous cessation of the excuse for a full time, it becomes clear that he was upon soundness when he prayed the prayer of the excused. And if it does not cease in the second prayer time until the time exits, the prayer is permissible. Appendix: He must repel his excuse or reduce it as much as possible, even by praying with gestures, meaning that if it is such that if he sits the blood does not flow and if he stands it flows, he sits obligatorily, and by repelling it he does not remain excused, unlike the menstruating woman; because her being characterized by menstruation does not separate from her during the period, even if it stops at some times.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute about when the wudu of a ma'dhur (an excused person suffering from chronic hadath like urinary incontinence) becomes invalid (batil). The base ruling states that the wudu of a ma'dhur is only invalidated by the exit of the prayer time, not by the entry of a new time. The author then details the positions: Abu Hanifa and Muhammad hold that invalidation occurs only at time exit; Zufar holds it occurs at time entry; Abu Yusuf holds it occurs at both entry and exit. The reasoning for the Imam and Muhammad is that time has been legally substituted for performance itself, so purity must actually precede performance. Abu Yusuf argues that the need for prayer is limited to the time, so purity is only relevant during the time. Zufar's view is that purity must be present when needed, and need arises at time entry. The practical consequence (thamarah) is illustrated: if a ma'dhur makes wudu at Fajr time, it becomes invalid at sunrise according to the three (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) but not according to Zufar because no entry occurred. Similarly, wudu before noon for a non-obligatory prayer can be used for Dhuhr according to Abu Yusuf and Zufar (due to entry) but not according to Imam and Muhammad (no exit of obligatory time). The passage also discusses the conditions for the excuse to be established: the hadath must exist throughout the entire time, and the excuse ceases only if a full time passes without any hadath. The appendix emphasizes that the person must minimize the excuse as much as possible, even by sitting to prevent flow, and if they can avoid it by doing so, they are no longer excused, unlike a menstruating woman whose state persists.

Key Terms
المعذور (al-ma'dhur): An excused person who suffers from a chronic hadath (e.g., urine drip, wind) that prevents maintaining wudu throughout the prayer time.
الحدث (al-hadath): The state of ritual impurity that invalidates wudu, specifically the chronic condition (e.g., incontinence) that the ma'dhur suffers from.
بطلان (butlan): Invalidation; the wudu becomes legally ineffective for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad), when does the wudu of a ma'dhur become invalid?
A) At the entry of the prayer time
B) At the exit of the prayer time
C) At both entry and exit
D) At the occurrence of a new hadath

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi majority (Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf) rules that the wudu of a ma'dhur becomes invalid at the exit of the prayer time, a ruling based on the principle that time substitutes for performance.

Nifas: Definition, Duration, and Key Disputes
Definition of nifas with legal details and disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition of nifas, identify its maximum duration, and explain the legal status of bleeding during pregnancy and after miscarriage.

Core Idea
Nifas is blood following childbirth, max 40 days; beyond that is istihadah.

This lesson defines nifas (postpartum bleeding) and clarifies when bleeding after childbirth is considered nifas versus istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding). It also addresses the controversy over the maximum duration, the effect of miscarriage, and the starting point of nifas for twins.

Guided Path
1
Define nifas linguistically and legally
Identify the linguistic root and the legal definition: blood that follows childbirth. Note that it is named like hayd (from the source).
2
Understand the ruling on blood during pregnancy
According to Hanafi, blood during pregnancy is istihadah unless it falls in the woman's usual menstrual period, in which case it is hayd. This is supported by a hadith.
The hadith: 'لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبرأن بحيضة'
3
Apply the rule to miscarriage (suqt)
If the fetus shows any formed limb (after 120 days), the miscarriage is considered a birth, triggering nifas. If no limb is formed, there is no nifas; the blood may be hayd or istihadah depending on the timing.
120 days: 40 sperm-drop, 40 clot, 40 lump of flesh.
4
Identify the maximum duration and the dispute
Hanafi: 40 days maximum. Shafi'i: 60 days. Maliki: 70 days. Beyond the maximum is istihadah.
5
Determine nifas for twins
Majority Hanafi view (Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf): nifas begins from the first twin. Muhammad and Zufar: from the last. The textbook supports the majority view.
The proof for the majority: nifas is blood following birth, and each birth triggers its own nifas.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
والنفاس: لغة: بالكسر من "نفست" المرأة بضم النون وفتحها إذا ولدت فهي نفساء، وهو من النفس يعني الدم، وشرعاً: "دم يعقب الولد" تسمية بالمصدر كالحيض. الولد ودم الحامل استحاضة والسقط إن ظهر بعض خلقه ولد، ولا حد لأقله وأكثره أربعون يوماً، والزائد استحاضة، ونفاس التوءمين من الأول. على الأربعين أي النفاس الولد أو أكثره ولو منقطعا عضوا عضوا؛ وإن لم تر دماً يجب عليها الغسل، وهو المذهب. ودم الحامل: عندنا وعند الشافعي: إذا رأته في أيام عادتها فهو حيض وإلا فاستحاضة اتفاقاً له: أنه دم خارج من الرحم وقت العادة فيكون حيضاً، لنا قوله عليه: "لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبرأن بحيضة" فجعل علينا الحيض معرفاً عن براءة الرحم، فدل على اجتماع الحمل مع الحيض. ذلك استحاضة: ولو في حال الولادة، وقال الشافعي حيض اعتباراً بالنفاس، قلنا: بالحبل ينسد فم الرحم، فالخارج يكون من الفرج. والسقط : بالحركات الثلاث، هو الذي يسقط من بطن أمه ميتا. بعض خلقه: كاليد والرجل والإصبع، وهذا لا يستبين إلا في مائة وعشرين يوماً، ووجهه أنه يكون أربعين يوماً نطفة، وأربعين يوماً علقة، وأربعين يوماً مضغة. ولد: لهذه المرأة شرعاً، حتى تصير به نفساء، وتصير الأمة أم ولد له وتنقضي العدّة به، فإن لم يظهر شيء من فلا نفاس، ولكن إن أمكن جعله حيضا بأن تقدمه طهر تامّ جعل حيضاً ، وإلا فهو استحاضة. أربعون يوماً قال الشافعي: ستون يوماً، وقال مالك: سبعون يوماً. نفاس التوءمين: التوءم كـ"جعفر" - اسم الولد إذا كان معه آخر في بطن واحد، يقال: "هما توءمان" كما يقال: "هما زوجان"، وقولهم: هما تؤم وهما زوج خطأ، ويقال للأنثى توءمة ولو كان ثلاثة أولاد وكان بين الأول والثالث أكثر من ستة أشهر، وبين الأول والثاني أقل فالأصح أنه يجعل حملاً واحداً، وابتداء النفاس من الأول عندنا، وعند محمد وزفر من الأخير، وبه قال الشافعي أيضاً لهم أنها حامل به، فلا يكون دمها من الرحم، ولهذا لا تنقضي العدة إلا بوضع الأخير ولنا أن النفاس هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة، وهو فصار كالدم الخارج عقب الولد الواحد، وانقضاء العدة متعلق بوضع حمل مضاف إليها، فليتناول الجميع.
And nifas: linguistically, with a kasrah on the nun, from 'nafisat' the woman (with dammah on the nun and fathah on the fa) when she gives birth, so she is nufasa' (a woman in nifas), and it is from 'nafs' meaning blood. Legally: 'blood that follows the child' naming by the infinitive like hayd. The child, and the blood of a pregnant woman is istihadah, and the miscarriage if some of its creation appears is a child, and there is no minimum for it, and its maximum is forty days, and what exceeds is istihadah, and the nifas of twins is from the first. (Commentary:) 'upon the forty' i.e., the nifas (blood) from the child or its majority even if intermittently limb by limb; and if she does not see blood, ghusl is obligatory upon her, and this is the madhhab. The blood of a pregnant woman: according to us and according to al-Shafi'i: if she sees it in the days of her habitual period, it is hayd, otherwise it is istihadah. According to him, it is blood exiting from the womb at the time of the habit, so it is hayd. Our proof: His saying (peace be upon him): 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver their burdens, nor with pregnant women until they are cleared by a haydah.' He made hayd a sign indicating the freedom of the womb, indicating the coexistence of pregnancy with hayd. That (blood) is istihadah: even at the time of childbirth, and al-Shafi'i said it is hayd by analogy to nifas. We said: during pregnancy the mouth of the womb is blocked, so what exits is from the vulva. The 'suqt' (miscarriage) with the three vowels (meaning suqt, suqt, or siqt) is that which falls from its mother's belly dead. 'Some of its creation': like the hand, foot, or finger, and this does not become clear except after one hundred and twenty days, and its reason is that it is a sperm-drop for forty days, a clot for forty days, and a lump of flesh for forty days. 'A child' for this woman legally, such that she becomes nufasa' by it, and a slave-woman becomes an umm walad by it, and the iddah is completed by it. If nothing appears, then no nifas, but if it is possible to make it hayd by a complete purity preceding it, it is made hayd; otherwise it is istihadah. Forty days: al-Shafi'i said sixty days; Malik said seventy days. Nifas of twins: twin is like 'ja'far' - the name for a child when there is another with it in one womb. It is said 'huma taw'man' just as 'huma zawjan'; and saying 'huma to'm' and 'huma zawj' is an error. For the female it is said 'taw'mah'. And if there were three children and between the first and third more than six months, and between the first and second less, then according to the soundest view, it is considered one pregnancy, and the beginning of nifas is from the first according to us (Hanafis), but according to Muhammad and Zufar, from the last, and al-Shafi'i also said this. Their proof: she is pregnant with it, so her blood is not from the womb, and hence the iddah is not completed except by the delivery of the last. Our proof: nifas is the blood exiting after childbirth, and it becomes like the blood exiting after a single child, and the completion of iddah is attached to the delivery of a pregnancy attributed to her, so it includes all.
Source pages p. 48

Commentary
This passage defines nifas (postpartum bleeding) and details numerous rulings and disputes. Linguistically, nifas derives from 'nafisat' meaning to give birth, and legally it is defined as blood that follows childbirth, analogous to hayd (menstruation). The passage states that the blood of a pregnant woman is considered istihadah (non-menstrual bleeding) in the Hanafi school, except if it coincides with her customary menstrual period, in which case it is hayd—a position shared with al-Shafi'i. The Hanafi proof is a hadith instructing that pregnant women should not be approached until they deliver, indicating that hayd can coexist with pregnancy. The passage then discusses miscarriage (suqt): if any part of a limb is formed (after 120 days), the miscarriage is considered a child, and the woman enters nifas; otherwise, if no features appear, there is no nifas. If the blood can be attributed to previous purity, it is considered hayd; otherwise istihadah. Regarding maximum duration: Hanafis hold forty days, al-Shafi'i holds sixty, and Malik holds seventy. For twins, nifas begins from the delivery of the first child according to the Hanafi view (Imam Abu Hanifa and Abu Yusuf? The text says 'at our view' but Muhammad and Zufar say from the last, along with al-Shafi'i). The Hanafi argument is that nifas is blood following birth, and each birth triggers nifas.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postpartum bleeding; blood that follows childbirth, legally treated like hayd in terms of prohibitions.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Non-menstrual uterine bleeding; considered a legal excuse (like chronic hadath) requiring wudu for each prayer.
السقط (al-suqt): Miscarriage; the fetus that falls from the womb dead. If any limb is formed (after 120 days), it is considered a child and triggers nifas.
التوءمان (al-taw'aman): Twins; two children born from one pregnancy. Nifas for twins is counted from the first birth according to the majority Hanafi view.

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) Seventy days

Key Takeaway
Nifas is postpartum bleeding with no minimum and a maximum of 40 days; beyond that is istihadah; blood during pregnancy can be hayd if it falls in the usual period.

Rules of Nifas (Postnatal Bleeding)
Defines nifas, duration, and related rulings with evidences and disputes.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi definition and maximum duration of nifas, distinguish it from istihadah, and apply the ruling for twin births and miscarriages.

Core Idea
Nifas lasts a maximum of 40 days; beyond that is istihadah; for twins, nifas begins from the first child.

Postnatal bleeding (nifas) carries distinct rulings that affect a woman's worship and marital relations. This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq with its sharh clarifies the definition, duration, and key disputes with other schools. You will learn how to identify nifas, when ghusl becomes obligatory, and how twin births and miscarriages factor into these rulings.

Guided Path
1
Define nifas and its maximum duration
Identify the key terms: 'الولد' (child), 'دم الحامل' (blood of a pregnant woman), 'السقط' (miscarriage). Note that nifas is the blood after childbirth, with no minimum and a maximum of forty days. Blood beyond forty days is istihadah.
The text explicitly says 'وأكثره أربعون يوماً' (its maximum is forty days).
2
Distinguish nifas from istihadah
Understand that blood from a pregnant woman is normally istihadah, except if it falls during her usual menstrual cycle, then it is menstruation. The proof is the hadith prohibiting intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver or complete a menstrual period, showing that menstruation can coexist with pregnancy.
The hadith is 'لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبرأن بحيضة'.
3
Determine the ruling for a miscarriage
A miscarriage is considered a childbirth only if some limbs are formed (after 120 days). The stages of fetal development are mentioned: 40 days nutfah, 40 days 'alaqah, 40 days mudghah. If limbs appear, the woman becomes nufasa' and nifas rulings apply. If no limbs, the bleeding may be treated as menstruation if possible, otherwise istihadah.
The text says 'والسقط إن ظهر بعض خلقه ولد' (if some of its creation appears, it is a child).
4
Examine the twin dispute
For twins, the Hanafi position (Abu Hanifa) is that nifas begins from the first child. Muhammad and Zufar (and al-Shafi'i) say from the last. The reasoning: nifas is blood after childbirth; the first delivery triggers it, similar to a single birth. The waiting period ends with the last delivery, but nifas is separate from 'iddah.
The text states 'ونفاس التوءمين من الأول' (nifas of twins is from the first). The proof for the opposing view is that she is still pregnant with the last child.
5
Apply the rulings to a practical scenario
Integrate all principles: Given a woman who gives birth to twins (first on June 1, second on June 2) and bleeds continuously until July 5 (34 days from first, 33 from second). Determine that nifas begins June 1, ends June 10 (if she stops earlier) or at 40 days from June 1. If bleeding stops before 40 days, ghusl is wajib. The waiting period ('iddah) ends only after the second delivery, but ritual purity for prayer is restored after nifas ends.
The thamarah al-khilaf (practical consequence) of the twin dispute affects when she can pray; Hanafi view allows prayer earlier.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بيان النفاس
الولد ودم الحامل استحاضة والسقط إن ظهر بعض خلقه ولد، ولا حد لأقله وأكثره أربعون يوماً، والزائد استحاضة، ونفاس التوءمين من الأول.
على الأربعين أي النفاس الولد أو أكثره ولو منقطعا عضوا عضوا؛ وإن لم تر دماً يجب عليها الغسل، وهو المذهب. (ط) ودم الحامل: عندنا وعند الشافعي: إذا رأته في أيام عادتها فهو حيض وإلا فاستحاضة اتفاقاً له: أنه دم خارج من الرحم وقت العادة فيكون حيضاً، لنا قوله عليه: "لا توطأ الحبالى حتى يضعن حملهن ولا الحبالى حتى يستبرأن بحيضة" فجعل علينا الحيض معرفاً عن براءة الرحم، فدل على اجتماع الحمل مع الحيض. (فتح) ذلك استحاضة: ولو في حال الولادة، وقال الشافعي حيض اعتباراً بالنفاس، قلنا: بالحبل ينسد فم الرحم، فالخارج يكون من الفرج. (ع) والسقط : بالحركات الثلاث، هو الذي يسقط من بطن أمه ميتا. (مسكين) بعض خلقه: كاليد والرجل والإصبع، وهذا لا يستبين إلا في مائة وعشرين يوماً، ووجهه أنه يكون أربعين يوماً نطفة، وأربعين يوماً علقة، وأربعين يوماً مضغة. (بدائع) ولد: لهذه المرأة شرعاً، حتى تصير به نفساء، وتصير الأمة أم ولد له وتنقضي العدّة به، فإن لم يظهر شيء من فلا نفاس، ولكن إن أمكن جعله حيضا بأن تقدمه طهر تامّ جعل حيضاً ، وإلا فهو استحاضة. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٧/١] أربعون يوماً قال الشافعي: ستون يوماً، وقال مالك: سبعون يوماً. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨/١] نفاس التوءمين: التوءم كـ"جعفر" - اسم الولد إذا كان معه آخر في بطن واحد، يقال: "هما توءمان" كما يقال: "هما زوجان"، وقولهم: هما تؤم وهما زوج خطأ، ويقال للأنثى توءمة ولو كان ثلاثة أولاد وكان بين الأول والثالث أكثر من ستة أشهر، وبين الأول والثاني أقل فالأصح أنه يجعل حملاً واحداً، وابتداء النفاس من الأول عندنا، وعند محمد وزفر من الأخير، وبه قال الشافعي أيضاً لهم أنها حامل به، فلا يكون دمها من الرحم، ولهذا لا تنقضي العدة إلا بوضع الأخير ولنا أن النفاس هو الدم الخارج عقب الولادة، وهو فصار كالدم الخارج عقب الولد الواحد، وانقضاء العدة متعلق بوضع حمل مضاف إليها، فليتناول الجميع. (فتح)
Explanation of Nifas: The child and the blood of a pregnant woman is istihadah. And a miscarriage, if some of its creation appears, is a child. There is no limit for its minimum, and its maximum is forty days, and what exceeds is istihadah. The nifas of twins is from the first. Upon forty days: meaning nifas, the child or most of it, even if piecemeal limb by limb; and if she does not see blood, ghusl is obligatory upon her, and this is the madhhab. (T) And the blood of a pregnant woman: In our view and according to al-Shafi'i: if she sees it during her usual days, it is menstruation, otherwise it is istihadah by agreement. For him: it is blood exiting the womb at the time of the usual period, so it is menstruation. For us: his statement (peace be upon him): 'Do not have intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver their burden, nor with pregnant women until they are cleared by one menstrual period.' He made menstruation an indicator of the womb being free, so it indicates the coexistence of pregnancy with menstruation. (Fath) That is istihadah: even at the time of childbirth, and al-Shafi'i said it is menstruation considering nifas. We said: due to pregnancy, the mouth of the womb is closed, so what exits is from the vagina. (A) And the miscarriage: by the three movements, it is what falls from her belly dead. (Miskin) Some of its creation: like the hand, foot, and finger, and this is not apparent except after one hundred twenty days, and its explanation is that it is a drop for forty days, a clot for forty days, and a lump of flesh for forty days. (Bada'i) A child: for this woman legally, so that she becomes a nufasa' by it, and the slave woman becomes umm walad for him, and the waiting period is completed with it. If nothing appears, then no nifas, but if it can be made menstruation by virtue of a complete prior purity, it is made menstruation, otherwise it is istihadah. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 37/1] Forty days: al-Shafi'i said sixty days, and Malik said seventy days. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 38/1] Nifas of twins: al-taw'am (like ja'far) - the name of a child if another is with it in one belly. It is said 'they are twins' as it is said 'they are a pair'. And their saying 'they are twin and they are a pair' is a mistake. The female is called taw'amah. If there are three children and between the first and third more than six months, and between the first and second less, then the most correct is that they are considered one pregnancy, and the beginning of nifas is from the first according to us, and according to Muhammad and Zufar from the last, and al-Shafi'i also said it. For them: she is pregnant with it, so her blood is not from the womb, and therefore the waiting period is not completed except with the delivery of the last. For us: nifas is the blood exiting after childbirth, so it is like the blood exiting after a single child, and the completion of the waiting period is attached to the delivery of a pregnancy attributed to her, so it encompasses all. (Fath)
Source pages p. 49

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof on the definition and rules of nifas (postnatal bleeding). It begins by stating that the blood of a pregnant woman is istihadah (irregular bleeding) unless it occurs during her usual menstrual cycle, in which case it is menstruation. The proof is the hadith of the Prophet (peace be upon him) that forbids intercourse with pregnant women until they deliver or until they are cleared by one menstrual period, indicating that menstruation can coexist with pregnancy. The passage then discusses the status of a miscarriage: if any part of the fetus is formed (after 120 days), it is considered a child, and the woman becomes nufasa' (in nifas). The bleeding after a miscarriage within 120 days is not nifas; if it can be menstruation, it is, otherwise istihadah. The maximum duration of nifas is forty days according to the Hanafi school, while al-Shafi'i said sixty days and Malik seventy days. Any bleeding beyond forty days is istihadah. For twins, the Hanafi position is that nifas begins from the first child, while Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i say from the last. The argument is that nifas is blood after delivery; the waiting period ends only with the last delivery, but the blood from the first is still nifas, analogous to a single birth.

Key Terms
النفاس (al-nifas): Postnatal bleeding that follows childbirth; it has a maximum of forty days in the Hanafi school.
الاستحاضة (al-istihadah): Irregular vaginal bleeding that is not menstruation or nifas; it does not prevent prayer or fasting, but necessitates wudu for each prayer.
السقط (al-suqt): A miscarriage; if some limbs are formed (after 120 days), it is considered a child for legal rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the maximum duration of nifas (postnatal bleeding)?
A) 40 days
B) 60 days
C) 70 days
D) No limit

Key Takeaway
Nifas is defined as postnatal bleeding lasting a maximum of 40 days; for Hanafis, it begins with the first of twins and all rulings of nifas apply fully within that limit.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Purification with Liquids Other Than Water
Ruling + proof + intra-madhhab dispute on purification liquids.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi position on purification with non-water liquids, identify the relevant Quranic and analogical evidence, and explain the intra-madhhab dispute among Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad, and Zufar.

Core Idea
Any pure liquid that removes impurity can purify – the Hanafi school extends purification beyond water.

The chapter on impurities opens with a ruling that the body and garment can be purified not only with water but also with any liquid that is pure and effectively removes the impurity, such as vinegar and rose water, but excluding oils. This lesson unpacks the legal reasoning behind that ruling, the proof from the Quran, and the important differences within the Hanafi school and with other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and its scope
The text states that purification is valid with water and with any 'muzil' (removing) liquid like vinegar and rose water, but not with oil. Note that the liquid must itself be pure and have the ability to remove impurity.
The ruling applies to both body and garments according to Abu Hanifa.
2
Examine the Quranic evidence
The author cites Surah Al-Furqan verse 48: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water.' This is the primary proof for water. For other liquids, the Hanafi school uses analogy (qiyas) based on the property of removing impurity.
The verse uses 'tahuran' which implies water is naturally purifying, but it does not explicitly exclude other liquids.
3
Trace the intra-Hanafi dispute
Abu Hanifa allows any pure liquid that removes impurity. Muhammad and Zufar restrict to water only. Abu Yusuf distinguishes: for garments any pure liquid, for body only water. Note the reasoning behind each view.
The mufta bihi (relied-upon) position is that of Abu Hanifa for objects, and for the body, the view of Abu Yusuf is considered.
4
Understand the thamarah al-khilaf
Practically, a Hanafi can use rose water or vinegar for washing clothes if no water is available, whereas a Shafi'i would need to perform tayammum.
This shows how a difference in usul leads to different daily practice.
5
Confirm the mufta bihi and its authority
The commentary indicates that Abu Hanifa's view is the basis for fatwa, though the text does not explicitly say 'عليه الفتوى' for this ruling. However, the analytical toolbox confirms it as mufta bihi within the school.
The authority weight is Zahir al-Riwayah.

يطهر البدن والثوب بالماء، وبمائع مزيل كالخل، وماء الورد، لا الدهن، والخف
وغيرهما من النجاسة
بالدلك بنجس ذي جرم،
باب الأنجاس لما فرغ من النجاسة الحكمية وتطهيرها شرع في الحقيقية وإزالتها، وقدم الحكمية؛ لأنها أقوى لكون قليلها يمنع جواز الصلاة اتفاقاً، ولا يسقط وجوب إزالتها بعذر ما إما أصلاً أو خلفاً بخلاف الحقيقية، وأما من به نجاسة وهو محدث إذا وجد ما يكفي أحدهما فقط، فإنما وجب صرف رفه للنجاسة لا للحدث؛ ليتيمم بعده فيكون تحصيلاً للطهارتين. وتعبيره بالإزالة دون التطهير ؛ لأنها أعم لصدقها بقطع محل النجاسة، والنجاسة شرعاً عين مستقذرة، وإزالتها عن الثوب والبدن والمكان فرض إن بلغت القدر المانع، وقال مالك: سنة، فلا يكفر جاحد افتراض إزالتها، وافتراض إزالتها مشروط بما إذا أمكن من غير ارتكاب ما هو أشد، حتى لو لم يتمكن من إزالتها إلا بإبداء عورته للناس يصلى معها؛ لأن كشف عورته أشد. (فتح) الأنجاس: هي جمع نحس بفتح الجيم، وهو أعم من الخبث الذي يطلق على الحقيقي، والحدث الذي يطلق على الحكمي، يعني النجس يطلق على الحقيقي والحكمي كليهما. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨/١] يطهر البدن والثوب: لو عبّر بـ "المتنجس" لكان أولى؛ ليعم كل شيء تنجس حتى المأكول. وإذا تنجس طرف الثوب فنسيه، غسل منه طرفاً من غير تحر يحكم بطهارته في المختار ولو رأى على ثوبه نجاسة ولا يدري متى أصابته، فالمختار عند الإمام أنه لا يعيد إلا الصلاة التي هو فيها، ومن شك في طرف النجس فليغسل الجميع احتياطاً؛ لأن موضع النجاسة غير معلوم لا ظناً ولا يقيناً، وليس البعض بأولى من البعض. (فتح المعين)
بالماء: أي المطلق؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنْزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُوراً (الفرقان: ٤٨)، ولو مستعملاً. وبمائع : المائع السائل من "ماع " أي سال، وتشترط طهارته؛ إذ تطهيره لغيره فرع طهارته في نفسه، فعلى هذا لو غسل المغلظة ببول ما يؤكل لا يزول وصف التغليظ وهو المختار، وقوله: "وماء الورد" حتى الريق، فيظهر إصبع وثدي بلحس ثلاثاً. (فتح) وماء الورد ونحوهما مما إذا عصر انعصر، وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي: لا يجوز بغير الماء، ولا فرق بين الثوب والبدن وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز في البدن بغير الماء. (مسكين) لا الدهن: عطف على الخل، أي المائع مثل الخل، لا مثل الدهن واللبن. (مسكين)] وكذا الدبس والعسل
والشيرج والسمن وهو الصحيح؛ لأن هذه الأشياء غير مزيلة بالدلك على الأرض، على وجه المبالغة. بنجس ذي جرم: أي يطهر الخف بالدلك بإصابة نجس ذي جرم، سواء كان رطباً أو يابساً عند أبي يوسف، وعليه الفتوى بشرط عدم بقاء الأثر، إلا أن يشق زواله؛ لقول علي: "فمن أراد أن يدخل المسجد فليقلب نعليه، فإن رأى بهما أذى فليمسحهما بالأرض، فإن الأرض لهما طهور، ووجه الاستدلال : أن النبي عليه أطلق فعمّ اليابس والرطب -
Book of Purity. Page 49. Chapter of Impurities. Chapter of Impurities. K. The body and garment are purified with water, and with a removing liquid like vinegar and rose water, not oil, and the khuff and others from impurity by rubbing with a solid impurity. Chapter of Impurities: When he finished from the ruling impurity and its purification, he began with the real impurity and its removal. He gave precedence to the ruling because it is stronger since its small quantity prevents the permissibility of prayer by agreement, and the obligation of removing it is not waived by any excuse either originally or substitutively, contrary to the real impurity. And as for the one who has impurity and is in a state of hadath if he finds enough for only one of them, then he must spend his water on the impurity, not on the hadath, so that he may do tayammum afterward, thus obtaining both purities. And his expression 'removal' instead of 'purification' because it is more general, including cutting away the place of impurity. And impurity legally is a filthy substance. Removing it from the garment, body, and place is obligatory if it reaches the preventing amount. Malik said: sunnah. So the denier of its obligation is not a disbeliever. Its obligation is conditional upon being possible without committing something more severe, so if he cannot remove it except by exposing his private parts to people, he prays with it because exposing his private parts is more severe. (Fath) The impurities (al-anjas): plural of najas with fatha on the jim, and it is more general than al-khabath which is applied to the real, and al-hadath which is applied to the ruling, meaning najis is applied to both real and ruling. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 38/1] He purifies the body and garment: if he had expressed 'the mutanajjis' it would have been better to include everything that becomes impure, even food. And if the hem of a garment becomes impure and he forgets, he washes a part of it without estimation; it is ruled pure in the chosen view. And if he sees impurity on his garment and does not know when it occurred, the chosen view according to the Imam is that he only repeats the prayer he is in. Whoever doubts the location of the impurity should wash all of it as a precaution because the location of the impurity is unknown, neither by probability nor certainty, and one part is not more likely than another. (Fath al-Mu'in) With water: meaning absolute water, due to His statement the Exalted: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (25:48), even if used water. And with a liquid: liquid is from 'ma'a' meaning flowed, and its purity is a condition; because purifying others is subsidiary to its own purity. On this basis, if he washes a severe impurity with the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten, the description of severity is not removed, and that is the chosen view. And his statement: 'and rose water' even saliva, so a finger or breast is made pure by licking three times. (Fath) And rose water and similar things that when crushed, they exude, and Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible with other than water, and there is no difference between the garment and the body. From Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible on the body with other than water. (Miskin) Not oil: it is an 'atf' on vinegar, meaning a liquid like vinegar, not like oil and milk. (Miskin) Similarly, molasses, honey, sesame oil, and ghee, and that is the correct; because these things are not removed by rubbing on the ground, in an exaggerated manner. With a solid impurity: meaning the khuff is purified by rubbing upon encountering a solid impurity, whether it is wet or dry according to Abu Yusuf, and upon it is the fatwa, on condition that no trace remains, unless its removal is difficult, due to the saying of Ali: 'Whoever wants to enter the mosque, let him turn over his sandals; if he sees on them filth, let him wipe them on the earth, for the earth is purification for them.' The point of evidence: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) spoke generally, including both dry and wet.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on impurities (al-anjas) and the first ruling on how to purify. It opens by stating that the body and garment are purified with water and any pure liquid that removes impurity, such as vinegar and rose water, but not oil. The khuff (leather socks) and other similar items can be purified from a solid impurity by rubbing on the ground. The commentary then discusses various details: why the chapter follows the previous one on ruling impurity, the definition of najasah, the obligation of removal, the ruling on liquid purifiers, and the purification of khuff. The proof for water is the Quranic verse 'And We sent down from the sky pure water.' For liquids other than water, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i do not permit purification with anything other than water, while Abu Hanifa permits with any pure liquid that can remove impurity. Abu Yusuf allows it for garments but not for the body. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that purification with non-water liquids is valid provided the liquid itself is pure and cleansing. For the khuff, the proof is the hadith of Ali about wiping sandals on the earth, which is generalized to include both wet and dry impurities. The preferred view is Abu Yusuf's: khuff is purified by rubbing if no trace remains, unless removal is difficult, then it is excused.

Key Terms
المائع (al-ma'i'): A liquid that flows; used in the context of purification if it is pure and removes impurity.
النجاسة (al-najasah): Impurity; its removal is obligatory for prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon Hanafi view, what is required for a liquid other than water to be valid for purification?
A) It must be water but can be used water.
B) It must be pure and able to remove the impurity.
C) It must be specifically vinegar or rose water.
D) It must be from a plant source.

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school permits purification with any pure liquid that effectively removes impurity, extending the means of purification beyond water alone.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of Khuff by Rubbing (Dalk)
Ruling with proof for purifying khuff by rubbing.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi ruling on purifying khuff (leather socks) by rubbing on earth, identify the conditions, and cite the evidence from the hadith.

Core Idea
Solid impurities on khuff can be removed by rubbing on earth if no trace remains, based on the general hadith.

The same chapter on impurities addresses a practical issue: how to purify the khuff (leather socks) when they come into contact with a solid impurity. The text presents the view of Abu Yusuf, which is the relied-upon position, that rubbing the khuff on the earth suffices. This lesson explores the ruling, its conditions, and the evidence from the sayings of Ali (RA) and the Prophet (SAW).

Guided Path
1
Identify the object and method of purification
The khuff (leather socks) can be purified from a solid impurity (dhil jirm) by rubbing (dalk) on the earth. This applies to both wet and dry solid impurities.
The ruling is specific to khuff and similar thick footwear that is impure only on the surface.
2
State the conditions for validity
The rubbing is valid if no trace of the impurity remains after rubbing. If removal is difficult, it is excused.
This is the condition mentioned in the text: 'بشرط عدم بقاء الأثر، إلا أن يشق زواله'.
3
Examine the evidence
The text cites the saying of Ali (RA): 'Whoever wants to enter the mosque, let him turn over his sandals; if he sees on them filth, let him wipe them on the earth, for the earth is purification for them.' This is used as evidence that rubbing on earth purifies solid impurities.
The hadith is generalized to apply to both dry and wet impurities.
4
Identify the mufta bihi
The text explicitly states 'وعليه الفتوى' (upon it is the fatwa), indicating that Abu Yusuf's view is the operative ruling.
This is a clear indication of the preferred position.
5
Apply to practice
A person wearing khuff steps on dry mud that is impure. He can rub the khuff on the ground until the impurity is no longer visible, and it becomes pure.
Liquid impurities require washing; this ruling is only for solid impurities.

Source Text

يطهر البدن والثوب بالماء، وبمائع مزيل كالخل، وماء الورد، لا الدهن، والخف
وغيرهما من النجاسة
بالدلك بنجس ذي جرم،
باب الأنجاس لما فرغ من النجاسة الحكمية وتطهيرها شرع في الحقيقية وإزالتها، وقدم الحكمية؛ لأنها أقوى لكون قليلها يمنع جواز الصلاة اتفاقاً، ولا يسقط وجوب إزالتها بعذر ما إما أصلاً أو خلفاً بخلاف الحقيقية، وأما من به نجاسة وهو محدث إذا وجد ما يكفي أحدهما فقط، فإنما وجب صرف رفه للنجاسة لا للحدث؛ ليتيمم بعده فيكون تحصيلاً للطهارتين. وتعبيره بالإزالة دون التطهير ؛ لأنها أعم لصدقها بقطع محل النجاسة، والنجاسة شرعاً عين مستقذرة، وإزالتها عن الثوب والبدن والمكان فرض إن بلغت القدر المانع، وقال مالك: سنة، فلا يكفر جاحد افتراض إزالتها، وافتراض إزالتها مشروط بما إذا أمكن من غير ارتكاب ما هو أشد، حتى لو لم يتمكن من إزالتها إلا بإبداء عورته للناس يصلى معها؛ لأن كشف عورته أشد. (فتح) الأنجاس: هي جمع نحس بفتح الجيم، وهو أعم من الخبث الذي يطلق على الحقيقي، والحدث الذي يطلق على الحكمي، يعني النجس يطلق على الحقيقي والحكمي كليهما. [رمز الحقائق: ٣٨/١] يطهر البدن والثوب: لو عبّر بـ "المتنجس" لكان أولى؛ ليعم كل شيء تنجس حتى المأكول. وإذا تنجس طرف الثوب فنسيه، غسل منه طرفاً من غير تحر يحكم بطهارته في المختار ولو رأى على ثوبه نجاسة ولا يدري متى أصابته، فالمختار عند الإمام أنه لا يعيد إلا الصلاة التي هو فيها، ومن شك في طرف النجس فليغسل الجميع احتياطاً؛ لأن موضع النجاسة غير معلوم لا ظناً ولا يقيناً، وليس البعض بأولى من البعض. (فتح المعين)
بالماء: أي المطلق؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنْزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُوراً (الفرقان: ٤٨)، ولو مستعملاً. وبمائع : المائع السائل من "ماع " أي سال، وتشترط طهارته؛ إذ تطهيره لغيره فرع طهارته في نفسه، فعلى هذا لو غسل المغلظة ببول ما يؤكل لا يزول وصف التغليظ وهو المختار، وقوله: "وماء الورد" حتى الريق، فيظهر إصبع وثدي بلحس ثلاثاً. (فتح) وماء الورد ونحوهما مما إذا عصر انعصر، وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي: لا يجوز بغير الماء، ولا فرق بين الثوب والبدن وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز في البدن بغير الماء. (مسكين) لا الدهن: عطف على الخل، أي المائع مثل الخل، لا مثل الدهن واللبن. (مسكين)] وكذا الدبس والعسل
والشيرج والسمن وهو الصحيح؛ لأن هذه الأشياء غير مزيلة بالدلك على الأرض، على وجه المبالغة. بنجس ذي جرم: أي يطهر الخف بالدلك بإصابة نجس ذي جرم، سواء كان رطباً أو يابساً عند أبي يوسف، وعليه الفتوى بشرط عدم بقاء الأثر، إلا أن يشق زواله؛ لقول علي: "فمن أراد أن يدخل المسجد فليقلب نعليه، فإن رأى بهما أذى فليمسحهما بالأرض، فإن الأرض لهما طهور، ووجه الاستدلال : أن النبي عليه أطلق فعمّ اليابس والرطب -
Book of Purity. Page 49. Chapter of Impurities. Chapter of Impurities. K. The body and garment are purified with water, and with a removing liquid like vinegar and rose water, not oil, and the khuff and others from impurity by rubbing with a solid impurity. Chapter of Impurities: When he finished from the ruling impurity and its purification, he began with the real impurity and its removal. He gave precedence to the ruling because it is stronger since its small quantity prevents the permissibility of prayer by agreement, and the obligation of removing it is not waived by any excuse either originally or substitutively, contrary to the real impurity. And as for the one who has impurity and is in a state of hadath if he finds enough for only one of them, then he must spend his water on the impurity, not on the hadath, so that he may do tayammum afterward, thus obtaining both purities. And his expression 'removal' instead of 'purification' because it is more general, including cutting away the place of impurity. And impurity legally is a filthy substance. Removing it from the garment, body, and place is obligatory if it reaches the preventing amount. Malik said: sunnah. So the denier of its obligation is not a disbeliever. Its obligation is conditional upon being possible without committing something more severe, so if he cannot remove it except by exposing his private parts to people, he prays with it because exposing his private parts is more severe. (Fath) The impurities (al-anjas): plural of najas with fatha on the jim, and it is more general than al-khabath which is applied to the real, and al-hadath which is applied to the ruling, meaning najis is applied to both real and ruling. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 38/1] He purifies the body and garment: if he had expressed 'the mutanajjis' it would have been better to include everything that becomes impure, even food. And if the hem of a garment becomes impure and he forgets, he washes a part of it without estimation; it is ruled pure in the chosen view. And if he sees impurity on his garment and does not know when it occurred, the chosen view according to the Imam is that he only repeats the prayer he is in. Whoever doubts the location of the impurity should wash all of it as a precaution because the location of the impurity is unknown, neither by probability nor certainty, and one part is not more likely than another. (Fath al-Mu'in) With water: meaning absolute water, due to His statement the Exalted: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (25:48), even if used water. And with a liquid: liquid is from 'ma'a' meaning flowed, and its purity is a condition; because purifying others is subsidiary to its own purity. On this basis, if he washes a severe impurity with the urine of an animal whose meat is eaten, the description of severity is not removed, and that is the chosen view. And his statement: 'and rose water' even saliva, so a finger or breast is made pure by licking three times. (Fath) And rose water and similar things that when crushed, they exude, and Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i said: it is not permissible with other than water, and there is no difference between the garment and the body. From Abu Yusuf: it is not permissible on the body with other than water. (Miskin) Not oil: it is an 'atf' on vinegar, meaning a liquid like vinegar, not like oil and milk. (Miskin) Similarly, molasses, honey, sesame oil, and ghee, and that is the correct; because these things are not removed by rubbing on the ground, in an exaggerated manner. With a solid impurity: meaning the khuff is purified by rubbing upon encountering a solid impurity, whether it is wet or dry according to Abu Yusuf, and upon it is the fatwa, on condition that no trace remains, unless its removal is difficult, due to the saying of Ali: 'Whoever wants to enter the mosque, let him turn over his sandals; if he sees on them filth, let him wipe them on the earth, for the earth is purification for them.' The point of evidence: that the Prophet (peace be upon him) spoke generally, including both dry and wet.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the beginning of the chapter on impurities (al-anjas) and the first ruling on how to purify. It opens by stating that the body and garment are purified with water and any pure liquid that removes impurity, such as vinegar and rose water, but not oil. The khuff (leather socks) and other similar items can be purified from a solid impurity by rubbing on the ground. The commentary then discusses various details: why the chapter follows the previous one on ruling impurity, the definition of najasah, the obligation of removal, the ruling on liquid purifiers, and the purification of khuff. The proof for water is the Quranic verse 'And We sent down from the sky pure water.' For liquids other than water, there is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i do not permit purification with anything other than water, while Abu Hanifa permits with any pure liquid that can remove impurity. Abu Yusuf allows it for garments but not for the body. The relied-upon view (mufta bihi) is that purification with non-water liquids is valid provided the liquid itself is pure and cleansing. For the khuff, the proof is the hadith of Ali about wiping sandals on the earth, which is generalized to include both wet and dry impurities. The preferred view is Abu Yusuf's: khuff is purified by rubbing if no trace remains, unless removal is difficult, then it is excused.

Key Terms
الخف (al-khuff): Leather socks worn over the feet; a specific type of footwear that has special rulings in purification and wiping during wudu.
الدلك (al-dalk): Rubbing; a method of purification for solid impurities on khuff.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Under what condition does the Hanafi school allow purifying khuff by rubbing on earth?
A) When the impurity is liquid and the earth is dry.
B) When the impurity is solid and no trace remains.
C) When the khuff is new and the earth is from the mosque.
D) When water is unavailable and the impurity is from a dog.

Key Takeaway
Solid impurities on khuff can be purified by rubbing on earth, provided no trace remains, making purification accessible in waterless situations.

The Ruling of Removing Najasah
Defining najasah and its removal ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi obligation of removing najasah and distinguish between legal and real impurity, including the conditions and exceptions.

Core Idea
Removing najasah is farḍ when it reaches a preventing amount, but not if it exposes one's awrah.

This passage opens the chapter on impurities by distinguishing between legal impurity (ḥadath) and real impurity (najāsah). It establishes that removing real impurity from the body, garment, and place is an obligation (farḍ) when the amount reaches the level that prevents prayer, with a key condition that the obligation is waived if removal would require exposing one's private parts or committing a more severe sin. The text also explains the priority of removing impurity over ḥadath when water is scarce.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two types of impurity
The text distinguishes between ḥukmī (legal/ḥadath) and ḥaqīqī (real/najāsah). Legal impurity is stronger because even a small amount prevents prayer by consensus, and its removal cannot be excused.
Legal impurity includes states like being without wuḍūʾ or ghusl.
2
State the ruling of removing real impurity
Removing najāsah from the body, garment, and place is farḍ (obligatory) if the impurity reaches the amount that prevents prayer (e.g., the size of a dirham for thick impurities). Imam Mālik considered it sunnah, but the Ḥanafī position is farḍ.
Denying this obligation does not make one a disbeliever because the evidence is open to interpretation.
3
Identify the condition and exception
The obligation is conditional upon the ability to remove without committing a more severe harm, such as exposing one's awrah to others. If impossible, one may pray with the impurity.
This is derived from the principle of preventing greater harm.
4
Apply the priority rule when water is scarce
If a person has both ḥadath and najāsah but only enough water for one, they must use the water to remove the najāsah first, then perform tayammum for the ḥadath. This achieves both purities.
This demonstrates that removing najāsah is prioritized over removing ḥadath in such cases.

باب الأنجاس لما فرغ من النجاسة الحكمية وتطهيرها شرع في الحقيقية وإزالتها، وقدم الحكمية؛ لأنها أقوى لكون قليلها يمنع جواز الصلاة اتفاقاً، ولا يسقط وجوب إزالتها بعذر ما إما أصلاً أو خلفاً بخلاف الحقيقية، وأما من به نجاسة وهو محدث إذا وجد ما يكفي أحدهما فقط، فإنما وجب صرف رفه للنجاسة لا للحدث؛ ليتيمم بعده فيكون تحصيلاً للطهارتين. وتعبيره بالإزالة دون التطهير ؛ لأنها أعم لصدقها بقطع محل النجاسة، والنجاسة شرعاً عين مستقذرة، وإزالتها عن الثوب والبدن والمكان فرض إن بلغت القدر المانع، وقال مالك: سنة، فلا يكفر جاحد افتراض إزالتها، وافتراض إزالتها مشروط بما إذا أمكن من غير ارتكاب ما هو أشد، حتى لو لم يتمكن من إزالتها إلا بإبداء عورته للناس يصلى معها؛ لأن كشف عورته أشد. (فتح المعين)

Chapter of Impurities. Chapter of Impurities. ... It purifies the body and garment with water, and with a liquid remover like vinegar and rose water, not oil, and the leather sock and others from impurity by rubbing with a solid impurity, otherwise wash. ... The opening: When he finished from the legal impurity and its purification, he began with the real impurity and its removal, and he gave precedence to the legal because it is stronger since its small amount prevents the permissibility of prayer by agreement, and its removal does not become waived due to any excuse either fundamentally or alternatively unlike the real. As for one who has impurity on him and is in a state of hadath, if he finds enough for only one of them, he must devote his water to the impurity not the hadath, so that he may do tayammum afterward, thereby attaining both purities. His expression 'removal' without 'purification' because it is more general, applying to cutting off the place of impurity. Impurity legally is a filthy substance, and its removal from garment, body, and place is obligatory if it reaches the preventing amount. Malik said: Sunnah, so one who denies its obligation is not a disbeliever. Its obligation is conditioned upon the possibility without committing what is more severe, such that if he cannot remove it except by exposing his private parts to people, he prays with it because exposing his private parts is more severe. (Fath) The 'anjas' is plural of 'najis' with fat-ha on the jim, and it is more general than 'khabath' which applies to real, and 'hadath' which applies to legal, meaning 'najis' applies to both real and legal. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/38] 'Purifies the body and garment': If he had expressed it as 'mutanajjis' it would be better to include everything that becomes impure including food. If the edge of a garment becomes impure and he forgets, he washes a part of it without specifying and it is ruled pure in the chosen view. If he sees impurity on his garment and does not know when it struck, the chosen view according to Imam is that he only repeats the prayer he is in. For one who doubts about the place of impurity, he should wash all as a precaution because the place of impurity is not known by conjecture or certainty. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'With water': i.e. absolute water, due to His saying: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (Al-Furqan: 48), even if used. 'With a liquid': liquid from 'ma'a' meaning flowed, and its purity is required since its purification of others is conditional upon its own purity. Accordingly, if one washes a heavy impurity with the urine of an edible animal, the description of heaviness is not removed, and that is the chosen view. His saying 'and rose water' even saliva, so he cleans finger and breast by licking three times. (Fath) Rose water and similar when squeezed, Muhammad, Zufar, and Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with other than water, and there is no difference between garment and body. Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible on the body with other than water. (Miskin) 'Not oil': conjuncted to vinegar, meaning liquid like vinegar, not like oil and milk. (Miskin) And likewise molasses, honey, sesame oil, and ghee, and this is the correct view because these things are not removing by rubbing on the ground in a manner of exaggeration.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on impurities (Bāb al-Anjās). The author first distinguishes between ḥukmī (legal) and ḥaqīqī (real) impurity, explaining why the legal impurity is stronger and prioritized in the text. He then states the ruling that purification from real impurity (najāsah) on body, garment, and place is farḍ (obligatory) if the amount reaches that which prevents prayer. Imam Mālik considered it sunnah, but the Ḥanafī position is that it is farḍ, though denial does not make one a kāfir. The passage details that this obligation is conditional—if removal requires exposing one's awrah, it is not required. It then discusses purification with water (absolute water, even if used) and with other pure liquids like vinegar and rose water, but not with oily substances like oil and ghee, as they do not remove impurity effectively. Disagreements are noted: Muḥammad, Zufar, and al-Shāfiʿī prohibit using non-water liquids; Abū Yūsuf prohibits on the body. The Ḥanafī position permits other liquids for garments and some for body, with conditions. The commentary also addresses rules for uncertainty and doubt about impurity location, and the priority of removing impurity over wuḍūʾ when water is limited.

Key Terms
النجاسة (al-najāsah): Impurity; a filthy substance that prevents prayer if present in a significant amount.
طهور (ṭahūr): Purifier; water that is pure and purifying, i.e., capable of removing impurity.
الفرض (al-farḍ): An obligation established by definitive evidence; in this context, removal of najasah is farḍ when conditions are met.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, when is removal of najasah farḍ?
A) Whenever any impurity is present on the body or garment
B) Only when the impurity reaches the amount that prevents prayer and removal is possible without severe harm
C) Only if the impurity is from an animal
D) Only if the impurity is dry

Key Takeaway
Removing najasah is farḍ when it reaches the preventing amount, but the obligation drops if removal would cause a greater harm.

Purification with Water and Other Liquids
Expanding on permissible purifiers

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify which liquids are valid for removing najasah and explain the Hanafi position, including the disagreements among imams.

Core Idea
Water is primary, but other pure liquids like vinegar remove impurity; oils and dairy do not.

This passage continues the discussion on purification by specifying the means. While absolute water is the primary purifier, the Hanafi school permits using other pure liquids that have the property of removing impurity, such as vinegar and rose water. However, oily substances like oil and ghee are not effective. There is intra-Hanafi and cross-madhhab disagreement on whether non-water liquids can be used on the body. The text also explains conditions for the liquid and practical applications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the primary purifier: water
The text says 'with water', meaning absolute water (even used water). The Quranic verse (Al-Furqan:48) is cited as evidence: water is a purifier.
Used water (musta'mal) is still valid for removing najasah, unlike for wuḍūʾ.
2
List other valid liquids
The text mentions 'liquid remover' like vinegar and rose water. These are pure liquids that can be used to remove impurity by pouring and rubbing.
The liquid must be pure itself and capable of removing impurity. Saliva is also mentioned as valid.
3
Identify invalid liquids
Oils (e.g., olive oil, sesame oil, ghee) and dairy products (milk) are not valid. The reason: they do not remove impurity effectively by rubbing on the ground.
The text explicitly says 'not oil' and includes honey and molasses as invalid.
4
Note the disagreements
Muhammad al-Shaybani, Zufar, and al-Shafi'i forbid using any non-water liquid for purification. Abu Yusuf allows it on garments but not on the body. The relied-upon Hanafi position (mufta bihi) is that other liquids are valid on both body and garment, except for oils and dairy.
The text sides with the permissive view, as it is the correct one (ṣaḥīḥ).

(فتح المعين)
بالماء: أي المطلق؛ لقوله تعالى: ﴿وَأَنْزَلْنَا مِنَ السَّمَاءِ مَاءً طَهُوراً (الفرقان: ٤٨)، ولو مستعملاً. وبمائع : المائع السائل من "ماع " أي سال، وتشترط طهارته؛ إذ تطهيره لغيره فرع طهارته في نفسه، فعلى هذا لو غسل المغلظة ببول ما يؤكل لا يزول وصف التغليظ وهو المختار، وقوله: "وماء الورد" حتى الريق، فيظهر إصبع وثدي بلحس ثلاثاً. (فتح) وماء الورد ونحوهما مما إذا عصر انعصر، وقال محمد وزفر والشافعي: لا يجوز بغير الماء، ولا فرق بين الثوب والبدن وعن أبي يوسف لا يجوز في البدن بغير الماء. (مسكين) لا الدهن: عطف على الخل، أي المائع مثل الخل، لا مثل الدهن واللبن. (مسكين)] وكذا الدبس والعسل
والشيرج والسمن وهو الصحيح؛ لأن هذه الأشياء غير مزيلة بالدلك على الأرض، على وجه المبالغة.
Chapter of Impurities. Chapter of Impurities. ... It purifies the body and garment with water, and with a liquid remover like vinegar and rose water, not oil, and the leather sock and others from impurity by rubbing with a solid impurity, otherwise wash. ... The opening: When he finished from the legal impurity and its purification, he began with the real impurity and its removal, and he gave precedence to the legal because it is stronger since its small amount prevents the permissibility of prayer by agreement, and its removal does not become waived due to any excuse either fundamentally or alternatively unlike the real. As for one who has impurity on him and is in a state of hadath, if he finds enough for only one of them, he must devote his water to the impurity not the hadath, so that he may do tayammum afterward, thereby attaining both purities. His expression 'removal' without 'purification' because it is more general, applying to cutting off the place of impurity. Impurity legally is a filthy substance, and its removal from garment, body, and place is obligatory if it reaches the preventing amount. Malik said: Sunnah, so one who denies its obligation is not a disbeliever. Its obligation is conditioned upon the possibility without committing what is more severe, such that if he cannot remove it except by exposing his private parts to people, he prays with it because exposing his private parts is more severe. (Fath) The 'anjas' is plural of 'najis' with fat-ha on the jim, and it is more general than 'khabath' which applies to real, and 'hadath' which applies to legal, meaning 'najis' applies to both real and legal. [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/38] 'Purifies the body and garment': If he had expressed it as 'mutanajjis' it would be better to include everything that becomes impure including food. If the edge of a garment becomes impure and he forgets, he washes a part of it without specifying and it is ruled pure in the chosen view. If he sees impurity on his garment and does not know when it struck, the chosen view according to Imam is that he only repeats the prayer he is in. For one who doubts about the place of impurity, he should wash all as a precaution because the place of impurity is not known by conjecture or certainty. (Fath al-Mu'in) 'With water': i.e. absolute water, due to His saying: 'And We sent down from the sky pure water' (Al-Furqan: 48), even if used. 'With a liquid': liquid from 'ma'a' meaning flowed, and its purity is required since its purification of others is conditional upon its own purity. Accordingly, if one washes a heavy impurity with the urine of an edible animal, the description of heaviness is not removed, and that is the chosen view. His saying 'and rose water' even saliva, so he cleans finger and breast by licking three times. (Fath) Rose water and similar when squeezed, Muhammad, Zufar, and Shafi'i said: It is not permissible with other than water, and there is no difference between garment and body. Abu Yusuf said: It is not permissible on the body with other than water. (Miskin) 'Not oil': conjuncted to vinegar, meaning liquid like vinegar, not like oil and milk. (Miskin) And likewise molasses, honey, sesame oil, and ghee, and this is the correct view because these things are not removing by rubbing on the ground in a manner of exaggeration.
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage is the opening of the chapter on impurities (Bāb al-Anjās). The author first distinguishes between ḥukmī (legal) and ḥaqīqī (real) impurity, explaining why the legal impurity is stronger and prioritized in the text. He then states the ruling that purification from real impurity (najāsah) on body, garment, and place is farḍ (obligatory) if the amount reaches that which prevents prayer. Imam Mālik considered it sunnah, but the Ḥanafī position is that it is farḍ, though denial does not make one a kāfir. The passage details that this obligation is conditional—if removal requires exposing one's awrah, it is not required. It then discusses purification with water (absolute water, even if used) and with other pure liquids like vinegar and rose water, but not with oily substances like oil and ghee, as they do not remove impurity effectively. Disagreements are noted: Muḥammad, Zufar, and al-Shāfiʿī prohibit using non-water liquids; Abū Yūsuf prohibits on the body. The Ḥanafī position permits other liquids for garments and some for body, with conditions. The commentary also addresses rules for uncertainty and doubt about impurity location, and the priority of removing impurity over wuḍūʾ when water is limited.

Key Terms
مائع مزيل (mā'iʿ muzīl): Liquid that is pure and effective in removing impurity (e.g., vinegar, rose water).
المطلق (al-muṭlaq): Absolute water; water that is pure and purifying in its original state.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which of the following liquids is NOT valid for removing najasah according to the Hanafi school?
A) Water
B) Vinegar
C) Olive oil
D) Rose water

Key Takeaway
Water is the primary purifier, but other pure and removing liquids like vinegar and rose water can be used; oils and dairy are ineffective.

Purifying the Leather Sock by Rubbing: The Intra-Hanafi Dispute
Ruling on purifying khuff from solid impurity by rubbing

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three Hanafi positions on purifying the khuff from a solid impurity by rubbing, and identify the mufta bihi with its condition.

Core Idea
Rubbing purifies a leather sock from solid impurity even when wet, per the relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf.

When a solid impurity (like mud) touches a leather sock (khuff), can rubbing on the ground purify it? The Hanafi school has three different answers, reflecting a classic intra-madhhab debate. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq presents the dispute and settles on the view of Abu Yusuf, which is the operative ruling for fatwa today.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and the impurity type
The passage concerns a solid impurity (najis dhi jirm) that strikes a khuff. Note that the ruling applies only when the impurity has physical substance (jirm), not liquid impurities like urine.
Solid impurities include mud, blood, or dry faeces.
2
State the three Hanafi positions
List the views of Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, and Muhammad al-Shaybani. Abu Hanifa: rubbing works only if the impurity is dry. Abu Yusuf: works whether wet or dry (mufta bihi). Muhammad: does not work in either case.
The disagreement hinges on whether moisture from a wet solid impurity penetrates the leather.
3
Analyse the proof (dalil) for Abu Yusuf's view
The passage cites the hadith of Ali (ra) where the Prophet (saw) commanded wiping sandals on the ground. The general command (ʿāmm) covers both wet and dry. Understand how the Hanafi usul principle of ʿumūm al-amr supports Abu Yusuf.
The hadith is a dalīl ẓannī al-thubūt but carries weight in fiqh.
4
Examine the objections and responses
Muhammad argues that wetness penetrates, making the surface like a liquid impurity that requires washing. Abu Yusuf responds that the sock is solid and non-absorbent, so only a negligible trace of moisture remains, which is forgiven (ʿafw).
This is an example of takhrīj al-manāṭ: specifying the effective cause (ʿilla) of penetration.
5
Apply the mufta bihi and note the condition
The relied-upon position is Abu Yusuf's view, but with a condition: no visible trace of impurity remains after rubbing, unless removal is extremely difficult (mashaqqa).
This condition is common in Hanafi tahāra rulings – trace must be removed effortfully.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بنجس ذي جرم: أي يطهر الخف بالدلك بإصابة نجس ذي جرم، سواء كان رطباً أو يابساً عند أبي يوسف، وعليه الفتوى بشرط عدم بقاء الأثر، إلا أن يشق زواله؛ لقوله علي: "فمن أراد أن يدخل المسجد فليقلب نعليه، فإن رأى بهما أذى فليمسحهما بالأرض، فإن الأرض لهما طهور، ووجه الاستدلال : أن النبي عليه أطلق فعمّ اليابس والرطب -- كتاب الطهارة ٥٠ باب الأنجاس وإلا يغسل، وبمني يابس بالفرك، وإلا يغسل، ونحو السيف بالمسح، والأرض باليبس
أي ويطهر
وقال محمد: لا يجوز فيهما؛ لأن رطوبته تتداخل في الخف والنعل، فصار كما لو أصابته رطوبتها دون جرمها، وله: ما روينا؛ ولأن الخف صلب لا يتداخله أجزاء جرم النجاسة وإنما يتداخله ،رطوبتها، وذلك قليل، ويجتذبه الجرم إذا جفّ، فلا يبقى بعد المسح إلا قليل، وذلك معفو، وجوزه أبو حنيفة إذا كان يابساً. (فتح) وإلا يغسل: [ أي وإن لم يكن النجس ذا جرم كالبول] مطلقاً سواء كان رطباً أو يابساً مخلوطاً بشيء أو لا، وعن الشيخين أنه إذا لزق به تراب أو رمل وجف يطهر بالدلك. (ط)
With a solid impurity: meaning the leather sock is purified by rubbing if a solid impurity strikes it, whether wet or dry according to Abu Yusuf, and upon this is the fatwa, provided no trace remains unless its removal is difficult, due to the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Whoever wants to enter the mosque, let him turn over his sandals, and if he sees any filth in them, let him wipe them on the ground, for the ground is a purifier for them.' The point of deduction is that the Prophet (peace be upon him) gave a general command including dry and wet. ... And Muhammad said: It is not permissible in either case because its moisture penetrates into the sock and sandal, so it becomes as if its moisture struck without its solid mass. And for him (Abu Yusuf) is what we narrated; and because the sock is solid, the parts of the solid impurity do not penetrate it, only its moisture, and that is little, and the solid mass absorbs it when dry, so after wiping nothing remains but a little, and that is forgiven. And Abu Hanifa allowed it if it is dry. (Fath) 'Otherwise wash': meaning if the impurity is not solid like urine, absolutely whether wet or dry mixed with something or not, and from the two shaykhs (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) that if dirt or sand sticks to it and dries, it is purified by rubbing. (T)
Source pages p. 50

Commentary
This passage discusses the purification of the leather sock (khuff) and similar items from solid impurity. The matn states that such an item is purified by rubbing (dalk) when the impurity has substance (jirm). There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Yusuf allows it whether the impurity is wet or dry, and this is the position on which fatwa is given, provided no trace remains unless removal is difficult. He cites the hadith of Ali regarding wiping sandals on the ground. Muhammad does not allow it because moisture penetrates, but Abu Yusuf argues the sock is solid and only minimal moisture remains. Abu Hanifa allows it only if the impurity is dry. The commentary also clarifies that if the impurity is not solid (e.g., urine), washing is required, except if dirt and sand adhere and dry—then rubbing suffices according to the two shaykhs.

Key Terms
الدلك (al-dalk): Rubbing; a method of purification by friction without water, applicable to solid impurities on solid surfaces.
الخف (al-khuff): Leather sock; a footwear item that, when impure with a solid impurity, can be purified by rubbing.
النجس ذو جرم (al-najis dhu jirm): An impurity that has a solid mass or substance, as opposed to liquid impurities like urine.
العفو (al-ʿafw): Forgiveness in Islamic law; here, the negligible trace of moisture remaining after rubbing is legally excused.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the relied-upon view (mufta bihi) in the Hanafi school, how is a leather sock purified if it comes into contact with a solid impurity?
A) It must be washed with water regardless
B) It is purified by rubbing on the ground whether the impurity is wet or dry
C) It is purified by rubbing only if the impurity is dry
D) It cannot be purified without water

Key Takeaway
The Hanafi school allows rubbing the leather sock on the ground to purify it from a solid impurity even when wet, based on the general command of the hadith and the solid nature of the khuff – a practical concession (rukhṣah) to ease purification.

Purification of Dry Semen by Rubbing (Fark)
Ruling on dry semen purification with disputes

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on purifying dry semen, identify the intra-Hanafi disagreement, and explain the Hanafi response to the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Dry semen is purified by rubbing; wet semen requires washing.

The purification of semen (manī) is a topic of practical significance and also a point of contention between madhhabs. The Hanafi school holds semen to be najis, requiring removal. For dry semen, rubbing suffices; for wet, washing is necessary. This passage from Kanz al-Daqā’iq with its commentary (al-Fatḥ al-Qarīb) presents the ruling and addresses internal and external disputes.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling and method
The matn states that dry semen is purified by rubbing (fark). The commentary explains that rubbing means scraping until it crumbles; any trace remaining does not harm. This applies absolutely, whether on garment or body, thick or thin, male or female.
2
Note the intra-Hanafi dispute
Muhammad restricts rubbing to thick dry semen; Abu Hanifa requires washing on the body. The text says the correct view is the first (absolute rubbing for dry), which is one of two narrations from Abu Hanifa.
This is a difference within the school.
3
Analyze the inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i
Al-Shafi'i considers semen pure (tahir) and only recommends wiping. He cites the hadith comparing semen to mucus and the fact that humans are created from it. The Hanafi response explains that the mucus analogy is about appearance, not ruling, and that impure substances can give rise to pure ones via transformation (istihalah).
The hadith about washing from five things includes semen.
4
Understand the Hanafi argument of istihalah
The Hanafis argue that semen, though impure, is the origin of human creation. They analogize to milk, which is generated from impure blood, yet is pure. Similarly, the human body is created from impure elements but becomes pure through transformation.
Istihalah is a principle of purification in Hanafi fiqh.
5
Apply the ruling in practice
The muftā bihi (relied-upon) view is that dry semen on garment or body is purified by rubbing until it crumbles, even if a trace remains. Wet semen must be washed. This is the operative ruling for fatwa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
بالفرك : [ أي يطهر بالفرك، هو الحط باليد حتى يتفتت ولا يضر بقاء الأثر. (فتح)] مطلقاً سواء كان على الثوب أو على البدن، وسواء كان غليظاً أو رقيقاً، وسواء كان منيه أو منيّها، وعند محمد: إن كان غليظاً فجفٌ يطهر بالفرك، وإلا بالغسل، وعند أبي حنيفة: إذا أصاب البدن لا يطهر إلا بالغسل، والصحيح الأول، وهو إحدى الروايتين عن أبي حنيفة. (فتح) وإلا : أي وإن لم يكن المني يابساً بأن كان رطباً. (ط) يغسل : قال العيني: لقوله علي : فاغسليه إن كان رطباً وافركيه إن كان يابساً [ رمز الحقائق: ٣٩/١] وقال الزيلعي: لقوله عليه: "إنما يغسل الثوب من خمسة وذكر المني، وقال الشافعي: المني طاهر؛ لقوله عليه: "إنما هو كالمخاط وإنما يكفيك أن تمسحه بخرقة أو بإذخرة "، ولأنه مبدأ خلق البشر، فصار كالطين، ولنا: ما روينا، و تشبيهه بالمخاط إنما هو في المنظر والبشاعة لا في الحكم، وقوله عليه: "إنما يكفيك إلخ " محمول على أنه كان قليلاً أو ليتمكن غسله، ويجوز أن يكون البشر من النجس، ثم يطهر بالاستحالة، فإن الشيء قد يكون نجساً ويتولد من
منه الطاهر كاللبن، فإنه متولّد من الدم، فاعتبرناه بالعلقة والمضغة في أنه يخلق منهما البشر وإن كانا نجسين. (فتح)
By rubbing (fark): meaning it is purified by rubbing, which is scraping with the hand until it crumbles, and the trace remaining does not harm. (Fath) Absolutely, whether on garment or on body, whether thick or thin, whether his semen or hers. According to Muhammad: if it is thick and dry, it is purified by rubbing, otherwise by washing. According to Abu Hanifa: if it strikes the body, it is not purified except by washing. The correct view is the first, and it is one of the two narrations from Abu Hanifa. (Fath) 'Otherwise': meaning if the semen is not dry, i.e., wet. (T) 'Wash': al-'Ayni said: due to the statement of Ali (may Allah be pleased with him): 'Wash it if it is wet and rub it if it is dry.' [Ramz al-Haqa'iq: 1/39] And al-Zayla'i said: due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'The garment is washed from five things' and he mentioned semen. Al-Shafi'i said: semen is pure; due to his statement (peace be upon him): 'It is only like mucus and it suffices for you to wipe it with a cloth or with a piece of izkhir.' And because it is the origin of human creation, so it is like clay. And for us: what we narrated, and the analogy to mucus is only in appearance and offensiveness, not in ruling. And his statement (peace be upon him): 'It suffices for you' etc. is interpreted as it being little or to facilitate its washing. And it is possible that the human is created from impure substance, then becomes pure by transformation, for an object may be impure yet from it emerges a pure thing like milk, which is generated from blood. So we analogize it to the clot and the chewed flesh in that humans are created from them although they are impure. (Fath)
Source pages p. 51

Commentary
This passage details the purification of semen (manī). The matn states that dry semen is purified by rubbing (fark), while wet semen requires washing. The commentary explains that rubbing means scraping until the impurity crumbles; the trace remaining is forgiven. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Muhammad restricts rubbing to thick dry semen; Abu Hanifa requires washing if on the body; but the correct view according to the text is that rubbing is sufficient absolutely (on garment and body, thin or thick). The passage then presents an inter-madhhab dispute with al-Shafi'i, who considers semen pure and only recommends wiping. The Hanafi response is that the hadith about mucus is only about appearance, and the hadith about washing from five things includes semen. They argue that semen is originally impure but can become pure through transformation (istihāla), similar to milk from blood.

Key Terms
الفرك (al-fark): Rubbing; specifically for dry semen, scraping with hand until crumbled.
الاستحالة (al-istihalah): Transformation; an impure substance becomes pure when it changes into another substance (e.g., milk from blood).

Key Terms from Source Passage

D) It is purified only if it is thick and dry

Key Takeaway
Dry semen is purified by rubbing until it crumbles; this applies absolutely and is the relied-upon Hanafi position, supported by hadith and the principle of istihalah.
