yؤكل لحمه، والفرس، وخرء طير لا يؤكل لحمه ودم السمك، ولعاب البغل والحمار،
أي عفي لعابهما
وبول ما لا يؤكل إلا بول الخفاش وخرءه، فإنه طاهر وخرء الفارة إذا طحن في الحنطة جاز أكل الدقيق ما لم يظهر أثر الخرء فيه. (فتح) والروث [سواء كان روث مأكول أو غيره، وهو عذرة ذي حافر. (ط،ع)] أي مطلقا، وإن كان روث ما يؤكل كروث بغل أمه بقرة، أو ذئب أمّه شاة، وبعر الإبل والغنم غليظ عنده، خفيف عندهما، ومرارة كل شيء كبوله وجرة البعير ،كسرقينه وكذا جرة الغنم والبقر والجرة: ما يخرجه الحيوان من ذوات الظلف من جوفه بعد أكله ثم يعيده قوله والخثى" أي عند أبي حنيفة وعندهما: خفيفة، وفرق بين المأكول وغيره زفر وقال روث ما لا يؤكل غليظة كبوله، وروث ما يؤكل خفيفة كبوله، وذكر في "الذخيرة" وغيرها: أن الأرواث كلها طاهرة عند زفر، فكأن له روايتين، وعن محمد: أن الروث لا يمنع وإن كان كثيراً فاحشاً، وقال مشايخنا على قياس رواية محمد طين بخارا لا يمنع جواز الصلاة وإن كان كثيراً فاحشاً مع أن التراب مخلوط بالعذرات؛ لعموم البلوى، وعدم إمكان الاحتراز عنه. (فتح، مسكين) والخثى بكسر الخاء المعجمة وسكون المثلثة، وهي عذرة ذي ظلف وعندهما نجاسة الروث والخثى خفيفة وكذا بعر الإبل والغنم (ط، ع) وما دون ربع الثوب: أي ربع أدنى ثوب تجوز فيه الصلاة كالميزر، وقيل: ربع الموضع الذي أصابه كالذيل والدخريص، وهو الأصح، وعن أبي يوسف: أنه شبر في شبر، أي شبر طولاً وشبر عرضاً. (مسكين) ربع الثوب: وعندهما نجاسة الروث والخثى خفيفة، وكذا بعر الإبل والغنم. كبول ما يؤكل إلخ: فإنه مخفف، أما عند أبي حنيفة فلتعارض النصين في حله وحرمته، فإن قوله علية: "إستنزهوا من "البول" يعارض قوله للعرنيين: اشربوا أبوالها"، وأما عند أبي يوسف فلا اختلاف، وكذا بول الفرس؛ لأن لحمه مأكول عنده ويكره للتبرك، وأما خرء طير لا يوكل فعندهما مخففة وعند محمد مغلظة، له: أنها تخالط النجاسة ولا ضرورة فيها؛ لعدم مخالطتها الناس ولهما أنها تزرق من الهواء، والتحامي عنه متعذر، فتحقق الضرورة. (مستخلص) لا يؤكل كالصقر والبازي، وعند محمد كلها طاهرة، وأما خرء طير يوكل لحمه فطاهر اتفاقاً إلا الدجاج والبط والإوز. ودم السمك: عطف على قوله : "قدر الدرهم" وعفي دم السمك وعن أبي . يوسف: أنه نجس بنجاسة خفيفة؛ لوجود صورة الدم، ولهما أنه ليس بدم حقيقة فلا يكون نجسا ، بل هو طاهر في ظاهر الرواية؛ لأن الدموي لا يسكن في الماء، ولأنه يحل بلا ذكاة مع أن الذكاة شرعت لإراقة الدم المسفوح، وكذا تبيض بالشمس، ومن خاصية الدم أنه تسود بالشمس. وعلى هذا عطفه على قدر الدرهم لا وجه له؛ لأن ذلك يقتضى التنجس. (عيني، مستخلص) ولعاب البغل لأنه مشكوك فيه فلا يتنجس به الطاهر كما لا يطهر به النجاسة الحكمية، وهو والجنابة، وهذا أيضاً مشكل؛ لأن لعابهما طاهر عندهما، وعند أبي يوسف نجس مخفف. [رمز الحقائق: ٤٠/١]
الحدث
The Book of Purification. Statement of what is excused from impurity. And urine of what whose meat is not eaten, and dung, and semi-solid dung, and less than a quarter of the garment of light impurity like urine of what whose meat is eaten, the complete one in the correct view, and the horse, and droppings of bird whose meat is not eaten, and fish blood, and saliva of the mule and donkey: it means their saliva is excused. And urine of what whose meat is not eaten, except the urine of the bat and its droppings, for it is pure, and mouse droppings if ground in wheat, eating the flour is permissible as long as the trace of the droppings does not appear. (Fath) And dung, whether it is dung of an edible or other, and it is the excrement of a hoofed animal. (T,A) meaning absolutely, even if it is dung of what is eaten like dung of a mule whose mother is a cow, or a wolf whose mother is a sheep, and camel and sheep pellets: thick according to him, light according to them both. And the bile of everything is like its urine, and the cud of the camel like its dung, and likewise the cud of sheep and cows. And cud is what the animal with cleft hoofs brings out from its belly after eating and then returns. His saying 'and al-khathī' i.e. according to Abu Hanifa it is light, and according to them both it is light, and Zufar made a distinction between edible and other. And he said: dung of what is not eaten is thick like its urine, and dung of what is eaten is light like its urine. And it is mentioned in al-Dhakhira and others that all dungs are pure according to Zufar, so he seems to have two narrations. And from Muhammad: that dung does not prevent (the validity of prayer) even if it is abundant and excessive. And our scholars said on the analogy of Muhammad's narration: the clay of Bukhara does not prevent the permissibility of prayer even if it is abundant and excessive, despite the soil being mixed with excrements, due to general affliction and the impossibility of avoiding it. (Fath, Miskin) And al-khathī (broken kha and silent tha) is the excrement of a cleft-hoofed animal. And according to them both, the impurity of dung and khathī is light, and likewise camel and sheep pellets. (T,A) And less than a quarter of the garment: i.e. a quarter of the smallest garment in which prayer is permissible, like an izār; and it is said: a quarter of the place that was hit, like the hem and the tail, and this is the most correct. And from Abu Yusuf: that it is a handspan by a handspan, i.e. a handspan length and a handspan width. (Miskin) A quarter of the garment: and according to them both, the impurity of dung and khathī is light, and likewise camel and sheep pellets. Like urine of what is eaten etc.: for it is light. As for Abu Hanifa, due to the conflict of the two texts regarding its permissibility and prohibition, for his saying, peace be upon him: 'Purify yourselves from urine' conflicts with his saying to the Urayniyyīn: 'Drink their urine.' As for Abu Yusuf, there is no conflict. And likewise the urine of the horse, because its meat is eaten according to him, and it is disliked for seeking blessing. As for the droppings of a bird that is not eaten, according to them both it is light, and according to Muhammad it is heavy. His argument: they mix with impurity and there is no necessity in it because they are not mixed with people. And their argument: they drop from the air, and avoiding them is difficult, so necessity is realized. (Mustakhlas) Not eaten, like the falcon and the hawk, and according to Muhammad all of them are pure. As for the droppings of a bird whose meat is eaten, it is pure by agreement, except chicken, duck, and goose. And fish blood: it is a conjunction on his saying 'the amount of a dirham' and fish blood is excused. And from Abu Yusuf: that it is impure with light impurity due to the existence of the form of blood. And according to them both, it is not truly blood, so it is not impure; rather it is pure in the apparent narration, because blood does not reside in water, and because it is lawful without slaughter, whereas slaughter was legislated to spill the effused blood; and likewise it is dried in the sun, and it is a property of blood to turn black in the sun. And upon this, its conjunction with 'amount of a dirham' has no basis, because that would necessitate impurity. (Ayni, Mustakhlas) And the saliva of the mule because it is doubtful; so the pure is not made impure by it, just as it does not purify legal impurity, and it is and janābah; and this is also problematic, because their saliva is pure according to them both, and according to Abu Yusuf it is light impurity. [Ramz al-Haqā'iq: 1/40]
Source pages p. 53

Commentary
This passage is a statement of what impurities are excused (ma'fu 'anhu) in Hanafi fiqh. It begins with the urine of animals whose meat is not eaten—this is excused in small amounts. Similarly, dung (rawth) and semi-solid dung (khathī) are excused, but there are differences among Hanafi imams. Abu Hanifa considers dung of all animals as thick impurity (maghlazah), while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad consider it light (mukhaffafah). Zufar holds all dungs to be pure. The amount excused is less than a quarter of the garment, with the correct view being a quarter of the area affected. For drops of urine and other light impurities, the excused amount is less than a quarter of the garment. The passage also discusses the urine of the horse (disliked but not impure according to Abu Yusuf), droppings of birds (light according to the Sahibayn, heavy according to Muhammad), fish blood (pure according to Sahibayn, light impurity according to Abu Yusuf), and saliva of the mule and donkey (pure according to Sahibayn, light impurity according to Abu Yusuf). The overriding principle is that these are excused due to necessity (darurah) or general affliction (umum al-balwa).

Key Terms
الروث (al-rawth): Dung of hoofed animals.
الخثى (al-khathī): Semi-solid dung of cleft-hoofed animals.
المخفف (al-mukhaffaf): Light impurity, such as dung according to Sahibayn.
المغلظ (al-mughallaz): Thick impurity, such as dung according to Abu Hanifa.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the mufta bihi in the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on camel dung?
A) It is pure (tahir).
B) It is a thick impurity (maghlazah).
C) It is a light impurity (mukhaffafah).
D) It is not najis at all.

Key Takeaway
The mufta bihi is that dung is a light impurity, so the quarter rule applies; special exceptions exist for situations of widespread difficulty.

Taharah — Purification
beginner
6 min
Purification of Visible Impurity
Defines visible impurity and its purification rule

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the definition of visible impurity and explain its purification method, including the exception for traces that are difficult to remove.

Core Idea
Visible impurity is removed by eliminating its essence; hardship pardons the stain that resists water.

Impurity in Islamic law is of two kinds: visible and non-visible. This lesson focuses on visible impurity—that which leaves a tangible trace. The Hanafi school provides a clear, practical rule: the essence must go, but if a stubborn stain remains, it is forgiven. We also examine the case of splashed urine, where minimal unavoidable impurity is pardoned entirely.

Guided Path
1
Define Visible Impurity
Identify the definition given in the text: 'that which one sees its essence after drying.' Note that the essence (عين) is the key consideration.
The text explicitly states that impurity settles by consideration of the essence.
2
State the Purification Rule
The rule is removal of the essence. Once the essence is gone, the surface is pure. This is the basic hukm.
3
Identify the Exception
If a trace remains that is difficult to remove (e.g., requiring soap), it is pardoned. The principle of hardship (حرج) is invoked.
The exception is not for the essence itself but for the aftereffect.
4
Apply to Splashed Urine
Analyze the case of urine that splashes in tiny amounts (like needle tips). Such impurity is pardoned because avoidance is impossible, per the Hadith of Ibn Abbas.
This is an example of the broader principle of pardon for unavoidable minimal impurity.
5
Contrast with Non-Visible Impurity
Recognize that visible impurity is purified differently from non-visible; the next lesson will cover the latter.
This step sets the stage for the sequel.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
كتاب الطهارة
طريق تطهير النجاسة
المرئي
وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس المرئي يطهر بزوال عينه إلا ما يشق زواله، وغيره وأثره بالغسل ثلاثاً والعصر كل مرة، وبتثليث الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر. وسن الاستنجاء بنحو

وقال الشافعي يغسل مرة

وهو
وبول انتضح: [يعني عفي الأجزاء التي تنتضح على الخف وغيره من البول مطلقاً مثل رؤوس الإبر حتى لا يجب غسلها وتجوز الصلاة معها، والرأس والجانب الآخر من الإبر سواء. (مسكين)] أي معفو عنه؛ لأنه لا يستطاع الامتناع عنه، وقد سئل ابن عباس عن ذلك، فقال: إنا نرجو عفو الله أوسع من ذلك، وعن أبي يوسف: إذا انتضح من البول شيء يرى أثره لا بد من غسله وإن لم يغسل حتى صلى معه وهو بحال لو جمع لكان أكثر من قدر الدرهم أعاد الصلاة. ثم إن هذا الثوب لو وقع في الماء القليل قال بعض مشايخنا: إن قيل: لا الماء، فله ينجس وجه؛ لأن اعتبار هذه النجاسة لما سقط عن الثوب سقط فله الماء جميعاً، وإن قيل: ينجس، عن الأصح؛ لأن سقوط اعتبار النجاسة إنما كان لدفع الحرج ولا حرج في الماء فيتنجس. (مستخلص) والنجس المرئي: يعني أن النجاسة على ضربين: مرئية وغير مرئية، فالمرئية ما يرى عينه بعد الجفاف، وطهارته بزوال عينها؛ لأن النجاسة حلت المحل باعتبار العين، فتزول بزوالها، إلا أن يبقى من أثرها ما يشق زوالها؛ لأن الحرج مدفوع، والنجاسة التي ليست لها عين مرئية فطهارتها أن يغسل ثلاثاً؛ لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج كما ورد في حديث المستيقظ، فإنه عليه أمر بالغسل ثلاث مرات في النجاسة الموهومة، ففي المتحققة أولى، ثم لا بد من العصر في كل مرة في ظاهر الرواية، فإن العصر هو المستخرج، وعن محمد: إذا غسلت ثلاثاً وعصرت في المرة الثالثة تطهر. (مستخلص) إلا ما يشق زواله أي الأثر الذي يشق زواله بأن يحتاج في إزالته إلى شيء غير الماء كالصابون والأشنان، فإنه معفو عنه وإن كان كثيراً. (ط) كل مرة ويبالغ في المرة الثالثة حتى لو عصر بعده لا يسيل منه شيء، ويعتبر في كل شخص قوته. (مسكين) وبتثليث الجفاف: اعلم أن الأواني ثلاثة أقسام: خزف وخشب وحديد ونحوها، وتطهير كل منها على طرق: حرق ونحت ومسح وغسل، فإن كان الإناء من خزف أو حجر أو كان حديداً ودخلت النجاسة في أجزائه يحرق، وإن كان عتيقا يغسل، وإن كان من خشب وكان جديداً ينحت وإن كان قديماً يغسل، وإن كان من نحاس أو صفر أو رصاص أو زجاج، وكان صقيلا يمسح، وإن كان خشناً يغسل، وفي "عمدة الفتاوى": نجاسة يابسة على الحصير ،تفرك وفي الرطبة يجرى عليه الماء ثلاثاً، والإجراء كالعصر؛ لأن العصر متعذر، فقام التوالي في الغسل مقام العصر، وقوله : "فيما لا ينعصر" أي يغسل ثلاث مرات في شيء لا ينعصر ، ويجفف في كل مرة بأن ينقطع التقاطر، ولا يشترط له اليبس، ولو موّه سكين بماء نجس يموه بالماء الطاهر ثلاثاً بتثليث الجفاف، وقال محمد: لا يطهر أبداً، والفتوى على الطهارة. (فتح)
Book of Purification
Method of Purifying Impurity
Visible
And urine that splashes like needle tips, and visible impurity is purified by the removal of its essence except what is difficult to remove, and other than that and its trace by washing three times and wringing each time, and by three-time drying for what is not wringable. And it is sunnah to perform istinja with something like...

And al-Shafi'i said: wash once...
...
And splashed urine: [meaning pardoned are the particles that splash on the leather sock and other than it from urine absolutely, like needle tips, so that washing them is not obligatory and prayer is permissible with them, and the head and the other side of the needle are equal. (Miskin)] i.e., it is pardoned because it cannot be avoided, and Ibn Abbas was asked about that, so he said: We hope for Allah's pardon broader than that. And from Abu Yusuf: If something of urine splashes and its effect is seen, washing it is necessary, and if he does not wash and prays with it while it is such that if collected it would be more than the size of a dirham, he repeats the prayer. Then if this garment falls into a small amount of water, some of our scholars said: If it is said it does not make the water impure, there is a face, because the consideration of this impurity fell from the garment, so the water is all pure; and if it is said it becomes impure, it is more correct, because the dropping of consideration of impurity is only to repel hardship, and there is no hardship in water, so it becomes impure. (Mustakhlas) And visible impurity: means that impurity is of two types: visible and non-visible. The visible is what one sees its essence after drying, and its purification is by removal of its essence, because impurity settled in the place by consideration of the essence, so it goes away by its removal, except what remains of its trace that is difficult to remove, because hardship is repelled. And impurity that has no visible essence, its purification is to wash three times, because repetition is necessary for extraction as came in the hadith of the one who wakes up, for he (peace be upon him) ordered washing three times for imagined impurity, so for actual impurity it is more appropriate. Then wringing is necessary each time in the apparent narration, because wringing is the extractor. And from Muhammad: If it is washed three times and wrung the third time, it becomes pure. (Mustakhlas) Except what is difficult to remove, i.e., the trace that is difficult to remove because it needs something other than water like soap and potash, then it is pardoned even if abundant. (T) Each time, and he exaggerates in the third time such that if he wrings after it nothing flows from it, and consideration is given to each person's strength. (Miskin) And three-time drying: Know that vessels are three types: pottery, wood, iron and the like, and the purification of each is by methods: burning, carving, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of pottery or stone or iron and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if it is old, it is washed; if it is of wood and new, it is carved, and if old, it is washed; if it is of copper, brass, lead, or glass, and it is polished, it is wiped, and if rough, it is washed. And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: Dry impurity on a mat is rubbed, and for wet, water is run over it three times, and running is like wringing, because wringing is impossible, so successive pouring in washing takes the place of wringing. And His saying: "in what is not wringable" means it is washed three times in something that cannot be wrung, and dried each time such that dripping stops, and complete dryness is not required. And if a knife is coated with impure water, it is coated with pure water three times with three-time drying, and Muhammad said: it never becomes pure, and the fatwa is on purity. (Fath)
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage on purification methods opens by distinguishing two types of impurity: visible (مرئي) and non-visible. For visible impurity (e.g., blood, wine), purification is achieved by the complete removal of the essence (عين النجاسة) from the surface. However, if some trace remains that is difficult to remove (like a stain requiring soap), it is pardoned due to the principle of hardship removal (رفع الحرج). For non-visible impurity (e.g., urine that leaves no trace), the required purification is to wash the affected area three times, with wringing after each wash in the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية). This is based on the hadith of the person who wakes up and finds a wet spot, where the Prophet ﷺ ordered washing three times for imagined impurity; it is even more applicable for actual impurity. Imam Muhammad has a narration that wringing is only required on the third wash. The passage then addresses a case of splashed urine (بول انتضح) that lands on clothing or leather socks in amounts like needle tips; this is pardoned because it cannot be avoided, per the practice of Ibn Abbas and the principle of necessity. A dispute among later Hanafi scholars about a garment with such pardoned najasah falling into a small amount of water: the preferred view (الأصح) is that the water becomes impure because the hardship that justified pardoning the najasah on the garment does not apply to the water. Finally, the passage discusses vessels: different materials (pottery, wood, iron, etc.) require different purification methods—burning, carving, wiping, or washing. For items that cannot be wrung (e.g., mats), drying between washes substitutes for wringing. The fatwa is given on the purificatory effect of three-time drying even for knives coated with impure water, contrary to Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
النجس المرئي (al-najis al-mar'iy): Impurity that has a visible essence (عين) that can be seen after drying.
العين (al-'ayn): The physical substance or essence of the impurity that is perceptible to the eye.
الحرج (al-haraj): Hardship or difficulty; the principle that hardship brings ease in Islamic rulings.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the purification method for visible impurity?
A) Washing three times with wringing
B) Removal of the essence (عين)
C) Drying in the sun
D) Wiping with a dry cloth

Key Takeaway
Visible impurity is removed by eliminating its physical essence, and any leftover stain that is hard to remove is excused.

Taharah — Purification

Purification of Non-Visible Impurity with Wringing
Explains purification of non-visible impurity with proof and intra-Hanafi variant

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the Hanafi method for purifying non-visible impurity: three washes with wringing each time (in the apparent narration), and apply it to wringable and non-wringable items.

Core Idea
Non-visible impurity requires three washes with wringing; wringing extracts impurity and is wajib in each wash.

When impurity leaves no visible trace—like dried urine on a fabric—the Hanafi school prescribes a specific washing procedure. This lesson unpacks the method: three washes, each followed by wringing, based on the hadith of the awakening person. We also explore the intra-Hanafi difference (Imam Muhammad’s view), the Shafi'i opposition, and the alternative of three-time drying for items that cannot be wrung.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Impurity Type
First, confirm we are dealing with non-visible impurity—no trace remains after the spot dries. The text defines it as 'that which has no visible essence.'
This category includes clear urine, diluted wine, etc.
2
State the Basic Rule: Three Washes
The purification is by washing three times. The reason given is that repetition is needed for extraction, as shown by the hadith.
The hadith is about imagined impurity; actual impurity is even more deserving.
3
Add the Requirement of Wringing
In the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية), wringing after each wash is wajib because wringing extracts the impurity. This is the mufta bihi position.
Intra-Hanafi difference: Imam Muhammad only requires wringing on the third wash.
4
Understand the Proof and Response to Shafi'i
The proof is the hadith of the awakening person (حديث المستيقظ). The command to wash three times for imagined impurity is applied to actual impurity. Al-Shafi'i holds that one wash suffices, but Hanafi argues that repetition is necessary for certainty.
This is a dalil naqli with a priority (فحوى الخطاب) argument.
5
Apply to Non-Wringable Items
For items like mats or rough vessels, wringing is impossible. Instead, three-time drying (تثليث الجفاف) is used, where the item is dried between washes until dripping stops. This substitutes for wringing.
The guidance on vessels: different materials have different methods (burning, carving, wiping, washing).

Source Text

المرئي
وبول انتضح كرؤوس الإبر والنجس المرئي يطهر بزوال عينه إلا ما يشق زواله، وغيره وأثره بالغسل ثلاثاً والعصر كل مرة، وبتثليث الجفاف فيما لا ينعصر. وسن الاستنجاء بنحو

وقال الشافعي يغسل مرة

وجه

وهو
وبول انتضح: [يعني عفي الأجزاء التي تنتضح على الخف وغيره من البول مطلقاً مثل رؤوس الإبر حتى لا يجب غسلها وتجوز الصلاة معها، والرأس والجانب الآخر من الإبر سواء. (مسكين)] أي معفو عنه؛ لأنه لا يستطاع الامتناع عنه، وقد سئل ابن عباس عن ذلك، فقال: إنا نرجو عفو الله أوسع من ذلك، وعن أبي يوسف: إذا انتضح من البول شيء يرى أثره لا بد من غسله وإن لم يغسل حتى صلى معه وهو بحال لو جمع لكان أكثر من قدر الدرهم أعاد الصلاة. ثم إن هذا الثوب لو وقع في الماء القليل قال بعض مشايخنا: إن قيل: لا الماء، فله ينجس وجه؛ لأن اعتبار هذه النجاسة لما سقط عن الثوب سقط فله الماء جميعاً، وإن قيل: ينجس، عن الأصح؛ لأن سقوط اعتبار النجاسة إنما كان لدفع الحرج ولا حرج في الماء فيتنجس. (مستخلص) والنجس المرئي: يعني أن النجاسة على ضربين: مرئية وغير مرئية، فالمرئية ما يرى عينه بعد الجفاف، وطهارته بزوال عينها؛ لأن النجاسة حلت المحل باعتبار العين، فتزول بزوالها، إلا أن يبقى من أثرها ما يشق زوالها؛ لأن الحرج مدفوع، والنجاسة التي ليست لها عين مرئية فطهارتها أن يغسل ثلاثاً؛ لأن التكرار لا بد منه للاستخراج كما ورد في حديث المستيقظ، فإنه عليه أمر بالغسل ثلاث مرات في النجاسة الموهومة، ففي المتحققة أولى، ثم لا بد من العصر في كل مرة في ظاهر الرواية، فإن العصر هو المستخرج، وعن محمد: إذا غسلت ثلاثاً وعصرت في المرة الثالثة تطهر. (مستخلص) إلا ما يشق زواله أي الأثر الذي يشق زواله بأن يحتاج في إزالته إلى شيء غير الماء كالصابون والأشنان، فإنه معفو عنه وإن كان كثيراً. (ط) كل مرة ويبالغ في المرة الثالثة حتى لو عصر بعده لا يسيل منه شيء، ويعتبر في كل شخص قوته. (مسكين) وبتثليث الجفاف: اعلم أن الأواني ثلاثة أقسام: خزف وخشب وحديد ونحوها، وتطهير كل منها على طرق: حرق ونحت ومسح وغسل، فإن كان الإناء من خزف أو حجر أو كان حديداً ودخلت النجاسة في أجزائه يحرق، وإن كان عتيقا يغسل، وإن كان من خشب وكان جديداً ينحت وإن كان قديماً يغسل، وإن كان من نحاس أو صفر أو رصاص أو زجاج، وكان صقيلا يمسح، وإن كان خشناً يغسل، وفي "عمدة الفتاوى": نجاسة يابسة على الحصير ،تفرك وفي الرطبة يجرى عليه الماء ثلاثاً، والإجراء كالعصر؛ لأن العصر متعذر، فقام التوالي في الغسل مقام العصر، وقوله : "فيما لا ينعصر" أي يغسل ثلاث مرات في شيء لا ينعصر ، ويجفف في كل مرة بأن ينقطع التقاطر، ولا يشترط له اليبس، ولو موّه سكين بماء نجس يموه بالماء الطاهر ثلاثاً بتثليث الجفاف، وقال محمد: لا يطهر أبداً، والفتوى على الطهارة. (فتح)
Book of Purification
Method of Purifying Impurity
Visible
And urine that splashes like needle tips, and visible impurity is purified by the removal of its essence except what is difficult to remove, and other than that and its trace by washing three times and wringing each time, and by three-time drying for what is not wringable. And it is sunnah to perform istinja with something like...

And al-Shafi'i said: wash once...
...
And splashed urine: [meaning pardoned are the particles that splash on the leather sock and other than it from urine absolutely, like needle tips, so that washing them is not obligatory and prayer is permissible with them, and the head and the other side of the needle are equal. (Miskin)] i.e., it is pardoned because it cannot be avoided, and Ibn Abbas was asked about that, so he said: We hope for Allah's pardon broader than that. And from Abu Yusuf: If something of urine splashes and its effect is seen, washing it is necessary, and if he does not wash and prays with it while it is such that if collected it would be more than the size of a dirham, he repeats the prayer. Then if this garment falls into a small amount of water, some of our scholars said: If it is said it does not make the water impure, there is a face, because the consideration of this impurity fell from the garment, so the water is all pure; and if it is said it becomes impure, it is more correct, because the dropping of consideration of impurity is only to repel hardship, and there is no hardship in water, so it becomes impure. (Mustakhlas) And visible impurity: means that impurity is of two types: visible and non-visible. The visible is what one sees its essence after drying, and its purification is by removal of its essence, because impurity settled in the place by consideration of the essence, so it goes away by its removal, except what remains of its trace that is difficult to remove, because hardship is repelled. And impurity that has no visible essence, its purification is to wash three times, because repetition is necessary for extraction as came in the hadith of the one who wakes up, for he (peace be upon him) ordered washing three times for imagined impurity, so for actual impurity it is more appropriate. Then wringing is necessary each time in the apparent narration, because wringing is the extractor. And from Muhammad: If it is washed three times and wrung the third time, it becomes pure. (Mustakhlas) Except what is difficult to remove, i.e., the trace that is difficult to remove because it needs something other than water like soap and potash, then it is pardoned even if abundant. (T) Each time, and he exaggerates in the third time such that if he wrings after it nothing flows from it, and consideration is given to each person's strength. (Miskin) And three-time drying: Know that vessels are three types: pottery, wood, iron and the like, and the purification of each is by methods: burning, carving, wiping, and washing. If the vessel is of pottery or stone or iron and impurity entered its parts, it is burned; if it is old, it is washed; if it is of wood and new, it is carved, and if old, it is washed; if it is of copper, brass, lead, or glass, and it is polished, it is wiped, and if rough, it is washed. And in 'Umdat al-Fatawa: Dry impurity on a mat is rubbed, and for wet, water is run over it three times, and running is like wringing, because wringing is impossible, so successive pouring in washing takes the place of wringing. And His saying: "in what is not wringable" means it is washed three times in something that cannot be wrung, and dried each time such that dripping stops, and complete dryness is not required. And if a knife is coated with impure water, it is coated with pure water three times with three-time drying, and Muhammad said: it never becomes pure, and the fatwa is on purity. (Fath)
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage on purification methods opens by distinguishing two types of impurity: visible (مرئي) and non-visible. For visible impurity (e.g., blood, wine), purification is achieved by the complete removal of the essence (عين النجاسة) from the surface. However, if some trace remains that is difficult to remove (like a stain requiring soap), it is pardoned due to the principle of hardship removal (رفع الحرج). For non-visible impurity (e.g., urine that leaves no trace), the required purification is to wash the affected area three times, with wringing after each wash in the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية). This is based on the hadith of the person who wakes up and finds a wet spot, where the Prophet ﷺ ordered washing three times for imagined impurity; it is even more applicable for actual impurity. Imam Muhammad has a narration that wringing is only required on the third wash. The passage then addresses a case of splashed urine (بول انتضح) that lands on clothing or leather socks in amounts like needle tips; this is pardoned because it cannot be avoided, per the practice of Ibn Abbas and the principle of necessity. A dispute among later Hanafi scholars about a garment with such pardoned najasah falling into a small amount of water: the preferred view (الأصح) is that the water becomes impure because the hardship that justified pardoning the najasah on the garment does not apply to the water. Finally, the passage discusses vessels: different materials (pottery, wood, iron, etc.) require different purification methods—burning, carving, wiping, or washing. For items that cannot be wrung (e.g., mats), drying between washes substitutes for wringing. The fatwa is given on the purificatory effect of three-time drying even for knives coated with impure water, contrary to Imam Muhammad's view.

Key Terms
النجاسة غير المرئية (al-najasah ghayr al-mar'iyyah): Impurity that has no visible essence; cannot be seen after drying.
العصر (al-'asr): Wringing or squeezing the fabric to extract the water containing impurity.
تثليث الجفاف (tathlith al-jafaf): Three-time drying, i.e., drying the item between washes for items that cannot be wrung.
ظاهر الرواية (zahir al-riwayah): The apparent narration, referring to the authoritative transmission from the early Hanafi masters (Abu Hanifa, Abu Yusuf, Muhammad) in the six major books.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the apparent narration (ظاهر الرواية) in this passage, what is the requirement for wringing in the purification of non-visible impurity?
A) Wringing is not required at all
B) Wringing is required only on the third wash
C) Wringing is required after each of the three washes
D) Wringing is required but only if the impurity is visible

Key Takeaway
Non-visible impurity requires three washes with wringing each time (mufta bihi); for non-wringable items, three-time drying substitutes.

Taharah — Purification
intermediate
10 min
Istinja' Rulings and the Three Stones Dispute
Rulings, prohibitions, and an inter-madhhab dispute on istinja'

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on the number of stones for istinja', explain why it is sunnah not fard, and distinguish the Hanafi position from the Shafi'i position.

Core Idea
Three stones are recommended, not required—the dispute is about whether the number is fard or sunnah.

Istinja' is the cleansing of the private parts after relieving oneself. While the Hanafi school emphasizes its status as a confirmed sunnah, a key difference with the Shafi'i school arises over the number of stones: is three obligatory or merely recommended? This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies the Hanafi position, the evidence, and the broader etiquettes of istinja'.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position on istinja' and three stones
Identify that according to the Hanafi school, using three stones is sunnah muakkadah (recommended), not fard (obligatory). The number itself is not required; oddness is preferred.
Al-Shafi'i holds that three stones are fard—if one omits them, prayer becomes invalid.
2
Identify the Shafi'i position and its proof
Find the hadith cited by al-Shafi'i: 'When one of you relieves himself, let him perform istinja with three stones.' Understand that a command (amr) in Shafi'i usul indicates obligation.
3
Follow the Hanafi reconciliation (ta'wil)
Examine the Hanafi proof: 'Whoever uses stones, let him use an odd number; whoever does good, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' This shows that omission is permissible, so the command in the other hadith is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab) to reconcile the two.
Hanafi usul allows moving an amr from wujub to nadb when there is evidence of permitted omission.
4
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
What is the practical difference? For Hanafis, using one or two stones makes istinja' valid and prayer correct; for Shafi'is, if one deliberately uses less than three, the prayer is invalid.
This matters in everyday practice, especially when water or stones are limited.
5
Note the broader istinja' rulings from the passage
Scan the rest of the passage for key rules: istinja' is sunnah muakkadah; water is preferable and becomes obligatory if impurity spreads; prohibited materials include bone, dung, food, and right hand; etiquettes include avoiding qibla, speaking, and urinating standing.
These are additional rulings that complete the fiqh of istinja'.

لأنه إسراف للنهي :
عنه
وما سن فيه عدد المنقى هو اللزوم في إقامة هذه السنة لا نفس العدد، كما قال الشافعي: إنه لا بد فيه من ثلاثة أحجار أو حجر له ثلاثة أحرف؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا أتى أحدكم حاجته فليستنج بثلاثة أحجار أو ثلاثة أعواد أو ثلاث خشبات، ولنا قوله عليه من استجمر فليوتر من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج"، والتنصيص على ذكر الثلاث في الحديث الآخر محمول على أن الأمر فيه للاستحباب جمعاً وتوفيقاً، والعدد عند الشافعي فرض
حتى لو تركه لا تجوز صلاته فتح وغيره وغسله أي موضع الاستنجاء بالماء، إن أمكنه بلا كشف عورة. أحب وأفضل، وإلا حرم الكشف مطلقاً ويكون فاسقاً بالكشف وقيل: الغسل سنة في زماننا.(مسكين، ط)]؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وفِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا (التوبة: ۱۰۸) نزل في قوم كانوا يتبعون الأحجار ثم الماء، وهو أدب، وقيل: سنة في زماننا، فيغسل بالماء إلى أن تقع في قلبه أنه قد طهر. ويجب إلخ أي يجب الغسل بالماء إذا تجاوز النجاسة مخرجها؛ لأن المسح بالحجر غير مزيل للنجاسة، إلا أنه اكتفي به في موضع الاستنجاء على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس عليه غيره، وكذا لو لم يجاوز وكان جنباً يجب الاستنجاء بالماء؛ لوجوب غسل المقعد لأجل الجنابة، وكذا الحائض والنفساء. (فتح، مستخلص موضع الاستنجاء قيد به؛ لأن النجاسة لو كانت أقل بحيث لو ضم هذا
إلى موضع الاستنجاء يصير أكثر من قدر الدرهم يكفيه الاستنجاء عندهما، وعند محمد يفرض غسله. (مسكين) لا بعظم [عطف على قوله: "بنحو حجر"، يعني لا يستنجى بعظم؛ لأنه زاد الجن. (مسكين)] أما عدم الاستنجاء بالعظم والروث؛ فلأن النبي عليه لما أتاه جماعة من الجن ليلتهم قالوا: يا رسول الله ! اِنْهَ أمتك عن الاستنجاء بالعظم والروث والحممة؛ فإن الله تعالى جعل لنا فيها رزقاً، فقال علي: "لا تستنجوا بالروث، ولا بالعظام، فإنها زاد إخوانكم" يعني إن العظام لهم، والروث علف لدوابهم. ويكره استقبال القبلة في البول والغائط وكذا استدبارها ولو في البنيان؛ لقوله علي: "إذا أتيتم الغائط فعظموا قبلة ،الله، ولا تستقبلوها ولا تستدبروها"، ويكره البول والغائط في الماء والظل، أي ظل قوم يتسريحون فيه والطريق، وتحت شجر مثمر والتكلم عليهما، والبول قائما إلا بعذر، فإن كان بعذر فلا بأس به؛ لأنه عليه بال قائما لوجع في صلبه يعني استشفى به من وجع الصلب على عادة العرب، ويستنجي بيساره سواء كان بالماء أو الحجر، فإن كان المستنجي رجلاً يستنجي بأوسط أصابعه لا . الأصابع، وإن كانت امرأة تستنجي برؤوس الأصابع عند البعض، وهي كالرجل عند البعض، ثم اليد تطهر بطهارة المحل تبعا، ويشترط إزالة الرائحة عنها وعن المخرج، إلا إذا عجز ويستحب غسل يده ،قبله لئلا تتشرب به النجاسة وبعده مبالغة، ويستحب مسحها على الأرض كما هو مروي عن النبي ، ويستحب تقديم الاستعاذة والتسمية، وتقديم الرجل اليسرى في الدخول، واليمنى في الخروج، وأن يقول بعد خروجه "الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني". (فتح وغيره) وروث : لأن النجس لا يزيل النجس. [رمز الحقائق: ٤١/١] إلا بعذر : أي لا يستنجي باليمين إلا بعذر في اليسار كالشل وغيره. ولا بخزف وورق الشجر والشعر واللحم، ولو استنجى بهذه الأشياء جاز؛ لأن الكراهة لمعنى في غيرها كما إذا توضأ بماء مغصوب.
بجميع
Istinja is wiping the place of impurity or washing it. (Miskin)] It is an absolute confirmed sunnah, and what is said of it being obligatory for something like menstruation or exceeding the exit is lenient. Istinja: seeking relief and from its trace with water or earth, and al-najw: what comes out of the belly of impurity, so it is not said of wind because it is not impure even if it exits the belly, and cleaning what exits from other than the two passages is not called istinja. (Fath)
...

What is permissible for istinja
...
A pure stone and what is made into a number. And washing it with water is preferable, and it becomes obligatory if the impurity exceeds the exit.
And the preventing measure is considered beyond the place of istinja, not with bone, dung, food, and the right hand except with an excuse.
Because it is extravagance due to the prohibition of it.
And what is made into a number of purification is the necessity of performing this sunnah, not the number itself, as al-Shafi'i said: It is necessary to have three stones or a stone with three edges because of his (peace be upon him) saying: "When one of you relieves himself, let him perform istinja with three stones or three sticks or three pieces of wood." And for us is his (peace be upon him) saying: "Whoever uses stones (istijmar) let him use an odd number; whoever has done good, and whoever does not, there is no harm." And the specification of mentioning three in the other hadith is interpreted that the command is for recommendation, for combination and reconciliation. And the number is obligatory according to al-Shafi'i such that if he omits it his prayer is not valid. (Fath and others) And washing it, i.e., the place of istinja with water, if he can do so without exposing his private parts, is preferable and better, and otherwise exposure is absolutely prohibited and he becomes sinful by exposure, and it is said washing is sunnah in our time. (Miskin, T)] Because the saying of Allah the Exalted: "In it are men who love to purify themselves" (9:108) was revealed about a people who used stones then water, and it is proper conduct, and it is said sunnah in our time, so he washes with water until he becomes confident in his heart that he has become purified. And it is obligatory, etc., meaning washing with water becomes obligatory if the impurity exceeds its exit, because wiping with stone does not remove impurity, but it is sufficed with it in the place of istinja contrary to analogy, so it is not analogized to other than it. And similarly, if it does not exceed and he is in janabah, istinja with water is obligatory due to the obligation of washing the sitting place for janabah, and similarly for the menstruating woman and postpartum woman. (Fath, Mustakhlas) The place of istinja is restricted, because if the impurity is less such that if this is added to the place of istinja it becomes more than the size of a dirham, istinja suffices according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), and according to Muhammad he is obliged to wash it. (Miskin) Not with bone [dependent on his saying: 'with something like a stone', meaning one should not perform istinja with bone because it is the provision of the jinn. (Miskin)] As for the prohibition of istinja with bone and dung, because when a group of jinn came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) on their night, they said: O Messenger of Allah, forbid your nation from performing istinja with bone, dung, and charcoal, for Allah has provided us with them. So he (peace be upon him) said: "Do not perform istinja with dung nor with bones, for they are the provision of your brothers," meaning the bones are for them and dung is fodder for their animals. And it is disliked to face the qibla during urination and defecation, and also to turn one's back to it, even in a building, because of his (peace be upon him) saying: "When you go to relieve yourselves, glorify the qibla of Allah, and do not face it nor turn your backs to it." And it is disliked to urinate and defecate in water and shade, i.e., the shade of people taking recreation, and on the road, and under fruit-bearing trees, and to speak during them, and to urinate standing except with an excuse; if there is an excuse then there is no harm because he (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to pain in his lower back, meaning he sought cure from back pain according to Arab custom. And one performs istinja with the left hand whether with water or stone; if the person is a man, he performs istinja with his middle finger, not the fingers; if a woman, she performs istinja with the tips of the fingers according to some, and she is like a man according to others. Then the hand becomes pure as a result of the purity of the place, and removal of smell from it and from the exit is necessary unless unable, and it is recommended to wash his hand before it lest it absorb impurity, and after it for thoroughness, and it is recommended to wipe it on the ground as is narrated from the Prophet (peace be upon him), and it is recommended to offer seeking refuge (istia'dha) and saying basmalah, and to enter with the left foot and exit with the right, and to say after exiting: "Praise be to Allah who removed from me harm and granted me well-being." (Fath and others) And dung: because impurity does not remove impurity. [Ramz al-Haqaiq: 41/1] Except with an excuse: i.e., one should not perform istinja with the right hand except with an excuse in the left like paralysis etc. And not with pottery, tree leaves, hair, and meat, and if one performs istinja with these things it is permissible because the dislike is for a reason in other than them, as when one performs wudu with usurped water.
...
Source pages p. 54

Commentary
This passage provides a comprehensive treatment of the rulings (ahkam) of istinja'—the cleansing of the private parts after relieving oneself. The author begins by defining istinja' as wiping or washing the place of impurity, then clarifies that it is a confirmed sunnah (سنة مؤكدة) for all cases, though some overly strict views consider it obligatory for menstrual blood or when impurity spreads beyond the exit. The term 'istinja' literally means seeking relief, and its application is limited to removals from the two passages; wind and other exits are not included. The passage then details what may be used for istinja': a pure stone (حجر منق) or any substance that is clean and solid. Washing with water is preferable (أحب) but becomes obligatory (يجب) if the impurity exceeds the exit area, because wiping with a stone does not fully remove impurity in that case. The text then engages in an inter-madhhab dispute with Imam al-Shafi'i regarding the number of stones: Shafi'i holds that three stones (or a stone with three edges) are obligatory (فرض) based on a hadith specifying three; the Hanafi position is that the number is recommended (سنة) rather than obligatory, citing another hadith that only recommends using an odd number and indicates no harm in doing less. The Hanafis reconcile the two hadiths by interpreting the specific mention of three as recommendation for completeness, not obligation (الاستحباب). The passage then forbids the use of certain materials for istinja': bone and dung (because these are provisions for the jinn, as per an incident with the Prophet ﷺ), food, and the right hand (except with an excuse like a disabled left hand). Additionally, pottery, leaves, hair, and meat are disliked (مكروه) but not strictly prohibited; if used, istinja' is still valid. The text then moves to etiquette (adab): it is disliked (يكره) to face or turn one's back to the qibla during relief, even in a building; to relieve oneself in water, public shade, on a road, under fruit-bearing trees, or while speaking; and to urinate standing without an excuse. Standing is permitted if needed (e.g., the Prophet ﷺ did so due to back pain). The left hand is always used for istinja'; a man uses the middle finger, while a woman uses fingertips according to some. After istinja', the hand becomes pure by the purification of the place (تبعاً), though it is recommended to wash the hand beforehand and afterwards, and to wipe it on the ground. Recommended acts include saying isti'adha and basmalah before entering, entering with the left foot and exiting with the right, and saying a specific dhikr after exiting.

Key Terms
الاستنجاء (al-istinja'): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself, either by wiping (with stones or similar) or washing with water.
الاستجمار (al-istijmar): Specifically using stones (or similar solid material) for istinja'.
الروث (al-rawth): Dung (animal droppings). Prohibited for istinja' because it is food for the animals of the jinn.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on using three stones for istinja'?
A) It is fard (obligatory)
B) It is sunnah (recommended)
C) It is makruh (disliked)
D) It is haram (prohibited)

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, istinja' with stones is sunnah muakkadah; the number used is recommended, not obligatory, and the prayer remains valid even with one stone.

The Hanafi View on the Number of Stones for Istinja': Sunnah or Fard?
Ruling on what may be used for istinja' and debate on the number of stones

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why the Hanafi school holds that using three stones for istinja' is sunnah and evaluate the Shafi'i counter-argument.

Core Idea
In Hanafi fiqh, using three stones for istinja' is sunnah — the number is recommended, not obligatory.

This passage addresses a well-known difference between the Hanafi and Shafi'i schools: the obligation versus recommendation of using three stones for istinja'. The Hanafi position relies on a hadith that gives leeway, while the Shafi'i school holds to a command for three. Understanding how the Hanafi school reconciles conflicting proofs is key to mastering this issue.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi position
Identify that the Hanafi school rules using three stones (or odd number) as sunnah (recommended), not fard (obligatory).
The sunnah here is the practice itself, not the specific number.
2
Identify the opposing school and its view
Imam al-Shafi'i holds that three stones are fard; omitting them invalidates the prayer.
The Shafi'i proof is a hadith that commands using three stones.
3
Follow the opponent's proof
Examine the hadith cited by al-Shafi'i: 'When one of you goes to relieve himself, let him cleanse with three stones...'
The command (ليستنج) is taken by Shafi'i as indicating obligation.
4
Analyse the Hanafi response
The Hanafi school cites another hadith: 'Whoever uses stones, let him make it odd; whoever does well, good; whoever does not, no harm.' The phrase 'no harm' shows that omitting the odd number is not sinful, so the command in the Shafi'i hadith is interpreted as recommendation (istihbab) to reconcile the texts.
This method of reconciliation is called al-jam' wa al-tawfiq.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
The practical difference: if a person uses one stone and cleans properly, Hanafi says prayer is valid; Shafi'i says it is invalid.
This demonstrates the real-world impact of the ikhtilaf.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وما سن فيه عدد المنقى هو اللزوم في إقامة هذه السنة لا نفس العدد، كما قال الشافعي: إنه لا بد فيه من ثلاثة أحجار أو حجر له ثلاثة أحرف؛ لقوله عليه: "إذا أتى أحدكم حاجته فليستنج بثلاثة أحجار أو ثلاثة أعواد أو ثلاث خشبات، ولنا قوله عليه من استجمر فليوتر من فعل فقد أحسن، ومن لا فلا حرج"، والتنصيص على ذكر الثلاث في الحديث الآخر محمول على أن الأمر فيه للاستحباب جمعاً وتوفيقاً، والعدد عند الشافعي فرض حتى لو تركه لا تجوز صلاته فتح وغيره
And what is sunnah regarding the number that cleanses is the obligation to observe this sunnah, not the number itself, as al-Shafi'i said: it is necessary to use three stones or a stone with three edges, due to his saying (peace be upon him): 'When one of you goes to relieve himself, let him cleanse with three stones or three sticks or three pieces of wood.' And for us is his saying (peace be upon him): 'Whoever uses stones for cleansing, let him make it odd. Whoever does well, then good, and whoever does not, there is no harm.' And the specification of mentioning three in the other hadith is interpreted as indicating recommendation, to reconcile and harmonize. And the number according to al-Shafi'i is obligatory such that if he omits it, his prayer is not valid.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is an intra-madhhab and inter-madhhabi discussion about the number of stones required for istinja'. The Hanafi position is that using three stones (or a stone with three edges) is a sunnah, not a fard. The commentator explains that what is sunnah is the commitment to performing this sunnah, not the specific number itself. The Shafi'i position, presented here, holds that three stones are obligatory (fard), based on a hadith that commands three. The Hanafi response invokes another hadith that makes odd numbers recommended but not obligatory, and interprets the three-stone hadith as indicating recommendation to reconcile both texts. The practical consequence is that if one omits the odd number, the Shafi'i would invalidate the prayer, while the Hanafi does not.

Key Terms
سن (sunnah): Recommended practice; its omission is not sinful and does not affect validity.
عدد منقى (adad munaqqā): The number (of stones) that results in cleansing; the minimum is three.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is obligatory
B) It is recommended
C) It is permissible
D) It is forbidden

Key Takeaway
In Hanafi fiqh, the number of stones for istinja' is sunnah, not fard; the obligation is to observe the sunnah practice, not the specific number.

When Istinja' with Water Becomes Obligatory: Hanafi Ruling and Proof
Ruling on washing with water for istinja' and conditions for obligation

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on washing with water for istinja' and identify the conditions that make it obligatory.

Core Idea
Washing with water is preferred for istinja', but becomes obligatory when impurity spreads or janabah is present.

Purification after relieving oneself is essential for prayer. The Hanafi school provides nuanced guidance on whether to use stones or water. This passage from Kanz al-Daqa'iq clarifies that while water is generally recommended, certain circumstances—like impurity spreading beyond the exit or the presence of major impurity—make it obligatory. Understanding this distinction protects the validity of your purification and prayer.

Guided Path
1
Identify the default ruling
The text states that washing with water is 'beloved and better' (أحب وأفضل) – this is the default ruling when impurity is contained. It is a recommended act (sunnah/mustahabb), not obligatory.
This default applies only if one can wash without exposing the private parts unnecessarily.
2
Recognize the condition for obligation
Washing becomes wajib if the impurity has spread beyond the exit (جاوز النجس المخرج). The reason: wiping with stones only suffices for the exit area as an exception to analogy; it does not remove impurity elsewhere.
This is the key distinction: contained impurity → stones suffice; spread impurity → water wajib.
3
Understand the secondary obligating factor
Even if impurity is contained, washing is wajib for a person in janabah (major impurity), menstruation, or postpartum bleeding. This is because the anus must be washed as part of ghusl.
This shows how different obligations can combine.
4
Analyze the Quranic proof
The verse 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' (9:108) was revealed about people who used stones then water. This indicates the preference for water as a more complete purification.
The proof is from the Quran (qat'i thubut) but the implication is zanni, hence it indicates preference, not obligation.
5
Note the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf
Imam Muhammad holds that if the impurity on the exit area plus surrounding tissue totals more than a dirham, washing is required. Abu Yusuf and Abu Hanifa do not require this. The mufta bihi is the general ruling.
This shows that even within the Hanafi school, there are nuanced differences.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وغسله أي موضع الاستنجاء بالماء، إن أمكنه بلا كشف عورة. أحب وأفضل، وإلا حرم الكشف مطلقاً ويكون فاسقاً بالكشف وقيل: الغسل سنة في زماننا.(مسكين، ط)]؛ لأن قوله تعالى: ﴿وفِيهِ رِجَالٌ يُحِبُّونَ أَنْ يَتَطَهَّرُوا﴾ (التوبة: ۱۰۸) نزل في قوم كانوا يتبعون الأحجار ثم الماء، وهو أدب، وقيل: سنة في زماننا، فيغسل بالماء إلى أن تقع في قلبه أنه قد طهر. ويجب إلخ أي يجب الغسل بالماء إذا تجاوز النجاسة مخرجها؛ لأن المسح بالحجر غير مزيل للنجاسة، إلا أنه اكتفي به في موضع الاستنجاء على خلاف القياس، فلا يقاس عليه غيره، وكذا لو لم يجاوز وكان جنباً يجب الاستنجاء بالماء؛ لوجوب غسل المقعد لأجل الجنابة، وكذا الحائض والنفساء. (فتح، مستخلص موضع الاستنجاء قيد به؛ لأن النجاسة لو كانت أقل بحيث لو ضم هذا إلى موضع الاستنجاء يصير أكثر من قدر الدرهم يكفيه الاستنجاء عندهما، وعند محمد يفرض غسله. (مسكين)
And washing the place of istinja' with water, if he can do so without exposing his private parts, is beloved and better. Otherwise, exposing the private parts is absolutely forbidden and he becomes a sinner by exposing. And it is said: washing is sunnah in our time. Because the verse of Allah: 'In it are men who love to purify themselves' was revealed about people who used stones and then water, and it is a practice of etiquette. And it is said: it is sunnah in our time, so he washes with water until he feels in his heart that he has become pure. And it is obligatory: meaning that washing with water is obligatory if the impurity has spread beyond its exit, because wiping with a stone does not remove impurity, except that it is deemed sufficient in the place of istinja' contrary to analogy, so it is not analogized to other places. Similarly, if it has not spread but he is in a state of janabah, istinja' with water is obligatory due to the obligation of washing the anus because of janabah. Similarly for the menstruating and postpartum woman.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage explains the rulings regarding washing the area of istinja' with water. The preferred and better method is to wash with water, provided one can do so without exposing the private parts unnecessarily. If exposure is unavoidable, it becomes forbidden. However, if the impurity (najasah) exceeds the exit (i.e., spreads beyond the area of istinja'), then washing with water becomes obligatory because wiping with a stone does not remove impurity thoroughly. The exception for stones is specific to the place of istinja' and is not to be extended to other areas. Additionally, if a person is in a state of major impurity (janabah), menstruation, or postpartum bleeding, istinja' with water is also obligatory as part of the general purification. The verse from Surah al-Tawbah is cited as a basis for the preference of water, as it was revealed about people who used stones and then water, showing that water is a more complete purification.

Key Terms
استنجاء (istinjā’): Cleansing the private parts after relieving oneself, typically with stones or water.
نجاسة (najāsah): Impurity that must be removed for prayer validity.
موضع الاستنجاء (mawdi' al-istinjā'): The area of the body that is cleaned during istinja'.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Only when one is in a state of janabah.
B) When the impurity has spread beyond the exit.
C) Whenever one uses the toilet.
D) It is never obligatory, always sunnah.

Key Takeaway
Washing with water for istinja' is sunnah by default, but it becomes wajib when impurity spreads beyond the exit or when the person is in janabah (or similar states).

Prohibition of Using Bone, Dung, and Right Hand for Istinja'
Prohibition of certain materials and the right hand with exceptions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the materials prohibited for istinja', cite the hadith evidence, and explain when using the right hand is permissible.

Core Idea
Bone and dung are forbidden because they are food for the jinn; the right hand is reserved for clean acts.

This passage from Kanz al-Daqaiq explains the fiqh of istinja' materials. The Prophet (peace be upon him) explicitly prohibited the use of bone and dung based on a request from the jinn. Additionally, the right hand is not to be used except in cases of necessity. Understanding these rulings preserves the sanctity of purification and distinguishes between pure and impure substances.

Guided Path
1
Identify the prohibited items
State which materials are explicitly forbidden: bone, dung, and the right hand.
2
Examine the primary evidence
Read the hadith where the Prophet says: 'Do not use dung nor bones, for they are the provision of your brothers.'
The hadith is reported in collections like Sunan Abi Dawud.
3
Understand the rationale
The jinn rely on these as food; thus they are not to be used for removing impurity.
This highlights the respect for other creations.
4
Note the exception for the right hand
The right hand is forbidden unless there is an excuse, such as paralysis of the left hand.
The Prophet himself used the right hand only under necessity.
5
Distinguish between prohibition and dislike
Other materials like pottery or leaves are disliked (makruh tanzihi) but not prohibited; using them is valid.
The dislike is due to a meaning in other than these materials.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
لا بعظم [عطف على قوله: "بنحو حجر"، يعني لا يستنجى بعظم؛ لأنه زاد الجن. (مسكين)] أما عدم الاستنجاء بالعظم والروث؛ فلأن النبي عليه لما أتاه جماعة من الجن ليلتهم قالوا: يا رسول الله ! اِنْهَ أمتك عن الاستنجاء بالعظم والروث والحممة؛ فإن الله تعالى جعل لنا فيها رزقاً، فقال علي: "لا تستنجوا بالروث، ولا بالعظام، فإنها زاد إخوانكم" يعني إن العظام لهم، والروث علف لدوابهم. ويكره استقبال القبلة في البول والغائط وكذا استدبارها ولو في البنيان؛ لقوله علي: "إذا أتيتم الغائط فعظموا قبلة الله، ولا تستقبلوها ولا تستدبروها"، ويكره البول والغائط في الماء والظل، أي ظل قوم يتسريحون فيه والطريق، وتحت شجر مثمر والتكلم عليهما، والبول قائما إلا بعذر، فإن كان بعذر فلا بأس به؛ لأنه عليه بال قائما لوجع في صلبه يعني استشفى به من وجع الصلب على عادة العرب، ويستنجي بيساره سواء كان بالماء أو الحجر، فإن كان المستنجي رجلاً يستنجي بأوسط أصابعه لا . الأصابع، وإن كانت امرأة تستنجي برؤوس الأصابع عند البعض، وهي كالرجل عند البعض، ثم اليد تطهر بطهارة المحل تبعا، ويشترط إزالة الرائحة عنها وعن المخرج، إلا إذا عجز ويستحب غسل يده قبله لئلا تتشرب به النجاسة وبعده مبالغة، ويستحب مسحها على الأرض كما هو مروي عن النبي، ويستحب تقديم الاستعاذة والتسمية، وتقديم الرجل اليسرى في الدخول، واليمنى في الخروج، وأن يقول بعد خروجه "الحمد لله الذي أذهب عني الأذى وعافاني". (فتح وغيره) وروث : لأن النجس لا يزيل النجس. [رمز الحقائق: ٤١/١] إلا بعذر : أي لا يستنجي باليمين إلا بعذر في اليسار كالشل وغيره. ولا بخزف وورق الشجر والشعر واللحم، ولو استنجى بهذه الأشياء جاز؛ لأن الكراهة لمعنى في غيرها كما إذا توضأ بماء مغصوب.
Not with bone, dung, food, and right hand except with an excuse. As for the prohibition of using bone and dung, it is because when a group of jinn came to the Prophet (peace be upon him) on their night, they said: 'O Messenger of Allah, forbid your ummah from using bone, dung, and charcoal for istinja', for Allah has provided us with sustenance in them.' So he said: 'Do not use dung nor bones, for they are the provision of your brothers' – meaning the bones are for them and the dung is fodder for their animals. And it is disliked to face the qibla while urinating or defecating, and likewise to turn one's back to it, even in buildings, due to his saying: 'When you go to relieve yourselves, honor the qibla of Allah, do not face it nor turn your backs to it.' And it is disliked to urinate or defecate in water, in the shade (meaning the shade where people gather), on the road, under a fruit-bearing tree, and to talk while doing so, and to urinate standing except with an excuse. If there is an excuse, it is permissible because the Prophet (peace be upon him) urinated standing due to pain in his back, meaning he sought treatment through it according to Arab custom. And he should cleanse with his left hand, whether with water or stone. If the person cleansing is a man, he should cleanse with the middle of his fingers, not the tips. If a woman, she cleanses with the tips of the fingers according to some, and she is like a man according to others. Then the hand becomes pure by the purification of the place as a consequence, but it is necessary to remove the smell from the hand and the exit, unless unable. It is recommended to wash the hand before cleansing to prevent the impurity from soaking in, and after it as a thorough measure, and to wipe it on the ground as narrated from the Prophet. It is recommended to say the seek refuge and basmalah, to enter with the left foot and exit with the right, and to say after exiting: 'Praise be to Allah who has removed from me harm and granted me well-being.' (Fath and others) And dung: because impurity does not remove impurity. [Ramz al-Haqaiq 1:41] Except with an excuse: meaning he should not use the right hand except due to an excuse in the left, such as paralysis etc. And not with pottery, paper of trees, hair, and meat. If one cleanses with these things, it is permissible because the dislike is due to a meaning in other than these, just as if one performs wudu with usurped water.
Source pages p. 55

Commentary
This passage is a collection of rulings regarding the etiquettes and prohibitions related to istinja'. It begins by forbidding the use of bone and dung based on a hadith where jinn requested the Prophet to forbid their use because these are provisions for them. Then it lists disliked acts: facing or turning one's back to the qibla, urinating in water or in public shade, on roads, under fruit trees, talking while relieving, and urinating standing unless excused. The example of the Prophet urinating standing due to back pain is given. It then details the method of istinja': using the left hand (men use the middle of fingers, women the tips according to some), the necessity of removing odor, and recommended acts like washing the hand before and after, wiping on ground, and saying certain supplications. The use of the right hand is forbidden except due to an excuse. Finally, it notes that using other materials like pottery or leaves is permissible though disliked, likening it to performing wudu with usurped water (valid but sinful).

Key Terms
روث (rawth): Dung (animal excrement); not pure and therefore not suitable for istinja'.
يمين (yamīn): Right hand; using it for istinja' is prohibited without excuse.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, which of the following is prohibited for istinja' without an excuse?
A) Using a smooth stone.
B) Using the right hand.
C) Using water.
D) Using a tissue.

Key Takeaway
Bone and dung are prohibited for istinja' due to explicit hadith; the right hand is reserved for clean acts and may only be used in necessity.

Disliked Times for Prayer: Rulings and Exceptions
Ruling with proof on disliked prayer times and exceptions.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three disliked times, identify the exceptions (Asr of the same day), and explain the Hanafi ruling on voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr with its proof.

Core Idea
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is prohibited except for the same-day Asr; no voluntary prayer after Fajr or Asr.

The time of prayer directly affects its validity. In this passage, al-Marghinani explains the three times when prayer is either prohibited or disliked, along with key exceptions. We will also analyze the Hanafi position on praying after Fajr and Asr, and how it differs from the Shafi'i school.

Guided Path
1
Identify the Three Disliked Times
List the three times explicitly mentioned: sunrise (until it rises), zenith (until it passes), and sunset (until it sets). Note that these times apply to all prayers unless an exception is specified.
These are based on the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir.
2
Recognize the Exceptions
The only exception is the Asr prayer of the same day, which is valid at sunset because it is performed in its actual time. Conversely, Fajr of the same day is invalidated by sunrise.
The difference: Asr's time ends deficiently, while Fajr's time is complete.
3
Analyze the Ruling on Voluntary Prayers after Fajr and Asr
According to the hadith 'No prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset,' all voluntary prayers (even with a cause) are prohibited. This is the Hanafi position.
The prohibition is general and covers Tahiyyat al-Masjid and other sunan.
4
Contrast with the Shafi'i View
Al-Shafi'i permits voluntary prayers with a cause (e.g., greeting the mosque, Tawaf) after Fajr and Asr, citing the hadith of Banu Abd Manaf. The Hanafi response is that the exception is specific to Makkah and does not override the general prohibition.
The practical difference: Hanafi students do not pray Tahiyyat al-Masjid after Fajr; Shafi'i students do.
5
Determine the Ruling for Janazah, Sajdah, and Qada
Janazah and Sajdah al-Tilawah are valid but disliked (makruh tahrimi) in the three times if the obligation arises at that moment. Qada of missed obligatory prayers is invalid (batil) because it was due complete.
This distinction is based on whether the act became obligatory in a complete or incomplete time.

كتاب الصلاة الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة والوتر إلى آخر الليل لمن يثق بالانتباه، وتعجيل ظهر الشتاء والمغرب، وما فيها عين أي ندب تأخيره يوم غين، ويؤخر غيره فيه. الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة في كل وقت ومنع عن الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة عند الطلوع والاستواء والغروب إلا عصر يومه وعن التنفل بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر، لا عن قضاء فائتة، وسجدة تلاوة وصلاة جنازة، وبعد طلوع الفجر لا يمنع في هذين الوقتين والغروب: أي لا يجوز الصلاة وسجدة التلاوة وصلاة الجنازة في هذه الأوقات الثلاثة؛ لحديث عقبة بن عامر أنه قال: ثلاثة أوقات نهانا رسول الله ﷺ أن نصلي فيها، وأن نقبر فيها موتانا عند طلوع الشمس حتى ترتفع، وعند زوالها حتى تزول، وحين تضيف للغروب حتى تغرب رواه مسلم والمراد من قوله: "أن نقبر" صلاة الجنازة؛ إذ الدفن غير مكروه، وقال الشافعي: لا يكره قضاء الفوائت في هذه الأوقات؛ لقوله ﷺ: "من نام عن صلاة أو نسيها فليصلها إذا ذكرها فإن ذلك وقتها"، وكذا النوافل عنده لا يكره في هذه الساعات بمكة؛ لقوله ﷺ: "يا بني عبد مناف! لا تمنعوا أحداً طاف بهذا البيت، وصلّى في أي ساعة شاء من ليل أو نهار"، والجواب عنه: أن الشرع نهي عن الصلاة في هذه الأوقات، واستثنى بني عبد مناف وعن أبي يوسف: إباحة النفل يوم الجمعة وقت الاستواء، والحجة عليه ما روينا، وسجدة التلاوة في معنى الصلاة؛ ولذلك نهي عنها، والمراد بالنهي عن صلاة الجنازة أو سجدة التلاوة الكراهة، حتى لو صلاها أو سجدها أجزأته؛ لأنها وجبت ناقصة بالشروع في الوقت المكروه فأديت كذلك، وأما قضاء الفوائت فلا يجوز أصلاً؛ لأنها شرعت كاملة، فلا يؤدى بالنقصان. (مستخلص) واعلم أن التطوع في هذه الأوقات يجوز ويكره، ولا يجوز قضاء الفرض والواجب الفائت فيها كسجدة تلاوة وجبت بتلاوة في وقت غير مكروه وكوتر، فالمنع يتناول الكراهة وعدم الجواز وفي البحر: أن يصلي على الجنازة إذا حضرت في الأوقات الثلاثة، ولا يؤخرها؛ لقوله ﷺ: "ثلاث لا يؤخرن جنازة أتت" الحديث؛ ولأنها أديت كما وجبت؛ إذ الوجوب بالحضور، وهو أفضل، والتأخير مكروه لما ذكرنا والظاهر أن ما ذكروا من الكراهة محمول على ما إذا حضرت في وقت كامل وصلى عليها في وقت مكروه، وكذا المراد بسجدة التلاوة إذا تلاها قبل هذه الأوقات؛ لأنها وجبت كاملة فلا تتأدى بالنقصان، وأما إذا تلا فيها جاز أداؤها من غير كراهة، لكن الأفضل التأخير إلى الوقت المستحب؛ لأنها لا تفوت بالتأخير. (فتح) إلا عصر يومه: [استثناء من منع، فإن عصر يومه تصح قبيل الغروب؛ ولأنه أداها كما وجبت حتى لا يجوز عصر أمسه؛ لأن الكامل لا يتأدى بالناقص. (ط، ف، ع)] فإنه يجوز، وأما فجر يومه فيبطل بالطلوع، والفرق بينهما أن السبب في العصر آخر الوقت، وهو وقت التغير ناقص، فإذا أداها فيه أداها كما وجبت، ووقت الفجر كله كامل فوجبت كاملة، فتبطل بطرء الطلوع (هدايه) وعن التنفل: أي مطلقاً سواء كان له سبب أو لا، وقال الشافعي: إن التنقل بعدهما إذا كان له سبب جائز بلا كراهة وأراد به ركعتي الطواف وتحية المسجد والسنن الموقتة والمنذورة، أما ابتداء النفل فإنه أيضاً عنده مكروه. (فتح) بعد صلاة الفجر والعصر أي وبعد صلاته لقوله ﷺ: "لا صلاة بعد صلاة الفجر حتى تطلع الشمس، ولا صلاة بعد صلاة العصر حتى تغرب الشمس"، رواه البخاري ومسلم، وهو حجة على الشافعي في تجويزه النفل الذي له سبب كتحية المسجد وركعتي الطواف. (ع)
Book of Prayer. The times in which prayer is disliked. And Witr until the end of the night for one who trusts himself to wake up. And hastening the Zuhr of winter and Maghrib. And what contains 'ayn (i.e., Asr and Isha): meaning its postponement on a cloudy day is recommended. And other than that is postponed in it. The times in which prayer is disliked: at every time, and prohibition of prayer, Sajdah al-Tilawah, and Janazah prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, except the Asr of that day. And regarding voluntary prayer after Fajr and Asr, not regarding making up a missed prayer, Sajdah al-Tilawah, and Janazah prayer. And after the break of dawn, it is not prevented in these two times. And sunset: i.e., prayer, Sajdah al-Tilawah, and Janazah prayer are not permissible in these three times due to the hadith of Uqbah ibn Amir that he said: Three times the Messenger of Allah ﷺ forbade us to pray in them and to bury our dead in them: at sunrise until it rises, at zenith until it passes, and when it inclines to set until it sets, reported by Muslim. And the meaning of his saying 'to bury' is the Janazah prayer; as burial is not disliked. Al-Shafi'i said: Making up missed prayers is not disliked in these times due to his saying ﷺ: 'Whoever sleeps through a prayer or forgets it, let him pray it when he remembers, for that is its time.' And similarly, voluntary prayers according to him are not disliked in these hours in Makkah due to his saying ﷺ: 'O Banu Abd Manaf! Do not prevent anyone from circumambulating this House and praying at any hour of night or day.' The answer to that: The Law forbade prayer in these times, and made an exception for Banu Abd Manaf. And from Abu Yusuf: Permissibility of voluntary prayer on Friday at the time of zenith. The proof against him is what we have reported. And Sajdah al-Tilawah is in the meaning of prayer; therefore it is forbidden. And the intended meaning of the prohibition of Janazah prayer or Sajdah al-Tilawah is dislike (karahah), so that if one prays or prostrates, it suffices him; because they were obligated incomplete by starting in the disliked time, so they are performed accordingly. As for making up missed obligatory prayers, it is not permissible at all; because they are legislated complete, so they cannot be performed deficiently. (Mukhtasar) And know that supererogatory prayer in these times is permissible but disliked. And making up a missed obligatory or obligatory (wajib) prayer is not permissible in them, like Sajdah al-Tilawah that became obligatory by recitation in a non-disliked time, and Witr. So the prohibition includes dislike and non-permissibility. In al-Bahr: That one should pray over the Janazah if it is present in the three times, and not delay it due to his saying ﷺ: 'Three things are not delayed: a Janazah that comes...' the hadith; and because it is performed as it became obligatory, since the obligation is by presence, and it is better, and delaying is disliked for what we mentioned. And it appears that what they mentioned of dislike is understood when it is present in a complete time and one prays in a disliked time. Similarly intended for Sajdah al-Tilawah if one recited before these times; because it became obligatory complete, so it is not performed deficiently. But if one recites in them, it is permissible to perform it without dislike, but it is better to delay to a recommended time because it is not lost by delay. (Fath) Except the Asr of that day: [Exception from the prohibition, for the Asr of that day is valid shortly before sunset; because one performs it as it became obligatory, unlike the Asr of the previous day; because the complete is not performed deficiently. (T, F, A)] So it is permissible. As for the Fajr of that day, it is invalidated by sunrise. The difference between them is that the cause in Asr is the end of the time, which is a deficient time of change, so if one performs it therein, one performs it as it became obligatory. And the time of Fajr is entirely complete, so it became obligatory complete, so it is invalidated by the occurrence of sunrise. (Hidayah) And regarding voluntary prayer: meaning absolutely, whether it has a cause or not. Al-Shafi'i said: Voluntary prayer after them if it has a cause is permissible without dislike, and he intended by that the two rak'ahs of Tawaf, the greeting of the mosque, the timed Sunan, and vows. As for initiating voluntary prayer, it is also disliked according to him. (Fath) After Fajr and Asr prayers: meaning after performing them, due to his saying ﷺ: 'There is no prayer after Fajr prayer until the sun rises, and no prayer after Asr prayer until the sun sets,' reported by Bukhari and Muslim, and it is a proof against al-Shafi'i in his permitting voluntary prayer that has a cause, like the greeting of the mosque and the two rak'ahs of Tawaf. (A)
Source pages p. 59

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof regarding the disliked times for prayer. It begins by stating the general prohibition of prayer, Sajdah al-Tilawah (prostration of recitation), and Janazah (funeral) prayer at three specific times: sunrise (from actual sunrise until the sun rises about a spear's length), zenith (when the sun is at its meridian until it passes, i.e., just before and at midday), and sunset (when the sun turns yellow until it sets). An exception is made for the Asr prayer of the same day, which is permissible shortly before sunset because it is performed in its proper time, but if one delays it until that point, it is valid. However, the Fajr prayer of the same day is invalidated if sunrise occurs during it; the difference is that the time of Asr at its end is considered a deficient time of necessity, while Fajr's time is fully complete, so the prayer is obligatory complete and cannot be performed deficiently. The passage then discusses voluntary prayers after Fajr and Asr: they are prohibited absolutely (both with and without a cause) according to the Hanafi school, based on the hadith 'No prayer after Fajr until sunrise and after Asr until sunset.' Imam al-Shafi'i distinguishes between voluntary prayers with a cause (like greeting the mosque, two rak'ahs of Tawaf) and those without; he permits the former but dislikes the latter in these times. The Hanafi position is that the general prohibition covers all voluntary prayers, and the hadith of Banu Abd Manaf is specific to Makkah and does not override the general rule. Regarding making up missed obligatory prayers (qada), the Hanafis hold that it is not permissible at all in these three times because the obligatory prayer was obligatory complete, and performing it in a deficient time would contradict its completeness. For Sajdah al-Tilawah and Janazah prayer, the ruling is that they are disliked but valid if performed in these times because they become obligatory in an incomplete state (the obligation arises from the act of recitation or presence of the deceased, which is not tied to a complete time). However, if the Sajdah became obligatory before the disliked time, it is not permissible to delay it into the disliked time; one should perform it earlier. The text also notes a difference from Abu Yusuf who allowed voluntary prayer on Friday at zenith, but the relied-upon position is the prohibition. The passage ends with a discussion of the wisdom behind hastening Zuhr in winter, Maghrib, and delaying Asr and Isha on cloudy days, but that is part of the broader context of preferred times. Overall, the Hanafi school strictly prohibits prayer (including qada and nafl) at sunrise, zenith, and sunset, with the only exception being the same-day Asr prayer.

Key Terms
الاستواء (al-istiwā'): The time when the sun is at its zenith (meridian), i.e., midday before it begins to decline.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the Janazah prayer at sunrise?
A) It is invalid and must be repeated after sunrise.
B) It is valid but disliked; one should not delay the Janazah.
C) It is absolutely prohibited and cannot be performed.
D) It is valid and recommended to delay it until after sunrise.

Key Takeaway
Prayer at sunrise, zenith, and sunset is prohibited for all types except the same-day Asr; Janazah and Sajdah are valid but disliked; qada is invalid.
